The Mu'tazila's Objections to Divine Attributes
Al-Nasafi lists the Mu'tazila's three objections to attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the main arguments the Mu'tazila used to deny the reality of God's attributes, based on the principles of kalām.

Core Idea
If attributes are not the essence, they must be other—implying multiple pre-eternal beings.

Al-Nasafi begins by summarizing the Mu'tazila's key suspicions against the reality of divine attributes. These objections center on the idea that if attributes are not identical to the essence, they must be separate entities, leading to multiple eternal beings. He presents these views with methodological fairness before refuting them.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila's arguments
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting the three distinct objections presented.
The passage lists three main suspicions; try to identify each one.
2
Understand the logic behind each objection
For each objection, ask yourself: what premise leads to the conclusion that attributes cannot be real?
The first objection relies on the dichotomy of 'being the essence or other'.
3
Recognize the theological stakes
Notice that these objections aim to protect tawhid (divine unity) from what they see as polytheism.
Al-Nasafi acknowledges the sincerity of their motives.
4
Prepare for the refutation
Realize that Al-Nasafi will later use a trilemma to counter these objections.
This lesson sets the stage for the next lesson's argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجيب أنها لا عين الذات، ولا غير الذات، ويأتى بشبه المعتزلة، ويعرضها بأمانته المنهجية من ذلك أن الصفة إذا لم تكن عين الذات كانت غير الذات لا محالة، والقول بالأشياء المتغايرة في الأزل ينافي التوحيد، وأنها لو كانت ثابتة لكانت أزلية، ولو كانت أزلية كانت قديمة، والقول بهذا يؤدي إلى القول بآلهة كثيرة، ومن ذلك أيضا - أن الصفات لو ثبتت لكانت باقية ضرورة، ولا وجه إلى القول ببقاء كل صفة ببقاء يقوم بها، لاستحالة قيام الصفة بالصفة. والنسفي يفند هذه الآراء بالعقل والسمع، وهو في رده يستعرض شبها كثيرة ظهرت لأبي على الجبائي، وللعلاف، ولأبي هاشم، وللكعبي، ويقول: نقول للمعتزلة. إنكم بين أمور ثلاثة : إما أن تسووا بين الشاهد والغائب في كل ذلك، وتقولوا: إن قدرة الصانع ثابتة بدلالة المفعول، وعلمه ثابت بدلالة أحكام المفعول، وفي هذا ترك مذهبكم، وإما أن تفرقوا بين الشاهد والغائب في كل ذلك فتقولوا: إن المفعول وإن دل على علمه ففي الغائب لا يدل على شيء. وهذا قمة الإنكار لوجود الصانع، وإما أن تسووا بين الشاهد والغائب في حق دلالته على القدرة والعلم، وتقولوا وإن كان ذلك دليلا عليهما في الشاهد فليس بدليل عليهما في الغائب. فتتناقضوا.
And he answers that they are neither the essence nor other than the essence. And he brings the suspicions of the Mu'tazila and presents them with his methodological trustworthiness, including that if the attribute is not the essence, then it is inevitably other than the essence, and affirming different things in pre-eternity contradicts tawhid; and that if they were established they would be eternal, and if they were eternal they would be qadim, and this leads to affirming many gods; and also that if attributes were established they would necessarily be enduring, and there is no way to say that each attribute endures by an endurance subsisting in it, because it is impossible for an attribute to subsist in an attribute. And al-Nasafi refutes these views with reason and revelation. In his refutation he reviews many suspicions that appeared from Abu Ali al-Jubbai, al-Allaf, Abu Hashim, and al-Ka'bi, and he says: We say to the Mu'tazila: You are among three matters: Either you equate the witnessed and the unseen in all that, and say that the power of the Maker is established by the evidence of the effect, and His knowledge is established by the evidence of the judgments of the effect, and in this is an abandonment of your school; or you differentiate between the witnessed and the unseen in all that, and say that the effect although it indicates His knowledge, in the unseen it indicates nothing, and this is the height of denial of the existence of the Maker; or you equate the witnessed and the unseen in the matter of its indication of power and knowledge, and say that although that is evidence for them in the witnessed, it is not evidence for them in the unseen, and thus you contradict yourselves.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila's denial of the attributes. Al-Nasafi first lists their main suspicions: if attributes are not the essence they must be other, implying multiple pre-eternal entities; if established they would be eternal and thus multiple gods; and attributes would need a separate endurance causing infinite regress. Then he counters by presenting a three-part logical division (taqsīm) concerning the analogy (tamthīl) between the witnessed (shāhid) and the unseen (ghā'ib). The three options are: (1) accept full analogy—then the effect in the unseen proves power and knowledge, which is what the Ahl al-Sunna affirm, but the Mu'tazila reject this; (2) reject all analogy—then the effect gives no knowledge of God, leading to atheism; (3) accept analogy for power but not for knowledge—this is arbitrary and inconsistent. Thus the Mu'tazila are forced into contradiction. This is a classic kalam argument using the logic of shāhid and ghā'ib.

Key Terms
شاهد
غائب
صفة
ذات
أزل
قديم
بقاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the third Mu'tazilite objection, why is it impossible for attributes to endure?
A) Because endurance is a separate attribute that would need to subsist in the attribute, which is impossible.
B) Because attributes are not real entities.
C) Because endurance would imply change in God.
D) Because the Qur'an denies endurance for God's attributes.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila argue that affirming real attributes leads to multiple eternal beings or an infinite regress, thus they deny attributes to preserve tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Mu'tazila argued that affirming attributes leads to polytheism. Have you ever, even subtly, imagined Allah's attributes as separate 'powers'? What does this tell you about the depth of tawhid required in your heart?
?
If you were to defend the Ash'ari position (attributes are neither essence nor other) to someone like the Mu'tazila, what part of your own understanding would you find most difficult to articulate? What does that reveal about your need to study more?
?
The Mu'tazila were driven by a pure desire to protect tawhid—yet the mainstream scholars rejected their conclusion. Is your zeal for protecting Allah's oneness matched by a willingness to accept the correct position even when it seems paradoxical? What are you willing to sacrifice for the truth?

The Trilemma: Forcing the Mu'tazila to Choose Consistently
Al-Nasafi presents a trilemma forcing the Mu'tazila to choose consistently on the shāhid-ghā'ib analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi uses a trilemma to show that the Mu'tazila cannot consistently deny attributes without falling into self-contradiction or disbelief.

Core Idea
Mu'tazila must either accept full analogy, reject all analogy, or be inconsistent—each has unacceptable consequences.

After presenting the Mu'tazila's objections, Al-Nasafi turns the tables by offering them a three-way logical division. The argument uses the principle of analogy (tamthīl) between the witnessed world and the unseen divine realm. The Mu'tazila must choose one of three options, but each option either contradicts their own principles or leads to atheism. This is a classic example of kalam's method of refutation through logical enumeration.

Guided Path
1
Understand the setting of the trilemma
Al-Nasafi introduces the trilemma after refuting specific Mu'tazilite objections. He addresses the Mu'tazila directly: 'You are among three matters.'
The trilemma concerns the analogy between shāhid (witnessed) and ghā'ib (unseen).
2
Analyze Option 1: Full analogy
If the Mu'tazila accept full analogy, then the effect in the unseen proves God's power and knowledge—this is the Sunni position, which they reject.
They would have to abandon their school.
3
Analyze Option 2: No analogy
If they reject all analogy, then the effect gives no knowledge of God in the unseen, leading to atheism—which they also reject.
This is 'the height of denial of the existence of the Maker.'
4
Analyze Option 3: Selective analogy
If they accept analogy for power but not for knowledge, they contradict themselves because the same evidence should be treated consistently.
This inconsistency refutes their position.
5
Realize the force of the argument
The trilemma shows that no matter which option the Mu'tazila choose, they cannot maintain their rejection of attributes without logical failure.
Al-Nasafi's method is a strong dialectical tool.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجيب أنها لا عين الذات، ولا غير الذات، ويأتى بشبه المعتزلة، ويعرضها بأمانته المنهجية من ذلك أن الصفة إذا لم تكن عين الذات كانت غير الذات لا محالة، والقول بالأشياء المتغايرة في الأزل ينافي التوحيد، وأنها لو كانت ثابتة لكانت أزلية، ولو كانت أزلية كانت قديمة، والقول بهذا يؤدي إلى القول بآلهة كثيرة، ومن ذلك أيضا - أن الصفات لو ثبتت لكانت باقية ضرورة، ولا وجه إلى القول ببقاء كل صفة ببقاء يقوم بها، لاستحالة قيام الصفة بالصفة. والنسفي يفند هذه الآراء بالعقل والسمع، وهو في رده يستعرض شبها كثيرة ظهرت لأبي على الجبائي، وللعلاف، ولأبي هاشم، وللكعبي، ويقول: نقول للمعتزلة. إنكم بين أمور ثلاثة : إما أن تسووا بين الشاهد والغائب في كل ذلك، وتقولوا: إن قدرة الصانع ثابتة بدلالة المفعول، وعلمه ثابت بدلالة أحكام المفعول، وفي هذا ترك مذهبكم، وإما أن تفرقوا بين الشاهد والغائب في كل ذلك فتقولوا: إن المفعول وإن دل على علمه ففي الغائب لا يدل على شيء. وهذا قمة الإنكار لوجود الصانع، وإما أن تسووا بين الشاهد والغائب في حق دلالته على القدرة والعلم، وتقولوا وإن كان ذلك دليلا عليهما في الشاهد فليس بدليل عليهما في الغائب. فتتناقضوا.
And he answers that they are neither the essence nor other than the essence. And he brings the suspicions of the Mu'tazila and presents them with his methodological trustworthiness, including that if the attribute is not the essence, then it is inevitably other than the essence, and affirming different things in pre-eternity contradicts tawhid; and that if they were established they would be eternal, and if they were eternal they would be qadim, and this leads to affirming many gods; and also that if attributes were established they would necessarily be enduring, and there is no way to say that each attribute endures by an endurance subsisting in it, because it is impossible for an attribute to subsist in an attribute. And al-Nasafi refutes these views with reason and revelation. In his refutation he reviews many suspicions that appeared from Abu Ali al-Jubbai, al-Allaf, Abu Hashim, and al-Ka'bi, and he says: We say to the Mu'tazila: You are among three matters: Either you equate the witnessed and the unseen in all that, and say that the power of the Maker is established by the evidence of the effect, and His knowledge is established by the evidence of the judgments of the effect, and in this is an abandonment of your school; or you differentiate between the witnessed and the unseen in all that, and say that the effect although it indicates His knowledge, in the unseen it indicates nothing, and this is the height of denial of the existence of the Maker; or you equate the witnessed and the unseen in the matter of its indication of power and knowledge, and say that although that is evidence for them in the witnessed, it is not evidence for them in the unseen, and thus you contradict yourselves.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila's denial of the attributes. Al-Nasafi first lists their main suspicions: if attributes are not the essence they must be other, implying multiple pre-eternal entities; if established they would be eternal and thus multiple gods; and attributes would need a separate endurance causing infinite regress. Then he counters by presenting a three-part logical division (taqsīm) concerning the analogy (tamthīl) between the witnessed (shāhid) and the unseen (ghā'ib). The three options are: (1) accept full analogy—then the effect in the unseen proves power and knowledge, which is what the Ahl al-Sunna affirm, but the Mu'tazila reject this; (2) reject all analogy—then the effect gives no knowledge of God, leading to atheism; (3) accept analogy for power but not for knowledge—this is arbitrary and inconsistent. Thus the Mu'tazila are forced into contradiction. This is a classic kalam argument using the logic of shāhid and ghā'ib.

Key Terms
شاهد
غائب
قدرة
علم
مفعول
دلالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the trilemma, what is the consequence of the Mu'tazila choosing Option 2 (full differentiation between shāhid and ghā'ib)?
A) They must abandon their school.
B) They fall into self-contradiction.
C) They deny the existence of the Maker.
D) They affirm the attributes of God.

Key Takeaway
The trilemma forces the Mu'tazila into an inescapable logical bind: they must either accept divine attributes, deny God's existence, or be inconsistent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you willing to follow logical arguments to their conclusion, even when they force you to abandon deeply held beliefs? Where in your own thinking about God do you make convenient distinctions that might be inconsistent?
?
When you present arguments for God, do you use evidence selectively—accepting what supports your view and dismissing what doesn't—or do you embrace full consistency even if it costs you?
?
If someone showed you that a core belief of yours leads to an inescapable contradiction, would you have the humility to change, or would you cling to it at the expense of truth? What would it take for you to abandon a position you once held dear?

Al-Maturidi's Formula: 'By His Essence'
Al-Nasafi quotes al-Maturidi and clarifies his intent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that al-Maturidi's phrase 'knowing by His essence' does not deny attributes but refutes the illusion of otherness.

Core Idea
God's attributes are real and eternal, not separate from His essence.

When al-Maturidi says God is knowing 'by His essence,' it might sound like the Mu'tazili denial of attributes. But as al-Nasafi explains, this phrase is meant to guard against thinking attributes are 'other' than God. Let's explore this nuanced position.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Maturidi's statement
Read the Arabic passage where al-Maturidi affirms that Allah is knowing, living, and powerful 'by His essence'. Notice the exact wording.
2
Understand the intended meaning
Al-Nasafi clarifies that al-Maturidi did not intend to negate attributes like the Mu'tazila. Instead, he aimed to reject the illusion that attributes are separate entities (mughāyara).
The formula 'by His essence' safeguards against both anthropomorphism and outright denial.
3
Contrast with the Mu'tazili view
The Mu'tazila also used similar language, but they denied any real attributes. Al-Maturidi affirmed attributes as real, so his phrase has a different purpose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد حديث طويل يثبت فيه الصفات، ويرد على منكريها، يقول: إن أبا منصور الماتريدي قال : إن الله تعالى عالم بذاته حي بذاته، قادر بذاته، ــ ولا يريد بهذا الكلام نفي الصفات كالمعتزلة لأنه أثبتها ، ودفع شبه الخصوم عنها، وإنما أراد بذلك دفع وهم المغايرة. والكلام في الصفات بين المعتزلة الذين نفوها اعتقادا منهم أنهم بذلك ينزهون الله تعالى وبين الأشاعرة الذين أثبتوها إلا أنهم يقسمونها إلى صفات ذات وصفات فعل، ويقولون بقدمها، ويقولون بحدوثها ، وبين الماتريدية والطحاوية الذين يثبتونها كلها قديمة الله تعالى أطال فيه النسفي، ولم يلتزم بما ألزم به نفسه من تبسيط وإيجاز. وخلاصة الكلام في الصفات عنده أن الصفات ليست غير الله، وليست ذات الله، وليست بعض الله، بل كل صفة لا هي هو ، ولا غيره، لأن الغيرين موجودان يتصور وجود أحدهما مع انعدام الآخر، وذلك ممتنع في ذات الله تعالى وصفاته إذ ذاته وصفاته أزليتان، والعدم على الأزلي محال فلا مغايرة إذا.
And after a long discussion in which he affirms the attributes and refutes their deniers, he says: Abu Mansur al-Maturidi said: 'Allah most high is knowing by His essence, living by His essence, powerful by His essence'—and he does not intend by this speech to negate the attributes like the Mu'tazila, because he affirmed them and repelled the suspicions of the opponents against them; rather, he intended by that to repel the illusion of otherness. And the discussion on attributes among the Mu'tazila who negated them, believing thereby that they are exalting Allah most high, and among the Ash'aris who affirmed them but divide them into attributes of essence and attributes of action, and say about their eternity and their temporality, and among the Maturidis and Tahawis who affirm them all as eternal—al-Nasafi prolonged it and did not adhere to the simplification and brevity he had imposed on himself. And the summary of the discussion on attributes according to him is that the attributes are not other than God, nor are they God's essence, nor are they a part of God; rather, every attribute is neither He nor other than Him, because the two others are two existents for which the existence of one along with the non-existence of the other is conceivable, and that is impossible regarding the essence of Allah most high and His attributes, since His essence and attributes are both eternal, and non-existence of the eternal is impossible, so there is no otherness.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage presents the Maturidi position on the divine attributes and al-Nasafi's final verdict. First, he quotes Abu Mansur al-Maturidi's well-known formula: 'Allah is knowing by His essence, living by His essence, powerful by His essence.' Al-Nasafi clarifies that this is not a denial of the attributes like the Mu'tazila, but rather a way to dismiss any notion of otherness between God and His attributes. Then he contrasts three groups: the Mu'tazila who negate attributes entirely; the Ash'aris who affirm them but distinguish between essential and active attributes (some eternal, some created); and the Maturidis/Tahawis who affirm all attributes as eternal. Al-Nasafi admits he has gone into detail beyond his self-imposed brevity. The conclusion is a classic Maturidi formulation: attributes are not identical to God's essence (not 'ayn al-dhāt), nor are they other than God (ghayr), nor are they parts of God. The reason is that 'other' requires the possibility of one existing without the other, which is false for God and His attributes because both are eternal; non-existence cannot apply to the eternal. Thus there is no otherness (lā mughāyara).

Key Terms
عالم بذاته
حي بذاته
قادر بذاته
مغايرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that saying 'by His essence' means attributes are merely nominal or mental, similar to the Mu'tazili view.
Correction: Al-Nasafi explicitly states that al-Maturidi affirmed the attributes and only used 'by His essence' to reject the idea that attributes are separate entities. The attributes are real and eternal.

Checkpoint
What did al-Maturidi intend by saying 'Allah is knowing by His essence'?
A) To negate the reality of attributes entirely, like the Mu'tazila.
B) To affirm attributes but reject the notion that they are separate from God.
C) To claim that knowledge is identical to God's essence with no distinction.
D) To suggest that God's knowledge is created.

Key Takeaway
Al-Maturidi's formula affirms attributes as real and eternal while denying any separateness from God's essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of Allah's power or knowledge, do you ever unconsciously imagine them as 'things' next to Allah? How does al-Maturidi's phrase 'by His essence' challenge you to purify your mental image of Allah? What one step can you take today to train your mind to avoid that illusion?
?
Have you ever been tempted to describe Allah's attributes in a way that makes them seem distant or abstract, as if they were not truly His? This lesson shows that affirming attributes as real yet not separate preserves both His majesty and intimacy. Which attribute (mercy, justice, etc.) do you most struggle to see as truly His essence, and how will you remind yourself of this truth in your next moment of need?
?
The Mu'tazila thought that affirming separate attributes would lead to multiple gods. Al-Maturidi avoided that by teaching that attributes are not other. Is there any belief you hold about Allah that you have not examined enough, fearing it might lead to something you think is wrong? Will you now courageously seek the middle path of the scholars?

The Maturidi Conclusion: Attributes Neither Identical Nor Other
Al-Nasafi compares sectarian views and gives a final summary on attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why, according to al-Nasafi, divine attributes are neither God's essence nor other than Him, and how this differs from other schools.

Core Idea
Eternal attributes cannot be 'other' because otherness implies separability, impossible for the eternal.

After comparing the views of the Mu'tazila, Ash'aris, and Maturidis, al-Nasafi gives his final verdict: attributes are not identical to God, nor are they other, nor parts. The key is the impossibility of otherness when both essence and attributes are eternal. Let's unpack this.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
Read the passage and list the three groups: Mu'tazila (negate attributes), Ash'aris (divide attributes into essential and active, some eternal some temporal), and Maturidis/Tahawis (affirm all attributes as eternal).
2
Understand al-Nasafi's conclusion
Al-Nasafi states that attributes are not other than God, not His essence, and not a part of Him. They are 'neither He nor other than Him'.
This is the classic Maturidi formulation: lā huwa wa lā ghayruhu.
3
Grasp the reasoning about otherness
The definition of 'two others' requires that one can exist without the other. Since God's essence and attributes are both eternal, non-existence cannot occur, so otherness is impossible.
Eternity (azal) precludes the possibility of non-existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

Have you ever downplayed a divine attribute (like anger or justice) because it made you uncomfortable, thinking you were being more 'reverent'? The Eternal Speech of Allah vs. the Created Speech of the Mu'tazila
Al-Nasafi contrasts eternal divine speech with created speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fundamental difference between the Ahl al-Haqq view of God's speech as an eternal attribute and the Mu'tazila view of it as a created accident.

Core Idea
God's speech is eternal, not composed of letters or sounds, but a single attribute.

This lesson introduces the crucial debate over the nature of God's speech (kalām Allāh). Al-Nasafi presents the position of Ahl al-Haqq—that divine speech is an eternal attribute of God's essence, not consisting of letters or sounds—and contrasts it with the Mu'tazila who regard speech as a created accident in a physical locus. Understanding this distinction is foundational to Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the translation. Notice the direct contrast between the two positions.
The passage is the opening of a topic; it ends mid-sentence.
2
Identify the two views
Find where Ahl al-Haqq's position is stated and where the Mu'tazila's position begins. Note the key phrases: 'صفة أزلية' and 'عرض محدث'.
3
Reflect on the analogy
Al-Nasafi gives an analogy of God's names in different languages. Think about why this analogy supports the idea that speech is one attribute.
The analogy shows unity despite diversity of expressions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في نفي الحدوث عن كلام الله تعالى: يقول أهل الحق: إن كلام الله عز وجل صفة له أزلية قائمة بذاته، ليست من جنس الحروف والأصوات، منافية للآفة، والله تعالى متكلم بها. وهذه العبارات دالة عليه على معنى أنها عبارات عن كلام الله. والاختلاف يكون في العبارات المؤدية لا في كلام الله الذي هو صفة نفسية له، وذلك مثل تسمية الله تعالى في لغات مختلفة بأسامي مختلفة إلا أن ذاته واحد. ويقول جمهور المعتزلة : إن كلام الله تعالى عرض محدث في محل، وكلامه من
The discussion on negating temporality from the speech of Allah most high: The People of Truth say: The speech of Allah Almighty is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, not of the genus of letters and sounds, free from defect, and Allah most high is speaking (mutakallim) by it. And these expressions indicate it in the sense that they are expressions about the speech of Allah. And the difference is in the expressions that convey, not in the speech of Allah which is an attribute of His self (nafsiyya), similar to calling Allah most high by different names in different languages while His essence is one. And the majority of the Mu'tazila say: The speech of Allah most high is an accident originated in a locus, and His speech is from
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is the opening of a new topic: the speech of Allah (kalām Allāh). Al-Nasafi states the position of Ahl al-Haqq (the People of Truth, i.e., the Ash'aris and Maturidis): God's speech is an eternal attribute, not composed of letters or sounds, free from any imperfection. The expressions (alphabets, voices) are merely indicators of that inner divine speech. The variation is only in the expressions, not in the speech itself, which is a single, eternal attribute of God (ṣifat nafsiyya). He gives the analogy of God being called by different names in different languages while His essence remains one. Then he contrasts this with the Mu'tazila who consider God's speech to be an accident (ʿaraḍ) created in a locus (i.e., in a physical medium like a tablet or heart). The passage cuts off mid-sentence, but it introduces the fundamental disagreement.

Key Terms
كلام الله
صفة أزلية
حروف
أصوات
عبارات
عرض محدث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The disagreement between Ahl al-Haqq and Mu'tazila is about whether the letters of the Quran are created or not.
Correction: The core disagreement is about the nature of God's speech itself: is it an eternal attribute of His essence or a created accident? The debate about letters and sounds is secondary; even Ahl al-Haqq affirm that the physical expressions (letters, sounds) are created, but the eternal speech they indicate is not.

Checkpoint
According to Ahl al-Haqq, what is the nature of God's speech?
A) A created accident subsisting in a physical medium.
B) An eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence, not composed of letters or sounds.
C) A set of letters and sounds revealed to prophets.
D) An attribute that is identical to God's essence.

Key Takeaway
God's speech is an eternal attribute of His essence, not a created accident; the expressions in Scripture are indicators of that eternal speech, not the speech itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, are you truly connecting with the eternal speech of Allah, or are you just moving your lips over letters and sounds? How would your heart change if you remembered that these words are only expressions pointing to an unfathomable, eternal attribute of your Lord?
?
You just read that Allah's speech is free from defect and not of the genus of letters and sounds. Does your reverence for the Quran reflect that belief? Or do you sometimes treat it like any other book—picking it up casually, reading without presence of heart, and putting it down unchanged? What would it take for you to approach it as an encounter with the eternal?
?
The difference between Ahl al-Haqq and the Mu'tazila is not just historical—it touches the core of whether you believe Allah's attributes are perfect and eternal. Have you ever doubted that Allah's word is truly timeless? If not, why does your urgency to act upon it not match its eternal weight? Commit to one change in how you engage with the Quran starting today.

4 min
The Maturidi Formula: Attributes Neither Identical Nor Other
Nasafi states the Maturidi conclusion on attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi position that divine attributes are neither identical to Allah's essence nor separate from it, and the rational argument supporting this via the impossibility of otherness between eternal entities.

Core Idea
Divine attributes are neither identical to nor separate from Allah's essence.

In this concluding passage, Imam al-Nasafi encapsulates the Maturidi school's precise position on the relationship between Allah's essence and His attributes. Having previously discussed various views, he now presents the definitive formula that avoids both extremes of identity and separation. The passage provides both the summary and the rational proof that otherness is impossible between eternal realities.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic and English carefully, noting the three negations.
The passage is dense; take your time with each phrase.
2
Understand the Maturidi formula
Focus on the phrase 'ليست غير الله، وليست ذات الله، وليست بعض الله' and then the positive statement 'بل كل صفة لا هي هو، ولا غيره.'
The formula is neither identity nor otherness.
3
Analyze the proof against otherness
Study the argument that otherness requires possible independent existence, which is impossible for the eternal essence and attributes.
The key premise: 'العدم على الأزلي محال.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخلاصة الكلام في الصفات عنده أن الصفات ليست غير الله، وليست ذات الله، وليست بعض الله، بل كل صفة لا هي هو، ولا غيره، لأن الغيرين موجودان يتصور وجود أحدهما مع انعدام الآخر، وذلك ممتنع في ذات الله تعالى وصفاته إذ ذاته وصفاته أزليتان، والعدم على الأزلي محال فلا مغايرة إذا.
And the summary of the discourse on the attributes according to him is that the attributes are not other than Allah, nor are they the essence of Allah, nor are they a part of Allah. Rather, every attribute is neither He nor other than He, because two distinct entities are existent and it is conceivable that one of them exist with the non-existence of the other, and that is impossible in the case of Allah's essence and His attributes since His essence and attributes are eternal, and non-existence is impossible upon the eternal, so there is no otherness.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal conclusion defining the Maturidi position on the relationship between Allah's essence and His attributes. It begins by stating the summary: the attributes are not other than Allah (i.e., not separate entities), not identical to His essence (so not a simple identity without distinction), and not a part of Him (so not composite). Then it explains the reasoning: for two things to be 'other' (غيرين), each must be able to exist without the other. But Allah's essence and attributes are both eternal, and non-existence cannot apply to the eternal. Therefore, the concept of otherness (مغايرة) is impossible. The final phrase 'فلا مغايرة إذا' concludes that there is no otherness, affirming the unique relationship that the attributes are neither identical nor separate.

Key Terms
صفات
مغايرة
أزلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The idea that 'not identical, not other' is a logical impossibility or a contradiction.
Correction: Nasafi's argument shows that otherness is defined as separable existence. Since eternal entities cannot be conceived as nonexistent, the relationship is unique: neither identity nor separateness.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why is otherness (mughāyara) impossible between Allah's essence and His attributes?
A) Because attributes are created and temporally contingent.
B) Because both are eternal, and otherness implies separability which cannot apply to the eternal.
C) Because attributes are identical to the essence in every respect.
D) Because Allah's essence cannot have any attributes.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi concludes that Allah's attributes are neither identical to His essence nor separate from it, because otherness would require possible nonexistence, which is impossible for eternal realities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you describe Allah as ar-Rahman or al-Karim, do you unconsciously imagine these as distinct 'things' He possesses? How does the truth that they are neither identical nor separate from His essence change the way you should feel when you call upon Him? Will you pause before each name to remind your heart that you are addressing His very being?
?
The passage says otherness requires possible non-existence, but Allah is eternal. Does your mind still try to sneak in a hint of limitation, thinking of His attributes as something added to Him? What concrete step can you take today to worship Him with the awe that comes from knowing nothing is separate from His eternal reality—not even His mercy or power?

The Eternal Speech of Allah: Ahl al-Haqq's Definition
Nasafi states the Ahl al-Haqq definition and distinguishes expressions from the attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi definition of divine speech as an eternal attribute distinct from recited expressions.

Core Idea
Allah’s speech is an eternal attribute; the recited Quran is its expression, not its essence.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi presents the foundational Sunni position on divine speech. He distinguishes between the eternal attribute of speech in Allah’s essence and the created expressions that convey it. Understanding this distinction is key to avoiding the error of equating the recited Quran with Allah’s eternal attribute.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the translation. Note the key terms.
2
Identify the two key claims
First, speech is an eternal attribute. Second, it is not composed of letters or sounds.
3
Reflect on the analogy
The passage compares variations in expressions to different names for Allah in languages. Think about how this reinforces the unity of the attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في نفي الحدوث عن كلام الله تعالى: يقول أهل الحق: إن كلام الله عز وجل صفة له أزلية قائمة بذاته، ليست من جنس الحروف والأصوات، منافية للآفة، والله تعالى متكلم بها. وهذه العبارات دالة عليه على معنى أنها عبارات عن كلام الله. والاختلاف يكون في العبارات المؤدية لا في كلام الله الذي هو صفة نفسية له، وذلك مثل تسمية الله تعالى في لغات مختلفة بأسامي مختلفة إلا أن ذاته واحد. ويقول جمهور المعتزلة : إن كلام الله تعالى عرض محدث في محل، وكلامه من جنس الحروف والأصوات، ويزعم الجبائي أن كلامه تعالى عبارة عن حروف مؤلفة بأصوات مقطعة على وجه مخصوص. ويعرض النسفي لتعريف أبي هاشم ويفرق بينه وبين تعريف أبيه، ثم يعرض كلام جعفر بن حرب، وجعفر بن مبشر، ويلخصه في أنهما يقولان بأن كلام الله خلقه الله في اللوح المحفوظ، ولا يجوز أن ينقل عنه، وما يقرأ ويحفظ فهو حكاية القرآن. وهذا القول نفسه هو قول الكعبي ومن تابعه من معتزلة بغداد أما النظّار فيقول: إن القرآن جسم، وعلى هذا فإن الله عندهم جميعاً متكلم أي خالق للكلام، ويخرج النسفي من جملة هؤلاء من لا يمكنهم القول بأن الله متكلم مثل أبي بكر الأصم، ومعمر السلمي، وثمامة بن الأشرس ويقول: إنه بناء على كلامهم لا يكون الله أمراً ولا ناهيا، ولا يكون القرآن كلامه، وفي هذا رد للشرائع، وتكذيب للرسول.
The discourse on negating temporality from the speech of Allah: The people of truth say: Verily the speech of Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, is an eternal attribute subsisting with His essence, not of the genus of letters and sounds, free from deficiency, and Allah is a speaker by it. And these expressions indicate it in the sense that they are expressions of the speech of Allah. And the difference is in the expressions that convey, not in the speech of Allah which is a mental attribute of His. This is like naming Allah in different languages with different names while His essence is one. And the majority of the Mu'tazila say: Verily the speech of Allah is an accident created in a locus, and His speech is of the genus of letters and sounds. And al-Jubba'i claims that His speech is composed of letters arranged with distinct sounds in a specific manner. And Nasafi mentions the definition of Abu Hashim and distinguishes between it and his father's definition. Then he presents the statement of Ja'far ibn Harb and Ja'far ibn Mubashshir and summarizes it as both of them saying that the speech of Allah is something Allah created in the Preserved Tablet, and it is not permissible to transmit it from it, and what is recited and memorized is a narration of the Qur'an. And this very statement is the statement of al-Ka'bi and those who followed him from the Mu'tazila of Baghdad. As for al-Nazzam, he says: Verily the Qur'an is a body. And on this basis, according to all of them, Allah is a speaker, i.e., creator of speech. And Nasafi excludes from the group of these those who cannot say that Allah is a speaker, such as Abu Bakr al-Asamm, Mu'ammar al-Sulami, and Thumama ibn al-Ashras. And he says: Based on their statement, Allah is neither commanding nor forbidding, nor is the Qur'an His speech, and this is a rejection of the laws and a denial of the Messenger.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a comparative doctrinal exposition. It begins by stating the position of Ahl al-Haqq (the People of Truth): Allah's speech is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, not composed of letters or sounds, and He is a speaker by it. The recited expressions (عبارات) are merely indicators of that eternal speech, not the speech itself. The difference is in the expressions, not the eternal attribute. Then it lists various Mu'tazila views: the majority say speech is a created accident composed of letters and sounds; al-Jubba'i specifies it as ordered letters with distinct sounds; Abu Hashim's definition differs (the author does not elaborate here); Ja'far ibn Harb and Ja'far ibn Mubashshir say it is created in the Preserved Tablet and cannot be transmitted, so what we read is a narration (حكاية) not the original; al-Ka'bi and Baghdad Mu'tazila follow this; al-Nazzam claims the Qur'an is a body. All these Mu'tazila consider Allah a speaker in the sense of creating speech. Nasafi then identifies a group (Abu Bakr al-Asamm, Mu'ammar al-Sulami, Thumama ibn al-Ashras) who cannot even affirm that Allah is a speaker because their principles deny that Allah is a command-giver. Nasafi warns that this entails a rejection of the divine laws (sharā'i') and a denial of the Prophet.

Key Terms
كلام الله
صفة نفسية
حروف وأصوات
عبارات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Believing that the recited Quran (the Arabic text) is identical to the eternal speech of Allah.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the recited expressions are ‘indications’ (عبارات) of the eternal speech, not the eternal speech itself. The eternal attribute is beyond letters and sounds.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between the recited expressions (عبارات) and Allah's speech?
A) They are the same thing.
B) The expressions are created and indicate the eternal speech.
C) The expressions are eternal like the speech.
D) The expressions are unrelated to the speech.

Key Takeaway
Allah's speech is an eternal attribute distinct from created expressions; the recited Quran indicates that eternal speech but is not it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you consciously connect your recitation to the eternal speech of Allah, or do you focus only on the sounds and letters? What practical step can you take today to increase your awareness of the divine attribute behind the words?
?
The passage emphasizes that Allah's speech is free from deficiency. Do you ever feel that certain verses are incomplete or inadequate for your situation? How can you remind yourself that it is your understanding that is deficient, not the speech itself?
?
If the expressions of Allah's speech differ across languages and recitations, but the eternal attribute is one, how should that affect your attitude towards other Muslims who recite differently? Will you commit to listening to a different qira'ah this week with a heart that seeks the one eternal speech?

Mu'tazila Positions on Divine Speech and Their Critique
Nasafi recounts Mu'tazila views on speech and critiques those who deny Allah is a speaker.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various Mu'tazila views on divine speech and Nasafi's critique of those who deny Allah as speaker.

Core Idea
Most Mu'tazila said speech is created; some even denied Allah is a speaker, leading to rejection of revelation.

After presenting the orthodox position, Imam al-Nasafi surveys multiple Mu'tazila opinions on divine speech. He shows that while most considered Allah a speaker by creating speech, a fringe group could not even affirm that, resulting in a denial of the divine law and the Prophet's mission.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the different views
Read the Arabic and translation. Identify the various Mu'tazila positions: majority, al-Jubba'i, Abu Hashim, Ja'far ibn Harb, al-Ka'bi, al-Nazzam.
2
Identify the common point among most
Notice that despite differences, most affirm Allah as speaker (creator of speech).
3
Focus on the exception group
Read about Abu Bakr al-Asamm, Mu'ammar, and Thumama. Understand why Nasafi singles them out.
4
Understand the implication
Nasafi says their view leads to rejecting laws and denouncing the Prophet. Think about why this is a serious charge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

What would change in your recitation if you suddenly realized that Allah is speaking to you right now, in this moment?
?

Is there a command in the Qur'an that you have knowingly neglected or explained away, perhaps because you do not really believe it comes directly from the One who has absolute authority over you? Reflect on one specific command—how would your life look if you obeyed it as if Allah Himself just said it?
?

Are you willing to confront the possibility that your heart has excused itself from submission? Ask Allah tonight to make you among those who say 'We hear and we obey' with sincerity.

The Command 'Be' Proves Allah's Speech is Eternal
Nasafi refutes Mu'tazila by proving the command 'Be' is eternal, preventing infinite regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses the verse 'Be' to prove that Allah's speech is eternal, refuting the Mu'tazila claim that it is created.

Core Idea
If Allah's command 'Be' were created, an infinite regress would occur, making creation impossible.

After presenting the doubts of the Mu'tazila, Nasafi responds with a powerful argument based on a well-known Qur'anic verse. The verse states that Allah says 'Be' to a thing and it comes to be. By analyzing this verse, Nasafi shows that the command 'Be' itself cannot be created, because that would lead to an impossible infinite chain of commands. This lesson walks through that argument and explains why it is decisive.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully, noting the key terms like 'محدث' and 'تسلسل'. Then read the translation to ensure understanding.
The verse reference is Surah al-Nahl 16:40.
2
Identify the logical structure
Notice that the argument has two parts: first, Allah creates things by the command 'Be'; second, if that command were created, it would need another command, leading to infinite regress, which is impossible. Therefore, the command must be eternal.
3
Reflect on the refutation
Consider how this argument refutes the Mu'tazila position that all divine speech is created. The key is that the verse itself is used to prove the opposite.
This argument is attributed to al-Ash'ari as well.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد أن يعرض كل الشبه، يرد عليها ليدحضها. وفي رده يتعلق بما تعلق به الأشعري من قوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّمَا قَوْلُنَا لِشَيْءٍ إِذَا أَرَدْنَهُ أَن نَقُولَ لَهُ كُن فَيَكُونُ ﴾ [النحل: ٤٠] فقد أخبر سبحانه وتعالى أنه يحدث المحدثات بخطاب كن، ولو كان هذا الخطاب محدثا لأحدثه بخطاب آخر إلى ما لا يتناهى، وتعلق وجود العالم بما لا يتناهى من الخطاب مما يدخل وجوده في حيز الممتنعات، وعلى هذا يثبت أن قوله تعالى كن ليس محدثا.
And after presenting all the doubts, he responds to them in order to refute them. And in his response he adheres to what al-Ash'ari adhered to from His statement, the Exalted: 'Our word to a thing when We intend it is only that We say to it, "Be," and it comes to be.' [Surah al-Nahl: 40]. For He, glorified and exalted, informed that He brings about originated things by the address 'Be', and if this address were originated, it would necessitate another address to bring it about, ad infinitum, and the existence of the world being dependent on an infinite chain of addresses is something that enters its existence into the realm of impossibilities. And on this basis, it is established that His statement 'Be' is not originated.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a refutation (رَدّ) of the Mu'tazila claim that Allah's speech is created. It begins by noting that after presenting the Mu'tazila's doubts (شبه), Nasafi responds by adhering to the same proof that al-Ash'ari used: the Qur'anic verse (16:40) where Allah says that His word to a thing when He intends it is 'Be' and it comes to be. The argument runs: Allah informs us that He originates things by the command 'Be' (بخطاب كن). If that command were itself originated (محدث), it would require another command to create it, leading to an infinite regress (إلى ما لا يتناهى). The existence of the world would then depend on an infinite chain of commands, which is impossible (ممتنع). Therefore, the command 'Be' cannot be originated; hence it is eternal. This refutes the Mu'tazila who claimed all divine speech is created.

Key Terms
قدم الكلام
تسلسل
محدث
خطاب كن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'Be' implies that Allah's speech is created because it is a 'word' (قول) addressed to a thing.
Correction: The verse actually shows the opposite: if the command 'Be' were created, it would require another command to create it, leading to an infinite regress which is impossible. Therefore, the command must be uncreated and eternal.

Checkpoint
What is the central logical problem that Nasafi uses to prove that Allah's command 'Be' is not created?
A) The command is composed of letters and sounds.
B) If created, it would require another command to create it, leading to an infinite regress that makes creation impossible.
C) The verse says 'Be' is uncreated explicitly.
D) Mu'tazila admit that some speech is eternal.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi's proof from the verse 'Be' establishes that Allah's speech is eternal, using the impossibility of infinite regress.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's command 'Be' were created, then every command of His would be temporary. How would that affect your confidence in His promises, such as the promise of Paradise? Have you ever treated a divine command as if it were temporary or optional?
?
The proof shows that infinite regress is impossible. Yet you may act as if your own actions are infinite — always delaying repentance. What would it mean to truly believe that your current moment is the only one that exists for you to respond to Allah's command?
?
Allah says 'Be' and it is — instantly. Is there any area of your life where you are waiting for a command from Allah that you already know? What keeps you from saying 'I am ready' and acting on it right now?

Mu'tazilite Proofs for the Createdness of God's Speech
Author presents Mu'tazilite scriptural and rational proofs for createdness of speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two types of proofs (scriptural and rational) that the Mu'tazila used to argue that God's speech is created.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila combined scripture and analogy to claim God's speech is created.

Before we can appreciate the refutation, we need to see the arguments that the Mu'tazila put forward. In this passage, the author presents their scriptural proofs (shubah naqliyya) and rational proof (shubah 'aqliyya) for the createdness of God's speech. Understanding these will help us grasp why the refutation is necessary.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the distinction between scriptural and rational proofs.
Focus on the two categories.
2
Identify the scriptural proofs
Look for the two verses cited: one about 'making' the Qur'an Arabic and one about a 'new' reminder. Understand how they equate 'making' with 'creating' and 'new' with 'created'.
3
Examine the rational proof
The rational proof uses analogy (qiyas al-gha'ib 'ala al-shahid). It argues that in the observed world, speech consists of letters and sounds, so God's speech must be similar. This is a key kalam argument.
Think about why this analogy might be problematic.
4
Reflect on the strength of these proofs
Consider why the Mu'tazila thought these proofs were decisive. Write down any questions you have before moving to the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يناقش آراء المعتزلة مبينا شبههم النقلية والعقلية، وعلى سبيل المثال لشبههم النقلية قوله تعالى: إِنَّا جَعَلْتَهُ قُرْءَانَا عَرَبِيًّا } [الزخرف: (٣]، والجعل والتخليق واحد، وقوله تعالى : مَا يَأْتِيهِم مِّن ذِكْرِ مِن رَّبِّهِم تُحْدَثٍ ﴾ [الأنبياء: ٢] والمحدث مخلوق. أما عن شبههم العقلية فمنها قياس الغائب على الشاهد بأن في الشاهد الكلام يكون من جنس الحروف والأصوات فمن أثبت غير ذلك في الغائب يخرج عن قضية العقول. وبعد أن يعرض كل الشبه، يرد عليها ليدحضها. وفي رده يتعلق بما تعلق به الأشعري من قوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّمَا قَوْلُنَا لِشَيْءٍ إِذَا أَرَدْنَهُ أَن نَّقُولَ لَهُ كُن فَيَكُونُ ﴾ [النحل: ٤٠] فقد أخبر سبحانه وتعالى أنه يحدث المحدثات بخطاب ،كن، ولو كان هذا الخطاب محدثا لأحدثه بخطاب آخر إلى ما لا يتناهى، وتعلق وجود العالم بما لا يتناهى من الخطاب مما يدخل وجوده في حيز الممتنعات، وعلى هذا يثبت أن قوله تعالى كن ليس محدثا.
Then he discusses the views of the Mu'tazila, showing their scriptural (naqliyya) and rational ('aqliyya) proofs. For example of their scriptural proofs is His statement—exalted is He: 'Indeed, We have made it an Arabic Qur'an' (al-Zukhruf 3), and making (ja'l) and creating (takhlīq) are the same. And His statement: 'There does not come to them a new reminder from their Lord' (al-Anbiya 2), and what is new (muhdath) is created. As for their rational proofs, among them is the analogy of the unobserved (gha'ib) on the observed (shahid), that in the observed, speech is of the genus of letters and sounds; so whoever asserts something else in the unobserved departs from the judgment of intellects. And after he presents all the proofs, he refutes them to demolish them. And in his refutation, he adheres to what al-Ash'ari adhered to from His statement: 'Our only saying to a thing when We intend it is that We say to it "Be," and it is' (al-Nahl 40). For He—glory be to Him—informed that He brings about created things by the address 'Be.' And if this address were created, He would have created it by another address, leading to an infinite regress; and the dependency of the existence of the world upon infinite addresses entails its existence entering the realm of impossibilities. On this basis, it is established that His statement 'Be' is not created.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage presents the Mu'tazilite arguments and then refutes them using the verse from Surah al-Nahl. First, the scriptural proofs: they cite verses where 'making' (ja'l) is used for the Qur'an, equating it with creation, and where God says a 'new' (muhdath) reminder comes, proving the Qur'an is created. Second, the rational proof: they analogize God's speech to human speech, which is composed of letters and sounds, so anything else would be unreasonable. The author then refutes these by adopting al-Ash'ari's argument from the verse 'Innama qawluna...' The argument is that God creates things by saying 'Be.' If that command itself were created, it would require another command to create it, leading to an infinite regress. Since an infinite regress is impossible in reality, the command 'Be' must be uncreated and eternal. This refutes the Mu'tazilite claim that God's speech is created, because the very act of creation by speech implies the speech itself is not created.

Key Terms
شبه نقلية
شبه عقلية
قياس الغائب على الشاهد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a scriptural proof used by the Mu'tazila?
A) The verse 'Innama qawluna li shay'in'
B) The verse 'Inna ja'alnahu Qur'an Arabiyyan'
C) The analogy of the seen and unseen
D) The concept of infinite regress

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila used both scriptural verses and rational analogy to argue that God's speech is created.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verse 'Indeed, We have made it an Arabic Qur'an,' do you feel the weight that this speech is from God, or do you treat it as ordinary words? How does acknowledging its origin affect your daily engagement with the Qur'an?
?
The Mu'tazila projected human speech onto God's speech through analogy. In what areas of your life do you unconsciously project human limitations onto God, and what would it mean to let God be God without confining Him to your expectations?
?
This passage shows the Mu'tazila using a verse out of context (according to Sunnis) to support their view. Have you ever twisted a verse or hadith to justify a desire or position you already held? How can you cultivate the humility to let Scripture correct you rather than the other way around?

Refutation of Mu'tazilite Proofs: The Infinite Regress Argument
Author refutes Mu'tazilites using verse 16:40 and infinite regress argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the verse 'Innama qawluna' demonstrates that God's command 'Be' is uncreated, thereby refuting the Mu'tazilite position.

Core Idea
If 'Be' were created, an infinite chain of commands would be needed, which is impossible.

Having seen the Mu'tazilite proofs, we now turn to the refutation. The author adopts al-Ash'ari's argument from the verse 'Our only saying to a thing when We intend it is that We say to it "Be," and it is' (16:40). This verse shows that God creates by His command. The key insight: if that command itself were created, it would need another command, leading to an infinite regress. Since infinite regress is impossible, the command 'Be' must be uncreated and eternal. This refutes the claim that God's speech is created.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Pay attention to the logical structure: if A then B, B is impossible, therefore not A.
The argument is a classic reductio ad absurdum.
2
Understand the key verse
The verse 'Innama qawluna' indicates that God creates by saying 'Be'. This is the starting point.
3
Analyze the infinite regress argument
Suppose the command 'Be' were created. Then it would need another command to create it, and that command would need another, ad infinitum. This would make the existence of the world dependent on an infinite chain, which is impossible.
Impossibility of actual infinite regress is a core principle in kalam.
4
Draw the conclusion
Therefore, the command 'Be' cannot be created; it must be uncreated and eternal, part of God's eternal speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

This passage presents the Mu'tazilite arguments and then refutes them using the verse from Surah al-Nahl. The Three Divisions Argument for the Eternity of God's Speech
The author presents a division argument against the creation of God's speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument that if God's speech were created, it would have to fall into one of three impossible categories, and why each is impossible.

Core Idea
If God's speech were created, it would have to be either in His essence, in another locus, or without a locus—all impossible.

This lesson examines a key rational proof used by Maturidi theologians to establish the pre-eternity of God's speech. The argument proceeds by dividing possible scenarios if speech were created and then showing that each scenario is rationally impossible. By understanding this division, you will see why the only coherent position is that God's speech is eternal.

Guided Path
1
Understand the structure of the argument
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that it presents a division (taqseem) argument: if speech is created, it must fit into one of three exhaustive categories. Identify the three categories mentioned.
The author asserts that all three are impossible and promises evidence for each.
2
Examine each of the three divisions
List the three possible loci for created speech: (1) in God's essence, (2) in a locus other than His essence, (3) not in a locus at all. Consider briefly why each might be problematic.
The details of why each is impossible are not given here but will be explored in subsequent lessons.
3
Grasp the conclusion
Since all three divisions are impossible, the original assumption that speech is created cannot hold. Therefore, God's speech must be pre-eternal (qadim).
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقول: ومن الأدلة المعقولة على قدم كلام الله تعالى أنه لو كان مخلوقا، حادثا لكان الأمر لا يخلو إما أن يكون حادثا في ذات الله تعالى، وإما أن يكون حادثا في محل آخر سوى ذاته تعالى، وإما أن يكون حادثا لا في محل، ولا تصور لقسم رابع، وهذه الأقسام كلها ممتنعة، ويدلل على امتناع كل قسم منها.
Then he says: Among the rational proofs for the pre-eternity (qidam) of God's speech—exalted is He—is that if it were created (makhluq) and originated (hadith), then the matter would not be free from either: it would be originated in the essence (dhat) of God—exalted is He, or it would be originated in a locus other than His essence, or it would be originated not in a locus; and there is no conception of a fourth division. And these divisions are all impossible (mumtani'a), and he provides evidence for the impossibility of each division.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage presents a rational proof for the eternity of God's speech. The author uses a division (taqseem) argument: if speech were created, it would have to be either: (1) created within God's essence, which would imply change and temporal events in God; (2) created in a separate locus (like the Preserved Tablet or the air); or (3) created without a locus. The author says each of these is impossible, and he will provide evidence for their impossibility. The argument is that since none of these options is valid, the original assumption (that speech is created) must be false, and speech must be eternal. The author does not expand on the impossibility proofs here but asserts them.

Key Terms
قدم الكلام
حادث
ذات الله
محل
قسم رابع
ممتعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is possible for an accident (like speech) to exist without a locus.
Correction: According to rational theology, accidents cannot subsist by themselves; they require a locus (substrate) to exist. The third division (no locus) is therefore impossible.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many possible divisions are there for God's speech if it were created?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
The three-division argument shows that if God's speech were created, it would have to be impossible in all possible scenarios, thus proving its eternity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The Dichotomy and Perfection Arguments for God's Eternal Speech
Two rational proofs for God's eternal speech: dichotomy and perfection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two rational arguments that establish the necessity of God's eternal speech: the dichotomy argument and the perfection argument.

Core Idea
God must be eternally speaking, or else obligations vanish and silence would make Him imperfect.

This passage presents two concise arguments that force the conclusion that God's speech is an eternal attribute. First, a logical dichotomy: either God is eternally speaking with command and prohibition, or the very basis of religious duties collapses. Second, an argument from perfection: silence would be a deficiency, and deficiency cannot belong to the Eternal. Together, they anchor the doctrine of kalām nafsī (inner speech).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once for its overall flow, then read the full translation. Notice the two 'Even' (إما) constructions.
The passage uses a logical structure with two separate arguments.
2
Identify the two arguments
Find where the first argument (dichotomy) ends and the second (perfection) begins. Mark them mentally.
The first concludes with 'بذلك تبطل فرضية العبادات'. The second begins with 'ويقول : إنه تعالى لو لم يكن...'
3
Analyze the dichotomy argument
Notice how the author presents two options: either God's speech subsists in His essence, or He has no speech at all. Then show the consequence of denial: no obligations.
This forces acceptance of the first option.
4
Analyze the perfection argument
The second argument shows that if God were not speaking in pre-eternity, He would have silence, which is a deficiency. Deficiency is a sign of origination, impossible for God.
Thus God must be eternally speaking.
5
Connect the arguments
Reflect on why both arguments are needed: the dichotomy shows necessity, the perfection removes any doubt about possibility.
Together they establish speech as an eternal attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد ذلك يقول : إما أن يقال إن كلام الله تعالى قائم بذاته، وهو متكلم آمر ناه، وإما أن ينكر أن يكون الله تعالى كلام وأمر ونهي، وبذلك تبطل فرضية العبادات، لانعدام أمره ونهيه. ويقول : إنه تعالى لو لم يكن في الأزل متكلما لكان موصوفا بضد من أضداد الكلام كالسكوت، واتصافه تعالى بذلك محال لأنه نقص، والنقص من أمارات الحدوث.
And after that he says: Either it is said that God's speech—exalted is He—subsists in His essence, and He is speaking (mutakallim), commanding, prohibiting, or it is denied that God has speech, command, and prohibition, and thereby the obligation of acts of worship is nullified, due to the absence of His command and prohibition. And he says: If He—exalted is He—were not in pre-eternity speaking, then He would be described with an opposite of speech, such as silence (sukut), and His being described with that is impossible because it is a deficiency (naqs), and deficiency is among the signs of origination (huduth).
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage contains two arguments. First, a dichotomy: either God's speech is an attribute subsisting in His essence (making Him a commander and prohibitor), or one denies that God has speech, command, and prohibition. If the latter, then the very basis for religious obligations (the commands and prohibitions) is lost. This argument forces the necessity of accepting the first option. Second, the argument from perfection: if God were not pre-eternally speaking, He would be characterized by the opposite of speech, like silence. However, silence in God is impossible because it is a deficiency, and deficiency is a sign of being originated (hadith). Since God is eternal and perfect, He cannot have deficiency. Therefore, God must be eternally speaking. This reinforces the doctrine that speech is an eternal attribute.

Key Terms
قائم بذاته
آمر ناه
فرضية العبادات
سكوت
نقص
أمارات الحدوث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God could be silent without it being a deficiency, because silence can be a virtue in humans.
Correction: The argument treats silence as a privation of speech. For God, speech is a perfection; its absence is a deficiency. Since God is infinitely perfect, He cannot have any deficiency.

Checkpoint
According to the second argument, why must God be eternally speaking?
A) Because silence would be a deficiency, and deficiency indicates createdness.
B) Because the Qur'an says He speaks.
C) Because the Prophet heard His speech.
D) Because speech is an accident.

Key Takeaway
God's eternal speech is necessary because otherwise obligations would be baseless and silence would be a deficiency incompatible with His perfection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's speech is eternal and has always been addressed to you, how does that change the way you listen to His commands? Are you truly attentive to His eternal address, or do you treat His words as distant and outdated?
?
The author argues that without God's command, worship obligations vanish. Reflect on a time when you neglected a religious duty. Did your action betray a hidden assumption that God's command is not eternally binding on you? What will you do today to reaffirm that His speech is ever-present?
?
Silence is considered a deficiency for God. Yet how often do we remain silent about His commands in our daily lives? In what area of your life are you effectively mute about what God has spoken – and what would it cost you to speak out?

Divine Speech as an Eternal Attribute
Nasafi states that divine speech is an eternal attribute, not letters/sounds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God's speech is one eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, not composed of letters or sounds.

Core Idea
God's speech is one eternal attribute, not created letters or sounds.

Nasafi begins by clarifying the true nature of divine speech, which is an essential attribute of God. This sets the foundation for distinguishing the Creator's eternal speech from temporal expressions. Let's examine his precise statements.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully. Notice how Nasafi defines divine speech: it is an attribute subsisting in God's essence, not from the genus of letters and sounds.
Remember: 'صفة قائمة بذاته' means an attribute that inheres in God's essence.
2
Identify key characteristics
List the characteristics Nasafi mentions: it is one attribute, it is eternal, it encompasses command and prohibition. See how these all follow from the definition.
3
Connect to common misunderstanding
Many people confuse the created expressions (Qur'an in written form) with the eternal speech. Nasafi explicitly separates them. Reflect on why this distinction matters for theology.
This guards against the misconception that God's speech is temporal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى هذا فإن كلام الله تعالى صفة قائمة بذاته، ليست من جنس الحروف، والأصوات، وهي صفة واحدة وهي أمر بما أمر به ونهي عما نهى عنه، وهي صفة أزلية. ثم هذه العبارات العبرية أو السريانية عبارات عنه، وهو يتأدى بها، وهذه العبارات حروف وأصوات وهي محدثة، مخلوقة في محلها، دلالات وهي على الكلام الذي هو صفة أزلية الله تعالى. وجعفر بن حرب وجعفر بن مبشر والكعبي من المعتزلة يقولون بقولنا: إن كلام الله في اللوح المحفوظ والمنزل عبارات دالة عليه، غير أنهم يقولون: إن هذه العبارات مؤدية ما فى اللوح المحفوظ، وهنا الخلاف بيننا وبينهم حيث نقول: هي مؤدية ما قام بالذات من الصفة.
And on this basis, indeed the speech of God Most High is an attribute subsisting in His essence, not from the genus of letters and sounds, and it is one attribute, and it is command concerning what He has commanded and prohibition concerning what He has prohibited, and it is an eternal attribute. Then these expressions in Hebrew or Syriac are expressions of it, and it is conveyed by them, and these expressions are letters and sounds, and they are originated, created in their locus, indications, and they are of the speech which is an eternal attribute of God Most High. And Ja'far ibn Harb, Ja'far ibn Mubashshir, and al-Ka'bi from the Mu'tazila say according to our statement: indeed the speech of God is in the Preserved Tablet and the revealed expressions are indicative of it, except that they say: these expressions convey what is in the Preserved Tablet. And here is the disagreement between us and them: we say they convey what has subsisted in the essence of the attribute.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage explains the implications of the definition and the nature of divine speech. Nasafi asserts that God's speech is an attribute subsisting in His essence, not from the genus of letters and sounds. It is a single attribute, and it is an eternal attribute. The various expressions in Hebrew or Syriac are expressions of that one attribute, and they convey it. These expressions are letters and sounds, created in their locus, and they are indications of the eternal speech. Then he notes that some Mu'tazila – Ja'far ibn Harb, Ja'far ibn Mubashshir, and al-Ka'bi – agree with us that the expressions are indicative of God's speech, but they say these expressions indicate what is in the Preserved Tablet. The disagreement is that we say the expressions indicate the attribute subsisting in God's essence. This is a key difference: the Mu'tazila locate the speech in a created tablet, while we locate it as an attribute of God.

Key Terms
صفة
أزلية
كلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Believing that God's speech is composed of letters and sounds, like human speech.
Correction: God's speech is an eternal attribute; letters and sounds are created expressions that indicate that eternal speech.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is divine speech NOT?
A) An attribute of God
B) Eternal
C) Composed of letters and sounds
D) One attribute

Key Takeaway
God's speech is one eternal attribute, not created letters or sounds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you truly believe you are engaging with God's eternal attribute, not just a created book? How does that change your reverence and attention in recitation? Commit to one small change in your recitation habit today.
?
If God's speech is one eternal attribute encompassing all commands and prohibitions, does your treatment of the Quran's commands reflect equal urgency for all? Where do you selectively delay or ignore a command? What will you do about that this week?
?
The lesson states that divine speech is not letters or sounds. When you think of God's speech, are you tempted to imagine it as human speech? How can you guard your heart from such anthropomorphism? Write down one specific reminder you can use before reading the Quran.

Expressions Indicate Eternal Speech; Partial Agreement with Mu'tazila
Nasafi contrasts his view with Mu'tazila on what created expressions indicate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between created expressions and eternal speech, and the partial agreement and key difference with the Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
Created expressions convey eternal speech; Mu'tazila say they convey the Preserved Tablet, Maturidis say they convey God's attribute.

After defining eternal speech, Nasafi explains that the actual words we recite (Hebrew or Syriac) are created expressions used to convey that eternal speech. He then notes that some Mu'tazila agree that expressions convey something, but they differ on what they convey. Let's explore this nuanced discussion.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Read from 'ثم هذه العبارات' to the end. Note the two layers: the eternal speech and the created expressions that indicate it.
The Arabic word 'عبارات' means expressions, i.e., the actual words in Hebrew or Syriac.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila view
Ja'far ibn Harb, Ja'far ibn Mubashshir, and al-Ka'bi agree that expressions are indicative of something, but they say they indicate what is in the Preserved Tablet.
This is their partial agreement: they affirm created expressions point to something beyond themselves.
3
Find the disagreement
Nasafi states the disagreement: we (Maturidis) say the expressions convey the attribute subsisting in God's essence, while they say they convey the Preserved Tablet.
The Preserved Tablet is a created entity, so for them speech is ultimately created.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى هذا فإن كلام الله تعالى صفة قائمة بذاته، ليست من جنس الحروف، والأصوات، وهي صفة واحدة وهي أمر بما أمر به ونهي عما نهى عنه، وهي صفة أزلية. ثم هذه العبارات العبرية أو السريانية عبارات عنه، وهو يتأدى بها، وهذه العبارات حروف وأصوات وهي محدثة، مخلوقة في محلها، دلالات وهي على الكلام الذي هو صفة أزلية الله تعالى. وجعفر بن حرب وجعفر بن مبشر والكعبي من المعتزلة يقولون بقولنا: إن كلام الله في اللوح المحفوظ والمنزل عبارات دالة عليه، غير أنهم يقولون: إن هذه العبارات مؤدية ما فى اللوح المحفوظ، وهنا الخلاف بيننا وبينهم حيث نقول: هي مؤدية ما قام بالذات من الصفة.
And on this basis, indeed the speech of God Most High is an attribute subsisting in His essence, not from the genus of letters and sounds, and it is one attribute, and it is command concerning what He has commanded and prohibition concerning what He has prohibited, and it is an eternal attribute. Then these expressions in Hebrew or Syriac are expressions of it, and it is conveyed by them, and these expressions are letters and sounds, and they are originated, created in their locus, indications, and they are of the speech which is an eternal attribute of God Most High. And Ja'far ibn Harb, Ja'far ibn Mubashshir, and al-Ka'bi from the Mu'tazila say according to our statement: indeed the speech of God is in the Preserved Tablet and the revealed expressions are indicative of it, except that they say: these expressions convey what is in the Preserved Tablet. And here is the disagreement between us and them: we say they convey what has subsisted in the essence of the attribute.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage explains the implications of the definition and the nature of divine speech. Nasafi asserts that God's speech is an attribute subsisting in His essence, not from the genus of letters and sounds. It is a single attribute, and it is an eternal attribute. The various expressions in Hebrew or Syriac are expressions of that one attribute, and they convey it. These expressions are letters and sounds, created in their locus, and they are indications of the eternal speech. Then he notes that some Mu'tazila – Ja'far ibn Harb, Ja'far ibn Mubashshir, and al-Ka'bi – agree with us that the expressions are indicative of God's speech, but they say these expressions indicate what is in the Preserved Tablet. The disagreement is that we say the expressions indicate the attribute subsisting in God's essence. This is a key difference: the Mu'tazila locate the speech in a created tablet, while we locate it as an attribute of God.

محدثة

اللوح المحفوظ

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that the Mu'tazila and Maturidis hold identical views on divine speech.
Correction: Both agree expressions are created and indicative, but differ on what they indicate: Preserved Tablet (Mu'tazila) vs. eternal attribute (Maturidis).

?

?
If the letters and sounds of the Qur'an are created but indicate an eternal attribute, what does that imply about your own efforts to memorize and recite? Are you content with the created form, or do you seek the eternal reality behind it?
