Introduction to the Attribute of Takwin: Three Key Questions
Al-Nasafi introduces the discussion on takwin with three questions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three initial questions posed by al-Nasafi regarding the divine attribute of takwin (bringing into existence) and their significance for the theology of divine attributes.

Core Idea
God's attribute of takwin cannot be simply equated with the created things it produces.

Al-Nasafi opens his discussion on the divine attribute of takwin by posing three foundational questions. These questions probe whether takwin is identical with the things it brings into existence, whether it is eternal or created, and whether its eternality implies the eternality of creation. These puzzles get to the heart of how we understand God's creative power in relation to the temporal world.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice that al-Nasafi begins with a series of questions, not a definition. This signals that the topic is complex and requires careful inquiry.
The passage uses very concise language typical of kalam literature.
2
Identify the three questions
List the three questions al-Nasafi raises. They are: (1) Is takwin identical with mukawwan? (2) Is takwin eternal and uncreated? (3) Does the eternality of takwin require the eternality of created things?
These questions are numbered by the word 'هل' repeated.
3
Reflect on the theological stakes
Consider why these questions matter. They explore the relationship between God's eternal attribute and temporal creation. The answers will shape the Islamic understanding of God's creative power and its relation to the world.
This lesson sets the stage for the arguments that follow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في صفة التكوين: هو يبدأ النسفي في حديث طويل عن التكوين، وهل التكوين بمعنى المكون؟ وهل أزلي غير محدث؟ وهل يقتضي قدم التكوين قدم المكونات؟
The speech on the attribute of bringing into existence (takwin): He (al-Nasafi) begins a long discussion about takwin: Is takwin identical with the thing brought into existence (mukawwan)? Is it eternal, uncreated? Does the pre-eternality of takwin necessitate the pre-eternality of the things brought into existence?
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage introduces the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence). Nasafi begins a long discussion on whether takwin is identical with the thing brought into existence (mukawwan), whether it is eternal and uncreated, and whether the eternality of takwin necessitates the eternal existence of the things brought into existence. These are fundamental questions about God's creative attribute and its relationship to creation. The passage sets up the problem that will be addressed in the following discussion.

Key Terms
التكوين
المكون
أزلي
محدث
قدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the first question Nasafi asks about the attribute of takwin?
A) Is takwin eternal or created?
B) Is takwin identical with the thing brought into existence (mukawwan)?
C) Does takwin apply to all things equally?
D) Is takwin a separate entity from God?

Key Takeaway
The attribute of takwin raises critical questions about its relationship to created things, its eternality, and the implications for the temporal nature of creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on God's act of creation, do you ever unconsciously blur the line between the Creator and the creation? Which of the three questions in this passage exposes that confusion most in your own heart? Take a moment to repent if needed.
?
The third question asks whether God's eternal act of bringing into existence would make the universe eternal. If you truly believed creation is distinct from God's attribute of takwin, how would that change your sense of awe when you look at the sky or ponder your own existence? Will you today, for just one minute, meditate on the fact that God's act of creation is eternal while the world is not?
?
Al-Nasafi poses these questions not as academic puzzles but as gates to deeper tawhid. Which of these three questions feels most personally urgent to you right now? What would it cost you to live as though the answer matters for your daily reliance on Allah?

Takwīn: The Eternal Attribute of Creation
Nasafi defines takwīn and affirms it as an eternal attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of takwīn and its synonyms, and why Nasafi affirms it as an eternal attribute following his predecessors.

Core Idea
Takwīn is the eternal act of bringing things from non-existence to existence.

This lesson introduces the concept of takwīn (creation) as a distinct eternal attribute of Allah. Nasafi begins by asking whether takwīn is identical with the created thing, and whether its eternity implies the eternity of creation. He then defines takwīn and its synonyms, setting the stage for the sectarian debate that follows.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage defining takwīn
Read the Arabic text carefully. Notice the three initial questions Nasafi poses about takwīn, its meaning, and its eternity.
The passage uses several synonyms for creation; try to spot them all.
2
Identify the synonymous terms
List the terms: التكوين, التخليق, الخلق, الإيجاد, الإحداث, الاختراع. They all mean bringing the non-existent into existence.
3
Understand Nasafi's affirmation
Nasafi states that he affirms takwīn following the choice of his predecessors. This shows his adherence to the early Sunni position that creation is an eternal attribute.
This sets up the later sectarian discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في صفة التكوين: هو يبدأ النسفي في حديث طويل عن التكوين، وهل التكوين بمعنى المكون؟ وهل أزلي غير محدث؟ وهل يقتضي قدم التكوين قدم المكونات؟ يعرفنا أولا أن التكوين والتخليق والخلق والإيجاد والإحداث، والاختراع أسماء مترادفة، يراد بها كلها إخراج المعدوم من العدم إلى الوجود، ثم يبين أنه قال بالتكوين اقتداء باختيار سلفه. وثانيا: يقول : إن المعتزلة والنجارية يمنعون قيام أي صفة بذات القديم، فهم لا يقولون بالتكوين، ويقول عامتهم مثل قول القلانسي والكلابية، والأشاعرة: إن التكوين ليس بمعنى غير المكون، بل هو عين المكون. أما أبو الهذيل العلاف، وبشر بن المعتمر ، ومعمر، وابن الراوندي، والكرامية فيقولون : إن التكوين معنى وراء المكون ، غير أنهم يقولون هو غير المكون ويقول بشر، وابن الراوندي: إن التكوين حدث لا في محل. ثم يعرض كلام أهل الحق فيقول : إن التكوين صفة أزلية قائمة بذات الله تعالى كصفة العلم، والقدرة، والسمع، فعلى هذا يكون التكوين أزليا، والمكون حادثا كالقدرة أزلية، والمقدور حادثا ، وكذا بقية الصفات.
The discussion on the attribute of takwīn (bringing into existence): He begins a long discussion about takwīn: Is takwīn synonymous with the created thing? Is it eternal and not originated? Does the eternity of takwīn necessitate the eternity of the created things? He informs us first that takwīn, takhlīq, khalq, ījād, iḥdāth, and ikhtirā' are synonymous terms, all intended to mean bringing the non-existent from non-existence into existence. Then he explains that he affirms takwīn following the choice of his predecessors. Second, he says: The Mu'tazila and Najjāriyya prevent the subsistence of any attribute in the Essence of the Eternal, so they do not affirm takwīn. And the majority of them say, like the statement of al-Qalānisī, al-Kullābiyya, and al-Ashā'ira: that takwīn is not a meaning other than the created thing; rather it is identical with the created thing. As for Abū al-Hudhayl al-ʿAllāf, Bishr ibn al-Muʿtamir, Maʿmar, Ibn al-Rāwandī, and the Karrāmiyya, they say: that takwīn is a meaning beyond the created thing, but they say it is other than the created thing. Bishr and Ibn al-Rāwandī say: that takwīn is an event not in a subject. Then he presents the statement of Ahl al-Haqq (the People of Truth), saying: that takwīn is an eternal attribute subsisting in the Essence of Allah Most High, like the attributes of knowledge, power, and hearing. Thus, takwīn is eternal, and the created thing is originated, just as power is eternal and the object of power is originated, and similarly the rest of the attributes.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage introduces the theological discussion on the attribute of takwīn (bringing into existence, creation). Nasafi begins by posing three key questions: Is takwīn identical with the created thing? Is it eternal and unoriginated? Does the eternity of takwīn imply the eternity of the created things? He then provides a definition: takwīn and its synonyms (takhlīq, khalq, ījād, iḥdāth, ikhtirā') all mean bringing the non-existent (ma'dūm) from non-existence into existence. Nasafi notes that he follows his predecessors in affirming takwīn as an attribute. Next, he reports the positions of various Islamic sects. The Mu'tazila and Najjāriyya deny that any attribute can subsist in the Essence of Allah, so they deny takwīn entirely. The majority of them, as well as al-Qalānisī (an early Ash'arī theologian), the Kullābiyya, and the Ashā'ira, hold that takwīn is not a distinct meaning apart from the created thing; rather it is identical with the created thing (ʿayn al-mukawwan). A second group (Abū al-Hudhayl, Bishr ibn al-Muʿtamir, Maʿmar, Ibn al-Rāwandī, and the Karrāmiyya) affirms that takwīn is a meaning (maʿnā) beyond the created thing, but they disagree on its nature; Bishr and Ibn al-Rāwandī go so far as to say it is an event (ḥadath) not subsisting in a subject (lā fī maḥall). Finally, Nasafi presents the position of Ahl al-Haqq (the Maturidi and orthodox Sunni position): takwīn is an eternal attribute (ṣifah azaliyyah) subsisting in the Essence of Allah, just like knowledge, power, and hearing. On this view, takwīn itself is eternal, while the mukawwan (the created thing) is originated (ḥādith). He draws an analogy: power (qudrah) is eternal, while its object (maqdūr) is originated; similarly for other attributes. This establishes the orthodox distinction between the eternal attribute of creation and the temporal created objects.

Key Terms
التكوين
التخليق
الخلق
الإيجاد
الإحداث
الاختراع
المكون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What do the terms takwīn, takhlīq, khalq, ījād, iḥdāth, and ikhtirā' all mean according to Nasafi?
A) They refer to the created things themselves
B) They are synonymous and mean bringing the non-existent into existence
C) They refer to different types of creation
D) They are names for Allah's power

Key Takeaway
Takwīn is an eternal attribute meaning the act of bringing into existence, and Nasafi affirms it following the early scholars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's attribute of takwīn is eternal, meaning He has always been the Creator, then your very existence right now is a direct result of that eternal act. How does this truth make you feel about your relationship with Allah? What should change in how you live today?
?
The passage lists six synonyms for takwīn, all meaning 'bringing into existence'. Reflect on the fact that every single thing that exists—including you, your breath, your heartbeat—is constantly brought into being by Allah. Does your daily life reflect this reality? What specific action can you take today to acknowledge that you depend on Allah for your existence?
?
Nasafi follows his predecessors in affirming takwīn as an eternal attribute. This implies that there was never a time when Allah was not the Creator. How does this understanding affect your conception of Allah's power and your own neediness? Write down one concrete resolution to live more consciously of Allah's creative power.

Divine Attributes

Sectarian Views on Takwīn
Nasafi reports and critiques sectarian views on takwīn, concluding with the Maturidi position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various Islamic theological positions on the attribute of takwīn and how the Maturidi view resolves the debate.

Core Idea
The Maturidi view holds takwīn eternal while creation is temporal.

Having defined takwīn, Nasafi now reports the views of different sects. Some deny it entirely, some identify it with the created thing, and some say it is a distinct but created event. The Maturidi position is that takwīn is an eternal attribute of Allah, like knowledge and power, while its objects are temporal.

Guided Path
1
Read the sectarian positions
Read the Arabic text listing the views of different groups. Notice the three main camps: those who deny takwīn, those who identify it with the created thing, and those who say it is a distinct meaning (either created or eternal).
Identify each group mentioned: Mu'tazila, Najjāriyya, al-Qalānisī, Kullābiyya, Ashā'ira, Abū al-Hudhayl, Bishr, Ma'mar, Ibn al-Rāwandī, Karrāmiyya, and Ahl al-Haqq.
2
Analyze the first two positions
The Mu'tazila and Najjāriyya deny any attribute subsisting in Allah's Essence, so they deny takwīn. The majority (including al-Qalānisī, Kullābiyya, Ashā'ira) say takwīn is identical with the created thing (ʿayn al-mukawwan).
3
Examine the third position
Abū al-Hudhayl, Bishr, Ma'mar, Ibn al-Rāwandī, and Karrāmiyya say takwīn is a meaning (maʿnā) beyond the created thing. Bishr and Ibn al-Rāwandī go further, claiming it is an event (ḥadath) not subsisting in a subject.
This group affirms takwīn as real but not eternal.
4
Understand the Maturidi position
Ahl al-Haqq (Maturidis and orthodox Sunnis) hold that takwīn is an eternal attribute (ṣifah azaliyyah) subsisting in Allah's Essence, like knowledge and power. Thus, takwīn itself is eternal, but the created things (mukawwan) are temporal.
Nasafi uses an analogy: power is eternal, but its object (maqdūr) is originated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في صفة التكوين: هو يبدأ النسفي في حديث طويل عن التكوين، وهل التكوين بمعنى المكون؟ وهل أزلي غير محدث؟ وهل يقتضي قدم التكوين قدم المكونات؟ يعرفنا أولا أن التكوين والتخليق والخلق والإيجاد والإحداث، والاختراع أسماء مترادفة، يراد بها كلها إخراج المعدوم من العدم إلى الوجود، ثم يبين أنه قال بالتكوين اقتداء باختيار سلفه. وثانيا: يقول : إن المعتزلة والنجارية يمنعون قيام أي صفة بذات القديم، فهم لا يقولون بالتكوين، ويقول عامتهم مثل قول القلانسي والكلابية، والأشاعرة: إن التكوين ليس بمعنى غير المكون، بل هو عين المكون. أما أبو الهذيل العلاف، وبشر بن المعتمر ، ومعمر، وابن الراوندي، والكرامية فيقولون : إن التكوين معنى وراء المكون ، غير أنهم يقولون هو غير المكون ويقول بشر، وابن الراوندي: إن التكوين حدث لا في محل. ثم يعرض كلام أهل الحق فيقول : إن التكوين صفة أزلية قائمة بذات الله تعالى كصفة العلم، والقدرة، والسمع، فعلى هذا يكون التكوين أزليا، والمكون حادثا كالقدرة أزلية، والمقدور حادثا ، وكذا بقية الصفات.

Finally, Nasafi presents the position of Ahl al-Haqq (the Maturidi and orthodox Sunni position): takwīn is an eternal attribute (ṣifah azaliyyah) subsisting in the Essence of Allah, just like knowledge, power, and hearing. On this view, takwīn itself is eternal, while the mukawwan (the created thing) is originated (ḥādith). He draws an analogy: power (qudrah) is eternal, while its object (maqdūr) is originated; similarly for other attributes. This establishes the orthodox distinction between the eternal attribute of creation and the temporal created objects.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the Maturidi view of takwīn as an eternal attribute implies that the world (created things) is also eternal.
Correction: Nasafi clarifies that takwīn itself is eternal, but the mukawwan (created things) are originated (ḥādith). The analogy with power (eternal) and its object (originated) shows this distinction.

Checkpoint
According to Ahl al-Haqq (Maturidi view), what is the relationship between takwīn and the created things (mukawwan)?
A) Takwīn is identical with the created things
B) Takwīn is a created event not in a subject
C) Takwīn is an eternal attribute, while the created things are originated
D) Takwīn does not exist; only the created things exist

Key Takeaway
For Ahl al-Haqq, takwīn is an eternal attribute of Allah, distinguishing the creator from creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's attribute of takwīn is eternal and constantly causing existence, do you truly feel that you are being created at every moment? How does that change the way you view your next breath?
?
The Muʿtazila denied takwīn as an attribute for fear of multiplicity in God. Have you ever avoided affirming a truth about Allah because it seemed too complex or intellectually uncomfortable? How can you submit to revelation even when it challenges your reasoning?
?
The Māturīdīs say takwīn is eternal while its objects are temporal. How does this affect your understanding of your own dependence on Allah? Are you living as if you are sustained by an eternal act, or do you sometimes feel self-sufficient?

Was Allah Creator in Eternity? The Maturidi Answer
Nasafi presents answers to whether Allah was Creator in eternity, with Maturidi view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Maturidis affirm that Allah was 'Creator' (Khāliq) in eternity, based on the eternal attribute of takwīn.

Core Idea
Allah was eternally Creator because His attribute of creation is essential.

The question of whether Allah could be called 'Creator' before any creation existed puzzled early theologians. Nasafi presents the answers of various schools, culminating in the Maturidi position that the attribute of creation (takwīn) is eternal and subsisting in Allah's essence, just like knowledge and power.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice how Nasafi structures the question and answers.
The passage begins with a direct question and then gives responses from different groups.
2
Identify the four answers
List the four groups mentioned: those who say takwīn is originated, Abu al-Hudhayl, the Karrāmiyya, and the Māturīdiyya.
Each group offers a different view on whether Allah was Creator in eternity.
3
Focus on the Maturidi answer
Read the Maturidi answer again: they say Allah was Creator because the attribute of creation (takwīn) subsists in His essence eternally, just like knowledge and power.
This is the key point: takwīn is an eternal, essential attribute.
4
Reflect on the significance
Think about why this matters: it affirms that Allah's attributes are eternal and not dependent on creation.
This distinguishes Maturidis from other groups who deny eternal attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسأل: هل كان الله في الأزل خالقا، رازقا؟ ويجيب بأن القائلين بحدوث التكوين يقولون : لم يكن في الأزل خالقا حتى حدث المخلوق، وأما أبو الهزيل فقد قال : إنه كان خالقا بمعنى أنه سيخلق، والكرامية: يقولون: كان في الأزل خالقا بالخالقية، ويفسرون الخالقية بالقدرة على التخليق. أما الماتريدية فإنهم يقولون: هو كان خالقا لقيام صفة الخلق وهي التكوين بذاته في الأزل كما كان عالما، قادرا إلخ. ويعرض بعد ذلك لمن يقول بصفات الذات وصفات الفعل، وأن صفات الذات أزلية ، وصفات الفعل محدثة، ويبين الحد الفاصل بين صفات الذات، وصفات الفعل من وجهة نظرهم فيقول : إن المعتزلة قالت : الفرق أن ما يثبت الله، ولا يجوز [؟].
And he asks: Was Allah in eternity Creator, Provider? And he answers: that those who say takwīn is originated say: He was not in eternity Creator until the created thing occurred. As for Abū al-Hudhayl, he said: He was Creator in the sense that He will create. The Karrāmiyya say: He was in eternity Creator by khāliqiyyah (creatorship), and they interpret khāliqiyyah as the power to create. As for the Māturīdiyya, they say: He was Creator because of the subsistence of the attribute of creation, which is takwīn, in His Essence in eternity, just as He was Knower, Powerful, etc. Then he presents [the position] of those who speak of attributes of essence (ṣifāt al-dhāt) and attributes of action (ṣifāt al-fiʿl), and that attributes of essence are eternal, and attributes of action are temporal. And he explains the boundary between attributes of essence and attributes of action from their perspective, saying: The Muʿtazila said: The difference is that what Allah establishes [?] and it is not allowed [?].
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific question: Was Allah described as 'Creator' (Khāliq) and 'Provider' (Rāziq) in eternity, before any creation existed? Nasafi presents the answers of different groups. Those who hold that takwīn is originated (ḥādith) say Allah was not Khāliq in eternity; He only became Creator when the created thing occurred. Abū al-Hudhayl (a prominent Mu'tazilī) said He was Khāliq in the sense of 'He will create' (i.e., future meaning). The Karrāmiyya say He was Khāliq in eternity by virtue of 'khāliqiyyah' (creatorship), which they interpret as the power (qudrah) to create. In contrast, the Māturīdiyya affirm that He was Khāliq in eternity because the attribute of creation (ṣifat al-khalq), which is takwīn, subsists in His Essence eternally, just as He is eternally Knower ('ālim) and Powerful (qādir). This is consistent with the Maturidi doctrine that takwīn is an eternal attribute. Then Nasafi turns to the broader classification of divine attributes into ṣifāt al-dhāt (attributes of essence) and ṣifāt al-fiʿl (attributes of action). He notes that attributes of essence are eternal, while attributes of action are temporal. He then mentions that the Mu'tazila distinguished between them by saying 'the difference is that what Allah establishes...' but the text is cut off. The intended meaning likely relates to whether an attribute is necessarily entailed by the essence or depends on creation. This passage shows the Maturidi insistence that descriptive predicates like 'Creator' apply to Allah eternally because the attribute of creation is essential and not dependent on the existence of created things.

Key Terms
خالق
رازق
التكوين
الخالقية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that calling Allah 'Creator' in eternity implies the world is eternal.
Correction: The Maturidis clarify that it refers to the eternal attribute of power to create, not actual creation of a pre-existent world.

Checkpoint
According to the Maturidi view, why is Allah called 'Creator' (Khāliq) in eternity?
A) Because the world is eternal
B) Because He created something in eternity
C) Because the attribute of creation (takwīn) subsists eternally in His Essence
D) Because He will create in the future

Key Takeaway
The Maturidis affirm that Allah was eternally Creator because the attribute of takwīn is an eternal essential attribute subsisting in His essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's attribute of creation is eternal and independent of any created thing, what does that mean for your feeling of security in His provision? Do you truly believe He has always been the Provider, even for what hasn't happened yet? How would your daily worries change if you lived by that truth?
?
When you ask Allah for something, do you assume He has just then decided to be the Creator of that thing, or do you recognize that His attribute of creation was always ready to bring it into existence? Pause and reflect: does your prayer life reflect a belief in an eternal, unchanging Creator, or one whose attributes change with His acts?
?
The lesson shows that some groups denied Allah was eternally Creator because they confused the eternal attribute with the temporal act. Have you ever subconsciously thought of Allah's attributes as temporary, based on immediate circumstances? What steps can you take today to affirm that Allah's Creatorhood is eternal—not just a description but a reality that should reshape your expectations of His power?

Attributes of Essence vs. Attributes of Action
Nasafi explains the distinction between ṣifāt al-dhāt and ṣifāt al-fi'l.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between attributes of essence (ṣifāt al-dhāt) and attributes of action (ṣifāt al-fi'l) according to Nasafi and the Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
Attributes of essence are eternal; attributes of action are temporal.

After resolving the status of 'Creator' as an eternal attribute, Nasafi turns to a broader classification: attributes of essence vs. attributes of action. He states that attributes of essence are eternal, attributes of action are temporal, and then mentions the Mu'tazila's attempt to define the boundary, though the text is cut off.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Note that the passage introduces two categories and then mentions a definition from the Mu'tazila.
The last sentence is incomplete in the source.
2
Distinguish the two categories
Identify: attributes of essence (ṣifāt al-dhāt) are eternal; attributes of action (ṣifāt al-fi'l) are temporal.
Example: knowledge is eternal; creating is temporal.
3
Understand the Mu'tazila's boundary
Nasafi says the Mu'tazila defined the boundary, but the text is cut off. Try to infer what they might have said based on context.
The phrase 'the difference is that what Allah establishes [?] and it is not allowed [?]' suggests a criterion for whether something is an essential or action attribute.
4
Reflect on the significance
Think about why this classification matters: it helps define which attributes are permanent and which are contingent on creation.
This is central to debates about divine simplicity and the relationship between God and creation.

Takwin as an Eternal Attribute
The author states the Maturidi view on takwin and distinguishes it from its effect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi position that takwin (God's act of bringing into existence) is an eternal attribute distinct from its temporal effect.

Core Idea
The attribute is eternal; its effect is temporal.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi's Tabsirat al-Adilla presents the Maturidi school's view on the divine attribute of takwin (bringing into existence). The author states clearly that takwin is an eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence, just like knowledge, power, and hearing. The key distinction is that the attribute itself is uncreated and eternal, while the thing produced (al-mukawwan) is contingently originated (hadith). This is a central point in Maturidi theology, defending the eternity of God's creative attribute without implying the eternity of the world.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
Read the first part of the passage to identify what the Maturidis affirm about takwin. Notice the comparison to other attributes like knowledge and power.
The phrase 'qawl ahl al-haqq' indicates this is the orthodox position.
2
Understand the analogy
Examine the analogy with qudra (power). Just as qudra is eternal but its object (maqdur) is created, takwin is eternal but its object (mukawwan) is created.
This analogy helps clarify how an eternal attribute can have temporal effects.
3
Distinguish attribute from effect
Focus on the distinction between the eternal attribute and the contingent effect. This is the core of the Maturidi argument.
The common misunderstanding is that if takwin is eternal, then the world must be eternal. The passage corrects this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يعرض كلام أهل الحق فيقول : إن التكوين صفة أزلية قائمة بذات الله تعالى كصفة العلم، والقدرة، والسمع، فعلى هذا يكون التكوين أزليا، والمكون حادثا كالقدرة أزلية، والمقدور حادثا ، وكذا بقية الصفات.
Then he presents the statement of Ahl al-Ḥaqq (the People of Truth), saying: Indeed takwīn is an eternal attribute subsisting in the essence of God Most High, like the attributes of knowledge, power, and hearing. Accordingly, takwīn is eternal, and the mukawwan (the thing brought into existence) is contingently originated (ḥādith), just as power is eternal and the empowered (maqdūr) is contingently originated, and likewise the rest of the attributes.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage states the Maturidi doctrinal position, referred to here as qawl ahl al-ḥaqq (the statement of the People of Truth). The author affirms that takwīn is an eternal attribute (ṣifa azaliyya) that subsists in God’s essence (qā’ima bi-dhāt Allāh), analogous to the attributes of knowledge, power, and hearing. From this it follows that takwīn itself is eternal and uncreated, while the thing produced (al-mukawwan) is contingently originated (ḥādith). The author draws a parallel with power (qudra): power is eternal, but what is empowered (al-maqdūr) is originated. The same relationship holds for all other attributes: the attribute is eternal, its object is temporal. This is the core Maturidi argument for distinguishing the attribute of creation (takwīn) from the created world.

Key Terms
أهل الحق
صفة أزلية
قائمة بذات الله
التكوين أزلي
المكون حادث
القدرة أزلية
المقدور حادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If takwin is eternal, then the world must also be eternal.
Correction: The passage clarifies that while takwin (the attribute) is eternal, the mukawwan (the thing brought into existence) is temporal (hadith). The attribute's eternity does not imply the eternity of its effect.

Checkpoint
According to the Maturidi view, how is takwin related to the mukawwan?
A) Both are eternal
B) Both are contingent
C) Takwin is eternal, the mukawwan is contingent
D) Takwin is contingent, the mukawwan is eternal

Key Takeaway
Takwin is an eternal attribute of God, while its effect (the created thing) is temporal—distinguishing the divine act from its product.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that God's attribute of takwin is eternal, always present, not something that started when the universe began. Does this change how you view your own existence? If God's power to create is eternal and ever-present, then you are constantly sustained by that attribute every moment. How should this awareness affect your sense of dependence on Him throughout your day? Will you pause today to acknowledge that you owe your very existence to this eternal attribute?
?
The passage compares takwin to knowledge and power: the attribute is eternal, its effect temporal. Think about your own life—do you often focus only on the temporal effects (what you can see, achieve, own) while ignoring the eternal attribute of God that makes them possible? What would it look like to shift your attention from the created things to the Creator who eternally brings them about? Name one specific situation today where you can remind yourself that the true reality is God's eternal attribute, not the temporary object.

God's Eternal Creatorship: The Maturidi View
Nasafi presents four theological positions on God being Creator in eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi argument that God was truly Creator in eternity, and how it differs from other theological schools.

Core Idea
For the Maturidis, God’s attribute of creation (takwin) is eternal, even if creatures appear in time.

This passage addresses a key theological question: Was God Creator in pre-eternity? Different schools offered varying answers. Imam al-Nasafi presents the Maturidi view, which affirms that God’s attribute of creation is eternal, just like His knowledge and power. Let's read the passage to see how this is argued.

Guided Path
1
Identify the question and responses
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice that the author first states the question, then lists four distinct answers from different theological groups.
The question is about God being Creator (Khāliq) and Provider (Rāziq) in pre-eternity.
2
Focus on the Maturidi answer
Pay close attention to the Maturidi position: 'He was Creator because the attribute of creation (khalq) – which is takwīn – subsists in His essence in eternity.' Understand what this means.
The Maturidis compare this to God being eternally Knower and Powerful, even when no known or powerful object exists.
3
Contrast with other views
Compare the Maturidi answer with the other three: those who deny, Abū al-Hudhayl's future-oriented view, and the Karrāmiyya's power-based interpretation. Ask yourself why the Maturidis reject these alternatives.
The key difference is whether God’s creatorship depends on the existence of creatures or not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسأل: هل كان الله في الأزل خالقا، رازقا؟ ويجيب بأن القائلين بحدوث التكوين يقولون : لم يكن في الأزل خالقا حتى حدث المخلوق، وأما أبو الهزيل فقد قال : إنه كان خالقا بمعنى أنه سيخلق، والكرامية: يقولون: كان في الأزل خالقا بالخالقية، ويفسرون الخالقية بالقدرة على التخليق. أما الماتريدية فإنهم يقولون: هو كان خالقا لقيام صفة الخلق وهي التكوين بذاته في الأزل كما كان عالما، قادرا إلخ.
And he asks: Was God in eternity Creator (Khāliq) and Provider (Rāziq)? And he answers: Indeed those who affirm the contingency of takwīn say: He was not in eternity Creator until the creature came to be. As for Abū al-Hudhayl, he said: He was Creator in the sense that He will create. The Karrāmiyya say: He was in eternity Creator by creatorship (al-khāliqiyya), and they interpret al-khāliqiyya as the power to create. As for the Māturīdiyya, they say: He was Creator because the attribute of creation (khalq) – which is takwīn – subsists in His essence in eternity, just as He was Knower, Powerful, etc.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is a theological question-and-answer. The question is whether God was Creator and Provider in pre-eternity (al-azal). The author then records the answers of different factions. Those who maintain that takwīn is contingent (i.e., created in time) say that God was not Creator until the creature actually came into existence. Abū al-Hudhayl al-‘Allāf conceded that God was Creator in eternity but only in the sense that He would create in the future. The Karrāmiyya affirm that God was Creator in eternity by virtue of ‘creatorship’ (al-khāliqiyya), which they interpret as the power (qudra) to create. The Māturīdiyya hold that God was truly Creator in eternity because the attribute of khalq, which is identical to takwīn, subsists in God’s essence from eternity; this is analogous to His attributes of knowledge and power. Thus for the Maturidis, God’s being Creator does not depend on the existence of any creature, just as His being Knower does not depend on the existence of any known object.

Key Terms
خالقا في الأزل (Khāliqan fī al-azal)
رازقا (Rāziqan)
الخالقية (al-khāliqiyya)
القدرة على التخليق (al-qudra ‘alā al-takhlīq)
صفة الخلق (ṣifat al-khalq)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God was Creator in eternity, then the world must be eternal.
Correction: The Maturidis distinguish between the eternal attribute and its temporal effect. The attribute of creation is eternal, but the created world is temporal.

Checkpoint
How do the Maturidis answer the question 'Was God Creator in eternity?'
A) No, He became Creator only when He created
B) Yes, in the sense that He will create
C) Yes, because the attribute of creation (takwin) subsists in His essence eternally
D) Yes, but only by creatorship which is power to create

Key Takeaway
The Maturidis affirm that God is eternally Creator because the attribute of creation is eternal and inseparable from His essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God’s attribute of creation is eternal and untouched by time, does your daily reliance on Him for provision reflect that He is always Creator, not just when you feel needy? What would change if you lived with that constant awareness?
?
The Maturidis affirm that God is eternally Creator even before anything existed. Does your heart find rest in knowing that God’s power to create is not dependent on the world? How might this truth transform your trust in His ability to bring good out of nothing in your own life?
?
Consider the difference between the Karrāmiyya view (power to create) and the Maturidi view (eternal attribute). If God’s creatorship were merely potential power, would your worship be less certain of His actual care for you? How does affirming the eternal attribute of creation deepen your gratitude for each moment of existence?

8 min
Distinguishing Attributes of Essence and Action
Author compares two criteria for ṣifāt al-dhāt and ṣifāt al-fi‘l, then states Maturidi view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazili and Ahl al-Hadith criteria for distinguishing attributes of essence from attributes of action, and why the Maturidi school rejects both criteria in favor of the eternal nature of all attributes.

Core Idea
All divine attributes are eternal; the distinction between essence and action does not imply temporal origination.

This passage presents two competing criteria for categorizing divine attributes as either attributes of essence (ṣifāt al-dhāt) or attributes of action (ṣifāt al-fi‘l). The Mu'tazila focus on affirmability and permissibility of denial, while Ahl al-Ḥadīth focus on whether denial entails deficiency. After presenting both, the author explicitly states that he is bound by neither, affirming the Maturidi position that all attributes are eternal. Understanding these distinctions reveals a key difference between theological schools.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Pay attention to the two criteria presented and the author's own stance.
Notice the contrast between the Mu'tazili and Ahl al-Hadith criteria.
2
Identify the Mu'tazili criterion
The Mu'tazila distinguish based on whether it is permissible to deny the attribute of God. If denial is never permissible, it is an attribute of essence; if denial is sometimes permissible (e.g., not creating for a specific person), it is an attribute of action.
They give examples: knowledge and power vs. creation and provision.
3
Identify the Ahl al-Hadith criterion
Ahl al-Ḥadīth distinguish based on whether denial entails a deficiency. If denying the attribute implies a lack (e.g., denying life or power), it is an attribute of essence; if not, it is an attribute of action.
Examples: life and power vs. giving life and causing death.
4
Recognize the author's rejection
The author says neither criterion binds him because he follows the Maturidi school in affirming the pre-eternity (qidam) of all attributes.
This means the distinction between essence and action is not about eternality vs. contingency.
5
Understand the Maturidi position
The author says what binds him is proving that takwīn (bringing into existence) is an eternal attribute subsisting in God, distinct from the created thing.
This highlights that for Maturidis, even attributes of action are eternal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويعرض بعد ذلك لمن يقول بصفات الذات وصفات الفعل، وأن صفات الذات أزلية ، وصفات الفعل محدثة، ويبين الحد الفاصل بين صفات الذات، وصفات الفعل من وجهة نظرهم فيقول : إن المعتزلة قالت : الفرق أن ما يثبت الله، ولا يجوز نفيه عنه فهو من صفات الذات كالعلم، والقدرة مثلا، أما الخلق والرزق مثلا فهما من صفات الفعل، يقال: يخلق لفلان، ولا يخلق لفلان، ويرزق فلانا، ولا يرزق فلانا فيجوز النفي في الثانية فهي صفة فعل. أما متكلمو أهل الحديث فقد قالوا في الفرق وما يلزم بنفيه نقص فهو من صفات الذات مثل الحياة والقدرة، وما لا يلزم بنفيه نقص فهو من صفات الفعل كالإحياء والإماتة، والتسكين والتحريك. وبعد ذلك يبين أن كلام الفريقين لا يلزمه، لأنه يقول مثل بقية الماتريدية بقدم الصفات كلها، والذي يلزمه بيان إقامة الأدلة على أن التكوين صفة ثابتة له في الأزل، وأنها معنى وراء المكون.
And after that he presents those who speak of attributes of essence (ṣifāt al-dhāt) and attributes of action (ṣifāt al-fi‘l), and that attributes of essence are eternal and attributes of action are contingent. And he clarifies the distinguishing boundary between attributes of essence and attributes of action from their perspective, saying: Indeed the Mu‘tazila said the difference is that whatever is affirmed of God and whose denial is not permissible concerning Him is among attributes of essence, like knowledge and power for example. As for creation and provision for example, they are among attributes of action; one says: He creates for so-and-so and He does not create for so-and-so, and He provides for so-and-so and He does not provide for so-and-so. So denial is permissible in the second [category]; thus it is an attribute of action. As for the theologians of Ahl al-Ḥadīth, they said regarding the difference: whatever denial entails deficiency is among attributes of essence, such as life and power; and whatever denial does not entail deficiency is among attributes of action, such as giving life and causing death, and giving stillness and movement. And after that he clarifies that the statement of the two groups does not bind him, because he says, like the rest of the Māturīdiyya, the pre-eternity (qidam) of all attributes. And what binds him is to present the establishment of proofs that takwīn is an attribute subsisting for Him in eternity, and that it is a meaning beyond the mukawwan.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is a comparative presentation of two criteria for distinguishing between attributes of essence (ṣifāt al-dhāt) and attributes of action (ṣifāt al-fi‘l), followed by the author’s own Maturidi position. First, the Mu‘tazila: an attribute is of essence if it is always affirmed of God and cannot be denied; if denial is permissible (like saying God does not create for a particular person), it is an attribute of action. Second, the theologians of Ahl al-Ḥadīth: an attribute is of essence if denying it entails a deficiency (such as denying life or power); if not (e.g., denying that He gives life to a specific person), it is an attribute of action. The author then states that he is not bound by either distinction because, like other Maturidis, he holds that all attributes are eternal (qidam al-ṣifāt kullihā). What he is obligated to do is provide proof that takwīn is indeed an eternal attribute subsisting in God and that it is a meaning distinct from the mukawwan (ma‘nā warā’ al-mukawwan). This clarifies that for Maturidis the essence/action distinction is not about eternality versus contingency, since all attributes are eternal; rather the distinction may relate to other considerations.

Key Terms
صفات الذات (ṣifāt al-dhāt)
صفات الفعل (ṣifāt al-fi‘l)
أزلية (azaliyya)
محدثة (muḥdatha)
قدم الصفات (qidam al-ṣifāt)
المعتزلة (al-Mu‘tazila)
أهل الحديث (Ahl al-Ḥadīth)
نقص (nuqṣ)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that Maturidis accept the Mu'tazili or Ahl al-Hadith criteria for distinguishing attributes.
Correction: The author explicitly says neither criterion binds him because all attributes are eternal.

Checkpoint
What is the author's position on the distinction between attributes of essence and action?
A) He accepts the Mu'tazili criterion
B) He accepts the Ahl al-Hadith criterion
C) He says neither binds him; all attributes are eternal
D) He says all attributes are contingent

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi school holds that all divine attributes are eternal; the distinction between attributes of essence and action does not imply that some attributes are contingent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Mu‘tazila and Ahl al-Ḥadīth both had criteria for distinguishing attributes, but the author says he is not bound by them because all attributes are eternal. Is your own understanding of God’s attributes shaped more by human reasoning or by the revealed texts? Which criterion do you unconsciously use when you think about God? Will you commit to examining your own criteria in light of the Maturidi principle of qidam al-ṣifāt?
?
The author says he must establish proof that takwīn is an eternal attribute. Do you have a settled belief about the eternity of God’s creative act, or have you ever doubted it? How does your view affect your reliance on God’s continuous creation? Write down one practical action you will take to strengthen your conviction about this.
?
If all attributes are eternal, then God’s mercy, anger, and will are also eternal. How does that affect how you approach God — are you ever hesitant because you think His attributes change? This week, find a moment to reflect on one eternal attribute and let it reshape your worship.

Second Objection: Eternal Takwin Implies Eternal Creation
Author presents the second objection: eternal takwin implies eternal creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of the second objection against the eternity of takwin and how the Maturidis begin to refute it using both reason and revelation.

Core Idea
An eternal attribute does not require its object to be co-eternal with it.

Opponents argue that if takwin (the act of bringing into existence) is an eternal attribute of God, then the created world must also be eternal. They compare it to a strike that cannot exist without something struck. This lesson explains that objection and introduces Imam al-Nasafi's response, which draws on rational and scriptural arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the passage once to get the overall flow. Notice the key terms takwin, mukawwin, mukawwan, and the analogy of strike and struck.
The Arabic phrase 'وجود الضرب ولا مضروب' may be a typo for 'بلا مضروب' (without a struck).
2
Identify the objection's logical structure
Break down the argument: premise (takwin is eternal), conclusion (mukawwan is eternal), justification (impossible to have a strike without a struck).
This is a conditional argument: if P then Q, and the justification supports the necessity.
3
Understand the analogy's flaw
Reflect on why the analogy might be faulty. Does an attribute always require a simultaneous effect? The Maturidis distinguish between essential attributes and their effects.
The refutation will be presented later in the text.
4
See the dual method of refutation
Notice that al-Nasafi begins to invalidate their argument using both reason ('aql) and transmitted texts (naql). This shows the comprehensive approach of Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الأمر الثاني : فيقولون: لو كان التكوين ثابتا في الأزل، وكان الله مكونا، خالقا للعالم لكان المكون موجودا، مخلوقا في الأزل، لما أن وجود الضرب ولا مضروب باطل، ويبدأ النسفي في مناقشتهم، ليبطل كلامهم بالعقل والنقل.
As for the second matter: They say: If takwīn were established in eternity, and God were a mukawwin (bringer into existence) and Creator of the world, then the mukawwan (the thing brought into existence) would exist, created in eternity – because the existence of a strike without a struck is invalid. And al-Nasafī begins his discussion with them to invalidate their argument by reason and transmission.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage presents the second objection that the opponents raise against the Maturidi doctrine. Their argument is: if takwīn (the act of bringing into existence) is an eternal attribute, and God is thus eternally a 'Mukawwin' (One who brings into existence) and Creator of the world, then the thing produced (al-mukawwan) – i.e., the world – would have to exist in eternity. They reason that just as the existence of a strike (ḍarb) without a struck object (maḍrūb) is impossible, so too cannot there be a Creator without a creation. Thus they conclude that eternal takwīn implies an eternal world, which is false. The author notes that al-Nasafī then begins to refute this objection using both rational arguments (al-‘aql) and transmitted texts (al-naql). This is only the introductory statement of the refutation; the full argument will follow.

Key Terms
مكون (mukawwin)
مكون موجود (mukawwan mawjūd)
وجود الضرب ولا مضروب (wujūd al-ḍarb wa-lā maḍrūb)
العقل (al-‘aql)
النقل (al-naql)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if God is eternally Creator, then the creation must also be eternal.
Correction: The Maturidis argue that an attribute like takwin does not require its object to be co-eternal; God could be eternally capable of creating without having actually created from eternity.

Checkpoint
What is the second objection that the opponents raise against takwin?
A) Takwin is not mentioned in the Quran
B) If takwin is eternal, then the created world must also be eternal
C) Takwin is a concept invented by al-Zabir Sha'i
D) Takwin implies God needs a helper

Key Takeaway
The second objection is based on a faulty analogy; an eternal attribute does not necessitate an eternal object, as the Maturidis will argue using reason and revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about Allah's eternal attributes, do you ever assume that His actions must follow the same cause-and-effect logic as created things? If so, where does that leave your trust in His absolute freedom and wisdom? How can you actively submit your reasoning to revelation on this point?
?
Imagine someone argues that if Allah is eternally Creator, then the world must be eternal. Are you prepared to answer from what you have learned? Does your reaction reveal a reliance on worldly analogies or a deeper trust in Allah's unique nature? What will you do to strengthen your response?

Attributes of Essence vs. Action: The Test of Negation
Al-Nasafi defines the general criterion for attributive distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the criterion for distinguishing attributes of essence from attributes of action based on whether negation of the attribute implies deficiency.

Core Idea
If negating an attribute suggests imperfection, it belongs to God's essence.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi introduces a foundational distinction in Islamic theology: the difference between attributes that are essential to God and those that describe His actions. The key test is whether we can say God does not do something without implying a flaw. Let's examine the passage.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the examples provided.
2
Identify the two categories
The passage presents two types of attributes: those whose negation is not permissible (essence) and those whose negation is permissible (action). Find the defining sentence.
3
Apply the test to examples
Use the examples given (knowledge, power vs. creation, provision) to see how the test works. Reflect on why knowledge cannot be negated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نفيه عنه فهو من صفات الذات كالعلم، والقدرة مثلا، أما الخلق والرزق مثلا فهما من صفات الفعل، يقال: يخلق لفلان، ولا يخلق لفلان، ويرزق فلانا، ولا يرزق فلانا فيجوز النفي في الثانية فهي صفة فعل. أما متكلمو أهل الحديث فقد قالوا في الفرق وما يلزم بنفيه نقص فهو من صفات الذات مثل الحياة والقدرة، وما لا يلزم بنفيه نقص فهو من صفات الفعل كالإحياء والإماتة، والتسكين والتحريك. وبعد ذلك يبين أن كلام الفريقين لا يلزمه، لأنه يقول مثل بقية الماتريدية بقدم الصفات كلها، والذي يلزمه بيان إقامة الأدلة على أن التكوين صفة ثابتة له في الأزل، وأنها معنى وراء المكون.
Its negation from Him is from the attributes of essence like knowledge and power for example. As for creation and provision for example, they are from the attributes of action. It is said: He creates for so-and-so, and does not create for so-and-so, and He provides for so-and-so, and does not provide for so-and-so. So negation is permissible in the second [type]; thus it is an attribute of action. As for the mutakallimun of Ahl al-Hadith, they said concerning the distinction: whatever entails deficiency by its negation is from the attributes of essence like life and power, and whatever does not entail deficiency by its negation is from the attributes of action like giving life and causing death, and making still and moving. After that he explains that the speech of the two groups does not bind him, because he says like the rest of the Maturidis in the eternity of all attributes, and what binds him is the presentation of proofs that takwin (التكوين) is an established attribute of His in pre-eternity, and that it is a meaning beyond the mukawwan (المكون).
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage defines the criterion for distinguishing between attributes of essence (ṣifāt al-dhāt) and attributes of action (ṣifāt al-fiʿl). First, a general definition is given: if negation of the attribute is permissible (i.e., it can be said that He does not do it for some), it is an attribute of action; if negation is not permissible because it would imply deficiency, it is an attribute of essence. Examples are provided. Second, the mutakallimun of Ahl al-Hadith define the distinction more explicitly: if negating the attribute would imply a deficiency (naqṣ) in God, it is an attribute of essence; otherwise, it is an attribute of action. Then the author clarifies that neither definition binds him personally, because as a Maturidi he holds all attributes, including what some consider attributes of action, to be eternal. His task is to prove that takwin (the attribute of bringing into existence) is an eternal attribute distinct from the created thing (mukawwan).

Key Terms
صفات الذات
صفات الفعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what makes an attribute an attribute of action?
A) It is mentioned in the Quran as an action.
B) It can be negated of God without implying deficiency.
C) It is temporal and created.
D) It is not eternal.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of negation is the key to distinguishing between essential and active attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about Allah's attribute of 'creation', do you treat it as a distant, static fact, or do you realize that it is a dynamic action He chooses moment by moment? How does this affect your gratitude for your own existence?
?
Consider a time you felt Allah had not provided for you. Did that make you doubt His power or mercy? How does knowing that provision is an attribute of action—not essence—help you trust that His inability to provide is not a flaw, but a divine wisdom?
?
If you were to test every belief you have about Allah by this criterion—whether negating it would imply imperfection—which of your current understandings would fail the test? What step will you take today to correct a misconception about Allah's attributes?

The Maturidi Position: All Attributes Eternal
Al-Nasafi presents the Maturidi position on the eternity of attributes and the proof of takwin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi position that all divine attributes, including those of action, are eternal, and the proof that takwin is an eternal attribute distinct from the created.

Core Idea
For Maturidis, even 'action' attributes like creation are eternal in God.

After presenting the standard distinctions, Imam al-Nasafi clarifies his own Maturidi school position. He aligns with the view that all attributes, including those termed 'of action', are eternal. He then sets out the task: proving that takwin (the attribute of bringing into existence) is an eternal meaning distinct from its effect.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author first presents the Ahl al-Hadith definition, then distances himself from both definitions.
2
Understand the Maturidi stance
The author states that he, like other Maturidis, holds all attributes to be eternal. Reflect on what this means for attributes typically considered 'actions'.
3
Focus on takwin
The author identifies his task: to prove that takwin is an eternal attribute and that it is distinct from the mukawwan (the created thing). This is a key Maturidi doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نفيه عنه فهو من صفات الذات كالعلم، والقدرة مثلا، أما الخلق والرزق مثلا فهما من صفات الفعل، يقال: يخلق لفلان، ولا يخلق لفلان، ويرزق فلانا، ولا يرزق فلانا فيجوز النفي في الثانية فهي صفة فعل. أما متكلمو أهل الحديث فقد قالوا في الفرق وما يلزم بنفيه نقص فهو من صفات الذات مثل الحياة والقدرة، وما لا يلزم بنفيه نقص فهو من صفات الفعل كالإحياء والإماتة، والتسكين والتحريك. وبعد ذلك يبين أن كلام الفريقين لا يلزمه، لأنه يقول مثل بقية الماتريدية بقدم الصفات كلها، والذي يلزمه بيان إقامة الأدلة على أن التكوين صفة ثابتة له في الأزل، وأنها معنى وراء المكون.
Its negation from Him is from the attributes of essence like knowledge and power for example. As for creation and provision for example, they are from the attributes of action. It is said: He creates for so-and-so, and does not create for so-and-so, and He provides for so-and-so, and does not provide for so-and-so. So negation is permissible in the second [type]; thus it is an attribute of action. As for the mutakallimun of Ahl al-Hadith, they said concerning the distinction: whatever entails deficiency by its negation is from the attributes of essence like life and power, and whatever does not entail deficiency by its negation is from the attributes of action like giving life and causing death, and making still and moving. After that he explains that the speech of the two groups does not bind him, because he says like the rest of the Maturidis in the eternity of all attributes, and what binds him is the presentation of proofs that takwin (التكوين) is an established attribute of His in pre-eternity, and that it is a meaning beyond the mukawwan (المكون).

Commentary
This passage defines the criterion for distinguishing between attributes of essence (ṣifāt al-dhāt) and attributes of action (ṣifāt al-fiʿl). First, a general definition is given: if negation of the attribute is permissible (i.e., it can be said that He does not do it for some), it is an attribute of action; if negation is not permissible because it would imply deficiency, it is an attribute of essence. Then the author clarifies that neither definition binds him personally, because as a Maturidi he holds all attributes, including what some consider attributes of action, to be eternal. His task is to prove that takwin (the attribute of bringing into existence) is an eternal attribute distinct from the created thing (mukawwan).

المكون

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that attributes of action indicate change in God or that they are created in time.
Correction: Maturidis hold that all attributes, including those called 'of action', are eternal and not subject to temporal occurrence.

Checkpoint

A) The Ahl al-Hadith definition.
B) The general definition based on permissibility of negation.

Key Takeaway
Maturidis affirm the eternity of all attributes, including takwin, which is an eternal meaning beyond its temporal effects.

?

?
The Maturidis hold that takwin is an eternal attribute distinct from its effects. ?

Refuting the Innovation Claim Against Takwin
Al-Nasafi refutes the claim of takwin's novelty by citing ancient authorities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Nasafi refutes the claim that takwin is a later innovation by citing early Hanafi authorities.

Core Idea
Takwin is an ancient doctrine, not a later invention.

The opponents of the doctrine of takwin (the attribute of bringing into existence) claimed that only a single person, al-Zabir al-Shay'i, affirmed it, and that it was a late innovation. Al-Nasafi directly refutes this by quoting none other than Abu Hanifa and al-Tahawi, showing that takwin is firmly rooted in the earliest Hanafi theological tradition. This passage defends the orthodoxy of takwin by grounding it in the foundational texts of the school.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation to get the full picture.
Notice the concise style of argumentation.
2
Identify the opponent's claim
Find the first part where al-Nasafi summarizes the opponent's objection. What is being claimed about the origin of takwin?
The opponent says only one man, al-Zabir al-Shay'i, around the 5th century AH, affirmed takwin.
3
Examine the refutation and evidence
See how al-Nasafi denies the claim and then provides quotations from Abu Hanifa and al-Tahawi. Note the specific phrases that affirm takwin as an eternal attribute.
Abu Hanifa says 'Creator by His creating (takhliq)' and that 'takhliq is an attribute in pre-eternity'. Al-Tahawi uses the analogy of 'Reviver of the dead' before actual revival.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why al-Nasafi uses these early authorities. What does this tell us about the methodology of defending a theological doctrine?
This shows that takwin is not an innovation but part of the received tradition from the earliest imams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يعرض تشنيعات الخصوم وشبههم ويلخصها في أمرين: الأول: القول بالتكوين لم يقل به أحد سوى رجل بمرو يسمى الزابر شائي نشأ بحد الأربعمائة من الهجرة. ويكذب النسفى هذا القول قائلا إن أبا حنيفة وأبا يوسف ومحمد بن الحسن والطحاوي قالوا بالتكوين. فقد قال أبو حنيفة في الفقه الأكبر مع شرحه لعلي القاري ٢١، ٢٢ وخالق بتخليقه والتخليق صفة له في الأزل، وفاعلا بفعله، والفعل صفة له في الأزل. وقال بذلك الطحاوي أيضا في عقيدته السلفية مع شرحها ص ٦٧ ٦٨: وله معنى الربوبية ولا مربوب، ومعنى الخالق، ولا مخلوق، ويعني بالخالق المخرج للشيء من العدم إلى الوجود، ويقول: وكما أنه محيي الموتى بعدما أحيا استحق هذا الاسم قبل إحيائهم كذلك استحق اسم الخالق قبل إنشائهم.
Then he presents the condemnations and doubts of the opponents and summarizes them in two matters: The first: the statement of takwin (التكوين) was not said by anyone except a man in Marw called al-Zabir al-Shay'i, who arose around the year four hundred of the Hijra. And al-Nasafi denies this statement, saying that Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, and al-Tahawi said takwin. For Abu Hanifa said in al-Fiqh al-Akbar with its commentary by Ali al-Qari [21,22]: 'And Creator (khāliq) by His creating (takhliq), and takhliq is an attribute of His in pre-eternity, and Agent (fāʿil) by His act (fiʿl), and the act is an attribute of His in pre-eternity.' And al-Tahawi also said that in his Salafi creed with its commentary p. 67-68: 'And He has the meaning of Lordship (rubūbiyya) with no lordship, and the meaning of Creator (khāliq) with no created, and by 'Creator' He means the One who brings forth the thing from non-existence to existence.' And he says: 'And just as He is the Reviver of the dead after He gave life, deserving this name before their revival, similarly He deserves the name of Creator before their creation.'
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage presents the first of two objections raised by opponents: that the doctrine of takwin (the attribute of bringing into existence) was innovated by a single individual named al-Zabir al-Shay'i around the 5th century AH. Al-Nasafi directly refutes this by citing earlier authorities who explicitly affirmed takwin. He quotes Abu Hanifa from al-Fiqh al-Akbar, where he states that 'Creator' is by His creating (takhliq) and that takhliq is an eternal attribute, and similarly that 'Agent' is by His act, which is also eternal. He then quotes al-Tahawi from his creed, who affirms that God has the meaning of Creator even when no created things exist, analogizing it to His being Reviver before actual revival. Thus, takwin is an ancient doctrine, not an innovation.

التكوين
الزابر شائي
أبو حنيفة
الطحاوي
الفقه الأكبر
عقيدة الطحاوي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Takwin is a later theological invention introduced by a single obscure figure.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows that takwin is affirmed by the earliest Hanafi imams, including Abu Hanifa and al-Tahawi, making it a foundational doctrine.

The Objection of Eternal Takwin and the Four-Point Response
Al-Nasafi presents the Mu'tazilite objection and counters with a four-point agenda.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite objection that an eternal takwin would entail eternal creation, and how al-Nasafi structures his response around four distinct topics.

Core Idea
Eternal takwin does not force eternal creation — four key distinctions.

This passage introduces a critical objection from the Mu'tazila against the Maturidi position that takwin (the attribute of bringing into existence) is eternal. If takwin is eternal, they argue, then its effect (the world) must also be eternal. Al-Nasafi responds by outlining four separate topics that their discussion must cover. Understanding this roadmap will help you follow the detailed arguments that follow.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Understand the Mu'tazilite argument: if takwin is eternal, then its object (the world) must also be eternal, because an action requires an object — just as striking requires a struck.
This is a logical inference based on the concept of 'action needing an object'.
2
Identify the four topics
Al-Nasafi lists four points that his response will cover. Note each one: (1) refuting Mu'tazila on eternal attribute, (2) proving takwin is other than the created thing, (3) proving takwin is eternal, (4) showing that eternal takwin does not mean eternal created things.
3
Reflect on the strategy
Why does al-Nasafi separate these points? He is systematically addressing different aspects to dismantle the objection step by step.
This layered approach is typical of kalam argumentation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الأمر الثاني : فيقولون: لو كان التكوين ثابتا في الأزل، وكان الله مكونا، خالقا للعالم لكان المكون موجودا، مخلوقا في الأزل، لما أن وجود الضرب ولا مضروب باطل، ويبدأ النسفي في مناقشتهم، ليبطل كلامهم بالعقل والنقل. فيقول: إن حديثنا معهم يتناول مواضع أربعة: أولا: مع المعتزلة في جواز وجود صفة أزلية بذات الباري - وقد انتهى من ذلك في مبحث الصفات، وثانيا: بيان أن التكوين غير المكون، وثالثا: بيان أن التكوين أزلي، ورابعا: بيان أن القول بقدم التكوين لا يؤدي إلى القول بقدم المكونات.
As for the second matter: They say: If takwin (التكوين) were established in pre-eternity, and God was mukawwin (مكون, the bringer into existence), Creator of the world, then the mukawwan (المكون, the created thing) would exist, created in pre-eternity, because the existence of striking without a struck is impossible. And al-Nasafi begins to discuss them, to refute their statement by reason and transmission. He says: Our discussion with them encompasses four topics: First: with the Mu'tazila concerning the permissibility of an eternal attribute subsisting in the Essence of the Creator - and he has finished that in the chapter on attributes. Second: the demonstration that takwin is other than the mukawwan. Third: the demonstration that takwin is eternal. Fourth: the demonstration that the statement of the eternity of takwin does not lead to the statement of the eternity of the created things (mukawwanāt).
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage presents the second objection against the eternity of takwin: if takwin were eternal, then the created world (mukawwan) would also have to be eternal, just as striking requires a struck. The author then summarizes his response by listing four distinct topics that the discussion with the opponents covers. The first topic is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite position that an eternal attribute cannot subsist in God's essence, already handled earlier. The second is to prove that takwin is distinct from the mukawwan (the created thing). The third is to prove that takwin itself is eternal. The fourth is to show that holding takwin to be eternal does not force one to hold the created things (mukawwanāt) to be eternal. These four points form the structure of the subsequent detailed arguments.

المكون
المكونات
أزلي
قدم
المعتزلة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: An eternal attribute of creation would necessarily produce an eternal world.
Correction: Al-Nasafi argues that this conclusion does not follow, as takwin is other than the created things, and its eternity does not imply the eternity of its effects.

Key Takeaway
Al-Nasafi sets out a four-point plan to refute the Mu'tazilite objection that eternal takwin would entail an eternal world.

The Absurd Analogy: Action and Object
The author refutes identity using an analogy of action and object.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the absurd consequence of equating takwin with mukawwan using the analogy of an act and its object.

Core Idea
If takwin were mukawwan, striking would be the same as the struck.

The author begins his refutation by presenting a simple analogy from everyday actions. He points out that if the act of bringing into existence were identical with the thing brought into existence, then it would be like saying the act of striking is the same as the thing struck. Clearly, an act and its object are distinct, so the claim is false.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how the author states the claim and gives the analogy.
2
Understand the analogy
Reflect on the examples: striking and struck, breaking and broken, eating and eaten. Why are these clearly distinct?
The act is a verb, the object is a noun.
3
Connect to takwin
See how this analogy applies to takwin and mukawwan. If takwin were identical with mukawwan, then the divine act of creation would be the same as the creature, which is absurd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما عن رده على القول بأن التكوين هو عين المكون فيقول : إن هذا الكلام باطل، لأنه يؤدي إلى القول بأن الضرب عين المضروب والكسر عين المكسور، والأكل عين المأكول مع أن الضرب فعل والمضروب مفعول. وكذلك لو كان التكوين هو المكون، والمكون قد حصل بالتكوين، فيكون حصول المكون بنفسه لا بالله، وهذا يؤدي أن تكون الأشياء خالقة لنفسها، ويبطل وجود الصانع، ويكون كل شيء خلق ومخلوق في وقت واحد، والقول بهذا واضح التناقض. وكذلك لو كان التكوين هو المكون، فلا حاجة إلى الله تعالى، ولا تمييز بينه، وبين غيره إلا بالقدم.
As for his refutation of the statement that takwin (التكوين) is identical (ʿayn) with the mukawwan (المكون), he says: This speech is false, because it leads to the statement that striking is identical with the struck, and breaking is identical with the broken, and eating is identical with the eaten, despite that striking is an act and the struck is an object. And likewise, if takwin were the mukawwan, and the mukawwan has come to be by takwin, then the coming to be of the mukawwan would be by itself, not by Allah. This leads to things being creators of themselves, nullifies the existence of the Creator, and would make everything creator and created at the same time, and this statement is clearly contradictory. And likewise, if takwin were the mukawwan, then there would be no need for Allah Almighty, nor distinction between Him and other than Him except by pre-eternity (qidam).
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage refutes the claim that takwin (the attribute of bringing into existence) is identical with the mukawwan (the created thing). The author presents several absurd consequences. First, if takwin were identical with the mukawwan, it would be like saying striking is the same as the struck, breaking is the same as the broken, etc., but they are clearly distinct – the act is different from its object. Second, if takwin and mukawwan were identical, then the created thing would be caused by itself (since takwin brings it about, and it is the same as takwin), eliminating God's role. This would mean things create themselves, which is impossible. Third, it would nullify the need for God entirely, leaving only pre-eternity as a distinguishing feature, which is insufficient. Therefore, the claim is false.

Key Terms
التكوين
المكون
عين
الضرب والمضروب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Takwin is the same as the creature (mukawwan).
Correction: Takwin is an attribute of God, mukawwan is the created object; they are distinct as action and object.

Checkpoint
What analogy does the author use to show the absurdity of equating takwin with mukawwan?
A) Writing and the written
B) Striking and the struck
C) Seeing and the seen
D) Creating and the created

Key Takeaway
Equating takwin with mukawwan is like equating an act with its object, which is rationally absurd.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'Allahu akbar' (God is Greater), does your heart truly separate the Creator from His creation, or do you sometimes unintentionally blur the two? This lesson shows that confusing the act (takwin) with the object (mukawwan) is an absurdity. Examine your thoughts: in what subtle ways might you be attributing created qualities to Allah? Repent and renew your tawheed today.
?
Imagine someone says, 'I feel like God is in everything.' Based on this lesson, how would you gently correct them using the analogy of action and object? More importantly, do you ever feel a similar confusion in your own spirituality? Commit to distinguishing between Allah's presence (as His knowledge and power) and His actual essence or acts, which are distinct from His creation.
?
This passage uses everyday examples (striking, breaking, eating) to show that an action is never the same as its object. In your daily worship, do you sometimes treat the act of worship (e.g., prayer, charity) as if it were the same as the reward or the object of worship? How can you apply this distinction to make your worship more sincere and directed solely to Allah?

Theological Absurdities of Identity
The author draws two theological absurdities: self-creation and elimination of the Creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how equating takwin with mukawwan leads to self-creation and the denial of God's role as Creator.

Core Idea
If takwin is mukawwan, then things create themselves.

The author now draws two deeper theological consequences from the identity claim. First, if takwin and mukawwan are identical, then the creature's existence would be self-caused, which is impossible. Second, it would eliminate the need for God entirely, leaving only pre-eternity as a distinguishing attribute.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the second part of the refutation. Notice the two 'likewise' statements.
2
First consequence: self-creation
The author argues that if takwin is mukawwan, then the coming-to-be of the mukawwan would be by itself, not by Allah. This implies things create themselves.
This contradicts the need for a Creator.
3
Second consequence: no need for God
The second consequence is that there would be no distinction between God and creation except pre-eternity, but that is insufficient. God would be unnecessary.
This leads to atheism or pantheism.
4
Reflect on the argument
Consider how these consequences show the original claim is false. The identity claim is self-defeating.

Source Text

Commentary
