Refutation of Takwin Being Identical to Mukawwan
The author refutes the identity claim via analogy and reductio ad absurdum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the attribute of takwin cannot be identical to the thing it brings into existence, and how this leads to logical absurdity.

Core Idea
If cause and effect were identical, everything would be self-creating.

In this passage, the author addresses a theological claim that could undermine the distinction between God's creative attribute and the created world. He argues that equating takwin with the created thing leads to impossible consequences, showing why we must maintain the distinction. By following his reasoning, you'll see how careful logic protects core Islamic beliefs about God's role as Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage once
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get the overall argument before analyzing.
Notice the author uses analogy and a causal argument.
2
Identify the two arguments
The author provides two proofs: an analogy with actions (hitting, breaking, eating) and a causal argument (if takwin=mukawwan, then things create themselves). Find both.
3
Analyze the analogy
Consider how hitting is distinct from what is hit; apply the same to takwin and mukawwan. Why does this analogy show the claim is false?
4
Consider the reductio
Trace the causal argument: if takwin is identical to the mukawwan, then the mukawwan comes about by itself, implying self-creation and nullifying the Maker. Understand why this is a contradiction.
This argument shows the absurd consequences of the claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما عن رده على القول بأن التكوين هو عين المكون فيقول : إن هذا الكلام باطل، لأنه يؤدي إلى القول بأن الضرب عين المضروب والكسر عين المكسور، والأكل عين المأكول مع أن الضرب فعل والمضروب مفعول. وكذلك لو كان التكوين هو المكون، والمكون قد حصل بالتكوين، فيكون حصول المكون بنفسه لا بالله، وهذا يؤدي أن تكون الأشياء خالقة لنفسها، ويبطل وجود الصانع، ويكون كل شيء خلق ومخلوق في وقت واحد، والقول بهذا واضح التناقض.
As for his refutation of the statement that takwin is identical to the mukawwan, he says: This speech is false, because it leads to the statement that the hitting is identical to the thing hit, and the breaking is identical to the thing broken, and the eating is identical to the thing eaten, while hitting is an action and the thing hit is an object. Likewise, if takwin were the mukawwan, and the mukawwan has come about by takwin, then the coming about of the mukawwan would be by itself, not by God, and this leads to things being creators of themselves, and nullifies the existence of the Maker, and everything would be creator and created at the same time, and saying this is clear contradiction.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage presents a refutation by analogy and reductio ad absurdum. The objection is that some claim takwin is identical to mukawwan (the thing brought into existence). The author refutes this by showing that it leads to impossible consequences. First, by analogy: if takwin were identical to its effect, then every action would be identical to its object (e.g., hitting identical to the object hit), but we know hitting is an action (fi'l) and the object is a passive object (maf'ul), so they are distinct. Second, if takwin is identical to the mukawwan, then the mukawwan comes about by itself because takwin is the same thing, so it would not need God. This would make things self-creators, negate the existence of God as Maker, and imply that everything is simultaneously creator and created—a clear contradiction. The argument is based on the principle that the cause of a thing cannot be identical to the thing itself, otherwise the thing would be self-causing, which is impossible.

Key Terms
عين (identical)
فعل (action)
مفعول (object)
صانع (Maker)
خلق (to create)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that takwin, as God's creative attribute, is the same as the created thing itself.
Correction: The author shows that this would make actions identical to their objects and things self-creating, which are impossible.

Checkpoint
What does the author argue would happen if takwin were identical to the mukawwan?
A) The world would be eternal
B) Things would be creators of themselves
C) Takwin would be created
D) God would be the same as His creation

Key Takeaway
The attribute of takwin is ontologically distinct from the created thing, otherwise absurdities follow.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you living as if your own existence is self-caused, independent of the Maker? How does this argument confront your daily forgetfulness of God's constant act of sustaining you?
?
If takwin is distinct from the created thing, then every moment of your existence is a fresh act of God. Does your heart feel the weight of that dependency? What would change if you truly believed this?
?
The argument shows that confusing cause and effect leads to absurdity. In what areas of your life are you confusing the means (sabab) with the ultimate Cause (God)? Name one specific habit where you attribute power to the method rather than the Maker.

Power Alone Is Not Enough: The Need for Takwin
First argument: power needs takwin for actualization.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why divine power (qudra) alone does not suffice for creation and why the attribute of takwin is necessary.

Core Idea
Power enables; takwin actualizes.

The author begins by clarifying a subtle but crucial distinction: God's power, though infinite, does not by itself bring things into existence. Power is an attribute of ability, not of efficient causation. We need another attribute, takwin, which is the very act of bringing things about. This passage lays out that distinction and sets the stage for a refutation of opposing views.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on power vs. takwin
Read the first part of the Arabic text and its translation. Notice the contrast between 'la yughni' (does not suffice) and the positive role of takwin.
The key difference: power does not necessitate actualization; takwin does.
2
Understand why power is insufficient
The author states that power does not require the actual occurrence of the thing it has power over. Think of human analogy: you may have the power to lift an arm but not actually lift it. Similarly, God's power is an ability to do or not do; it doesn't force action.
3
Contrast with takwin
Takwin, on the other hand, necessitates the occurrence in reality. It is the attribute that brings about existence directly.
This distinction is essential for Maturidi theology.
4
Reflect on the theological importance
Ask yourself: why would anyone deny takwin? The Ash'aris, for example, see creation as direct with no separate attribute. This passage argues that would be insufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقول بأن حصول العالم بقدرة الله لا يغني عن التكوين، لأن القدرة لا توجب حصول المقدور بالفعل، بخلاف التكوين فإنه يوجب حدوث المكونات في الواقع بالفعل. ويبطل كلام الأشاعرة لأنهم يقولون في الاستدلال على قدم كلام الله بقوله تعالى: {إِنَّمَا قَوْلُنَا لِشَيْءٍ إِذَا أَرَدْنَهُ أَن تَقُولَ لَهُ كُن فَيَكُونُ} واستشهادهم بهذه الآية هو عين ما يقول به النسفي من قدم صفة التكوين، فلو كان التكوين عين المكون، لوقعوا في مناقضة واضحة، وذلك لأن حصول الشيء لو حصل بتكوين هو نفسه كان حصوله بنفسه لا بغيره، وما لا يحتاج في حصوله إلى غيره يكون قديما، فيكون الشيء على كلامهم قديما، وهذا بدوره يؤدي إلى قدم كل العالم وهو محال.
And the statement that the occurrence of the world by the power of God does not suffice without takwin, because power does not necessitate the actual occurrence of the thing empowered, unlike takwin, for it necessitates the occurrence of the things brought into existence in reality. And the speech of the Ash'ari is refuted, because they argue for the eternity of God's speech by His saying: 'Our saying to a thing when We will it is to say to it: Be, and it is.' And their citing this verse is exactly what al-Nasafi says regarding the eternity of the attribute of takwin. For if takwin were identical to the mukawwan, they would fall into clear contradiction, because if the occurrence of a thing occurs by a takwin that is itself [the thing], then its occurrence is by itself, not by another, and whatever does not need another for its occurrence is eternal, so the thing according to their speech would be eternal, and this in turn leads to the eternity of the whole world, which is impossible.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage contains two arguments. First, a direct argument: the power (qudra) of God does not by itself necessitate the actual existence of the thing it has power over (al-maqdur), because power is the ability to do or not do; it does not entail actualization. In contrast, takwin is the attribute that actually brings things into existence, so it is necessary. Second, a refutation of the Ash'ari proof for the eternity of God's speech. The Ash'aris cite the Quranic verse 'إنما قولنا لشيء إذا أردناه أن نقول له كن فيكون' to argue that God's speech (al-kalam) is eternal. The author points out that this very verse actually supports the eternity of takwin, because 'Be' (kun) is a command that brings about existence. If the Ash'aris maintain that takwin is identical to the created thing (as some might hold), they fall into contradiction: the thing would then cause itself, making it eternal, which leads to the impossibility of the whole world being eternal. The author uses the Ash'aris' own reasoning to argue against them, showing that the verse implies an eternal attribute of command that is distinct from the created thing.

Key Terms
القدرة (qudra)
المقدور (al-maqdur)
التكوين (takwin)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think God's power alone directly creates everything, so no separate attribute is needed.
Correction: Power is an attribute of ability, not efficient causation. Actual creation requires an additional attribute, takwin, which directly causes existence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does power alone not suffice for creation?
A) Power is limited
B) Power does not necessitate actual occurrence
C) Power is not eternal
D) Power requires an external cause

Key Takeaway
Divine power (qudra) is an attribute of ability, not efficient causation; takwin is the attribute that actually brings things into existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray for something, do you trust only that God can do it (qudra), or do you also truly believe He will bring it into existence (takwin) at the right time? Which attribute do you rely on more, and how does that affect your patience?
?
How often do you assume that because God is All-Powerful, He should act in a certain way or solve your problems instantly? What does this lesson teach you about the relationship between God's ability and His actual creation? Will you change how you wait for His action?
?
If God's power alone does not guarantee actual existence, what does that imply about your own efforts and reliance on Him? Are you content with just having the ability, or do you seek the actualization that comes only from Him?

Refuting the Ash'ari Proof for Eternal Speech
Second argument: refutation of Ash'ari proof using their own verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'ari proof for the eternity of God's speech is turned against them to actually support the eternity of takwin.

Core Idea
The Ash'ari proof backfires: 'Be' implies an eternal command.

The Ash'aris cite a Quranic verse to argue that God's speech is eternal. The author of the passage turns this argument around: the very verse they use, 'Be' (kun), is a command that brings about existence. This, he argues, actually supports the Maturidi view that takwin (the attribute of bringing into being) is eternal. If takwin were identical to the created thing, the Ash'aris would fall into a contradiction leading to the eternity of the world.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation passage
Read the second part of the Arabic text and its translation. Notice the logical structure: the author takes the Ash'ari proof and shows it leads to a contradiction.
2
Identify the Ash'ari proof
The Ash'aris use the verse 'إنما قولنا لشيء إذا أردناه أن نقول له كن فيكون' to argue that God's speech (the command) is eternal.
3
See how the author turns it
The author points out that this very verse is what al-Nasafi uses to support the eternity of takwin. The command 'Be' is an eternal attribute.
4
Understand the contradiction
If the Ash'aris claim that takwin is identical to the created thing, then the thing would be self-causing and thus eternal, leading to an impossible consequence.

Proofs for the Eternity of Takwin
Proofs for eternity of takwin with two arguments and a conclusion on created things.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational arguments proving that takwin (the attribute of bringing into existence) is eternal and why its eternity does not imply the eternity of created things.

Core Idea
Takwin must be eternal—if originated, either infinite regress or impossible consequences follow.

This passage presents the Maturidi case for the eternity of the divine attribute of takwin. Using logical proofs from infinite regress and exhaustive division, the author establishes that takwin cannot be originated. He then clarifies that this eternal attribute does not force the created world to be eternal as well.

Guided Path
1
Understand the central question
Recognize that takwin is either eternal or originated. This dichotomy frames the entire argument.
The author will eliminate the possibility of origination.
2
Follow the first proof: infinite regress
If takwin were originated, it would need another act of origination, leading to an infinite chain. This is impossible because the world exists and depends on takwin.
3
Examine the trilemma of possibilities
Consider the three possible loci for an originated takwin: no locus, a locus other than God, or in God. Each option is shown to be false or leads to disbelief.
This is an exhaustive division.
4
Grasp the conclusion on eternity
Since all alternatives fail, takwin must be eternal and subsisting in God's essence. Then understand why this does not make created things eternal.
5
Reflect on the distinction
Created things are dependent on takwin and therefore originated. The eternal attribute does not impart its eternity to its effects.
This guards against a common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتكوين بعد هذا إما أن يكون أزليا، وإما أن يكون حادثا، فلو كان حادثا للزم إحداث آخر، والآخر بآخر إلى ما لا يتناهي، وهو محال، لأن حصول العالم متعلق بحصوله، وما علق حصوله بما يستحيل ثبوته لا يتصور وجوده لكن العالم موجود بالفعل، فكان القول بحدوث التكوين باطل. ولأنه لو كان حادثا فلا يخلو الأمر إما أن يحدث لا في محل وهو باطل لاستحالة قيام العرض بنفسه، وأما أن يحدث في محل سوى ذات الله فيكون المحل هو الخالق لا الله وهو باطل، وإما أن يحدث في ذات الله، وهذا يقتضي قيام الحوادث به وهو باطل لأنه يؤدي إلى حدوث ذات الباري وهو كفر، وعلى هذا فإن التكوين أزلي قائم بذاته تعالى، ولا يوجب قدمه قدم المكونات، وذلك لأن ما تعلق تكونه بالتكوين يكون حادثا لا محالة إذ المحدث يعلق حدوثه بغيره فأما القديم فهو مستغن عن ذلك، ولأننا نقول كما يقول الأشاعرة بأن الله عالم، وأن الله قادر ولم
And takwin after this is either eternal or originated. If it were originated, then another origination would be necessary, and that another ad infinitum, which is impossible, because the occurrence of the world is dependent on its occurrence, and what is depended upon for its occurrence by something whose establishment is impossible is inconceivable, but the world exists in actuality, so the statement of takwin's temporality is false. And because if it were originated, then the matter is either that it occurs without a locus, which is false because it is impossible for an accident to subsist by itself; or that it occurs in a locus other than God's essence, then that locus would be the creator, not God, which is false; or that it occurs in God's essence, which necessitates the occurrence of originated things in Him, which is false because it leads to the temporality of the Essence of the Creator, which is unbelief. On this basis, takwin is eternal, subsisting in His essence, and its eternity does not necessitate the eternity of the things brought into existence, because that which its becoming is dependent on takwin is necessarily originated, since the originated is dependent for its occurrence on another, while the eternal is independent of that. And because we say, just as the Ash'aris say, that God is knowing, and that God is powerful, and [the text cuts off]
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage provides two main proofs for the eternity of takwin. First, a proof from infinite regress: if takwin were originated, it would require another act of origination, leading to an infinite chain, which is impossible. Moreover, the world's existence depends on takwin; if takwin itself were impossible (due to infinite regress), the world could not exist, but it does, so takwin must be eternal. Second, a proof by exhaustive division: if takwin were originated, it must occur either (a) without a locus (impossible, as accidents cannot subsist by themselves), (b) in a locus other than God (making that locus the creator), or (c) in God's essence (implying that God is subject to temporal events, which leads to His temporality and is disbelief). All options are false, so takwin must be eternal. The passage then clarifies that takwin's eternity does not entail the eternity of created things (al-mukawwanat), because the created things are dependent on takwin and hence originated, while the eternal (God) is independent. The text ends abruptly while comparing to the Ash'ari view that God is knowing and powerful, likely to show that just as those attributes are eternal, so is takwin.

Key Terms
تكوين
أزلي
حادث
إحداث
محل
عرض
كفر
مكونات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If takwin is eternal, then the things it brings into existence (the world) must also be eternal.
Correction: The author explicitly states that takwin's eternity does not necessitate the eternity of created things, because created things are dependent on takwin and therefore originated.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is one of the false possibilities if takwin were originated?
A) Takwin occurs in a locus other than God
B) Takwin occurs without any effect
C) Takwin is identical to the world
D) Takwin is created by angels

Key Takeaway
Takwin is an eternal attribute of God, and its eternity does not make the created world eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage warns that attributing temporality to takwin could lead to unbelief. Are there any beliefs you hold about God’s attributes that, if scrutinized logically, might lead to unacceptable consequences? How will you ensure your understanding remains sound?
?
The author insists that takwin’s eternity does not make creation eternal. Do you ever unconsciously assume that because God is eternal, His acts or their effects must also be eternal? How does this lesson compel you to rethink God’s relationship with time?
?
The tripartite impossibility shows that takwin cannot be originated because each possibility fails. When you face a difficult theological question, do you exercise such rigorous logical reasoning, or do you rely on comfortable assumptions? What step will you take today to sharpen your intellectual commitment to the truth?

5 min
The Necessity of the Attribute of Takwin
Nasafi argues that power does not necessitate actual existence; takwin does.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Maturidis argue that God's power (qudra) alone is insufficient for creation and that a distinct attribute, al-takwin, is necessary.

Core Idea
Power enables; takwin brings into existence.

The Maturidi school distinguishes between God's power to create and the act of creating itself. This lesson introduces the argument that power does not by itself produce existence; rather, a separate eternal attribute, al-takwin, is required for actual bringing-into-existence. Understanding this distinction is key to the Maturidi position on divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage contrasts power (qudra) with takwin directly.
2
Understand the distinction between power and takwin
Identify what each attribute does: power is a capacity, takwin is the actual bringing into existence. Why does power alone not suffice?
The passage says power does not necessitate the actual existence of the object of power.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider: if power alone were enough, creation would be automatic. What does this say about God's attributes?
This distinction prevents temporality from entering God's essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقول بأن حصول العالم بقدرة الله لا يغني عن التكوين، لأن القدرة لا توجب حصول المقدور بالفعل (73) ، بخلاف التكوين فإنه يوجب حدوث المكونات في الواقع بالفعل. ويبطل كلام الأشاعرة لأنهم يقولون في الاستدلال على قدم كلام الله بقوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّمَا قَوْلُنَا لِشَيْءٍ إِذَا أَرَدْنَهُ أَن تَقُولَ لَهُ كُن فَيَكُونُ ﴾ [النحل: ٤٠] واستشهادهم بهذه الآية هو عين ما يقول به النسفي من قدم صفة التكوين، فلو كان التكوين عين المكون، لوقعوا في مناقضة واضحة، وذلك لأن حصول الشيء لو حصل بتكوين هو نفسه كان حصوله بنفسه لا بغيره، وما لا يحتاج في حصوله إلى غيره يكون قديما، فيكون الشيء على كلامهم قديما، وهذا بدوره يؤدي إلى قدم كل العالم وهو محال والتكوين بعد هذا إما أن يكون أزليا، وإما أن يكون حادثا، فلو كان حادثا للزم إحداث آخر، والآخر بآخر إلى ما لا يتناهي، وهو محال، لأن حصول العالم متعلق بحصوله، وما علق حصوله بما يستحيل ثبوته لا يتصور وجوده لكن العالم موجود بالفعل، فكان القول بحدوث التكوين باطل. ولأنه لو كان حادثا فلا يخلو الأمر إما أن يحدث لا في محل وهو باطل لاستحالة قيام العرض بنفسه، وأما أن يحدث في محل سوى ذات الله فيكون المحل هو الخالق لا الله وهو باطل، وإما أن يحدث في ذات الله، وهذا يقتضي قيام الحوادث به وهو باطل لأنه يؤدي إلى حدوث ذات الباري وهو كفر، وعلى هذا فإن التكوين أزلي قائم بذاته تعالى، ولا يوجب قدمه قدم المكونات، وذلك لأن ما تعلق تكونه بالتكوين يكون حادثا لا محالة إذ المحدث يعلق حدوثه بغيره فأما القديم فهو مستغن عن ذلك، ولأننا نقول كما يقول الأشاعرة بأن الله عالم، وأن الله قادر ولم (73) لأنها عند الماتريدية ليست صفة تأثير وإنما هي صفة يصح لمن اتصف بها الإيجاد والإعدام، أما الإيجاد والإعدام الفعلي فيرجع إلى صفة التأثير التي هي التكوين.
And the statement that the world's existence through God's power does not dispense with al-takwin (bringing-into-existence), because power does not necessitate the actual existence of the thing capable of being brought into existence (al-maqdur), contrary to al-takwin, for it necessitates the occurrence of the things brought into existence (al-mukawwanat) in reality. And he refutes the speech of the Ash'aris, because they argue for the eternity of God's speech by His saying, the Exalted: {Our word to a thing when We will it is only that We say to it 'Be', and it is} [Surat an-Nahl: 40]. And their citing this verse is exactly what an-Nasafi says about the eternity of the attribute of al-takwin. For if al-takwin were identical to the thing brought into existence (al-mukawwan), they would fall into clear contradiction. That is because if a thing were to come to be by an al-takwin that is itself that thing, its coming to be would be by itself, not by another, and whatever does not need another for its coming to be would be eternal. Thus the thing according to their statement would be eternal, and this in turn leads to the eternity of the entire world, which is impossible. And al-takwin after this is either eternal or originated. If it were originated, it would necessitate another bringing into existence, and another after another ad infinitum, which is impossible, because the world's existence is dependent upon its existence, and whatever is dependent in its existence upon what is impossible to establish cannot be conceived to exist. But the world does exist in reality, so the statement that al-takwin is originated is false. And because if it were originated, the matter would not be free from: either it comes to be not in a locus, which is false due to the impossibility of an accident subsisting by itself; or it comes to be in a locus other than God's essence, so that locus would be the creator, not God, which is false; or it comes to be in God's essence, and this necessitates the occurrence of originated things in Him, which is false because it leads to the origination of the essence of the Creator, which is disbelief. Upon this, al-takwin is eternal, subsisting by His essence, Exalted, and its eternity does not necessitate the eternity of the things brought into existence. That is because whatever is brought into being by al-takwin is necessarily originated, since the originated thing depends for its origination upon another. As for the eternal, it is independent of that. And because we say, as the Ash'aris say, that God is knowing and that God is powerful and not—(73) because, according to the Maturidis, it is not an attribute of effect, but rather it is an attribute by which one who is qualified by it is capable of producing and annihilating. As for actual producing and annihilating, it reverts to the attribute of effect, which is al-takwin.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the eternity of the divine attribute al-takwin (bringing-into-existence) and a refutation of the Ash'ari position that identifies it with the thing brought into existence. The argument proceeds as follows: First, it states that the world's existence through God's power does not eliminate the need for al-takwin, because power (qudra) does not by itself necessitate the actual existence of the thing it is capable of effecting; rather, it is the attribute of al-takwin that brings about existence. Then it refutes the Ash'ari appeal to the Quranic verse 'When We will a thing, We say to it "Be", and it is' which they use to argue for the eternity of God's speech. an-Nasafi points out that the verse actually supports his own position that al-takwin is eternal, because if al-takwin were identical to the thing created, then the thing would be self-caused and therefore eternal, leading to the impossible consequence that the entire world is eternal. Next, he examines the alternatives for al-takwin: either it is eternal or originated. If originated, it would require an infinite chain of creations, which is impossible because the world's existence depends on it and an infinite regress cannot be realized. Moreover, if it were originated, it would have to subsist either in no locus (impossible for an accident), in a locus other than God (making that locus the creator), or in God's essence (which would imply change in God and lead to His origination, which is disbelief). Therefore al-takwin must be eternal. Finally, he explains that the eternity of al-takwin does not entail the eternity of the things brought into existence, because things that come into being through al-takwin are by nature originated, while the eternal is self-sufficient. The footnote clarifies that power (qudra) according to the Maturidis is not an attribute of effect but rather the capacity to produce or annihilate; the actual producing and annihilating is the attribute of effect, which is al-takwin.

B) It necessitates the actual existence of the created thing.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidis posit a distinct attribute, al-takwin, which directly brings things into existence, a role not fulfilled by power alone.

?
If takwin is an eternal attribute of God, meaning He is always bringing-into-existence, how does that change your view of God's relationship with creation? Does this make you feel closer to God or more dependent on His constant act of sustaining you? Why?

Refuting the Ash'ari Use of the 'Be' Verse
Nasafi refutes the Ash'ari interpretation of the verse and shows its implication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi refutes the Ash'ari argument for the eternity of God's speech by showing that their own proof actually supports the Maturidi view of al-takwin as an eternal attribute.

Core Idea
The Ash'ari verse proves takwin's eternity, not just speech.

The Ash'aris cite the Quranic verse 'When We will a thing, We say to it "Be" and it is' to argue for the eternity of God's speech. Nasafi points out that this very verse supports the Maturidi claim that al-takwin is an eternal attribute. Moreover, if the Ash'aris identify takwin with the created thing, they would fall into a contradiction that leads to the eternity of the world.

Guided Path
1
Read the Ash'ari argument as presented
The Ash'aris use the verse to argue that God's speech is eternal. Notice the verse and their inference.
They equate 'Be' with God's speech.
2
Understand Nasafi's counter
Nasafi says the verse actually shows the eternity of takwin. How does he reinterpret the verse?
The command 'Be' is the expression of takwin.
3
Grasp the reductio ad absurdum
If takwin were identical to the thing created, then the thing would be self-caused and eternal, leading to the eternity of the world. Why is this impossible?
The world is clearly originated, so takwin cannot be identical to it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقول بأن حصول العالم بقدرة الله لا يغني عن التكوين، لأن القدرة لا توجب حصول المقدور بالفعل (73) ، بخلاف التكوين فإنه يوجب حدوث المكونات في الواقع بالفعل. ويبطل كلام الأشاعرة لأنهم يقولون في الاستدلال على قدم كلام الله بقوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّمَا قَوْلُنَا لِشَيْءٍ إِذَا أَرَدْنَهُ أَن تَقُولَ لَهُ كُن فَيَكُونُ ﴾ [النحل: ٤٠] واستشهادهم بهذه الآية هو عين ما يقول به النسفي من قدم صفة التكوين، فلو كان التكوين عين المكون، لوقعوا في مناقضة واضحة، وذلك لأن حصول الشيء لو حصل بتكوين هو نفسه كان حصوله بنفسه لا بغيره، وما لا يحتاج في حصوله إلى غيره يكون قديما، فيكون الشيء على كلامهم قديما، وهذا بدوره يؤدي إلى قدم كل العالم وهو محال والتكوين بعد هذا إما أن يكون أزليا، وإما أن يكون حادثا، فلو كان حادثا للزم إحداث آخر، والآخر بآخر إلى ما لا يتناهي، وهو محال، لأن حصول العالم متعلق بحصوله، وما علق حصوله بما يستحيل ثبوته لا يتصور وجوده لكن العالم موجود بالفعل، فكان القول بحدوث التكوين باطل. ولأنه لو كان حادثا فلا يخلو الأمر إما أن يحدث لا في محل وهو باطل لاستحالة قيام العرض بنفسه، وأما أن يحدث في محل سوى ذات الله فيكون المحل هو الخالق لا الله وهو باطل، وإما أن يحدث في ذات الله، وهذا يقتضي قيام الحوادث به وهو باطل لأنه يؤدي إلى حدوث ذات الباري وهو كفر، وعلى هذا فإن التكوين أزلي قائم بذاته تعالى، ولا يوجب قدمه قدم المكونات، وذلك لأن ما تعلق تكونه بالتكوين يكون حادثا لا محالة إذ المحدث يعلق حدوثه بغيره فأما القديم فهو مستغن عن ذلك، ولأننا نقول كما يقول الأشاعرة بأن الله عالم، وأن الله قادر ولم (73) لأنها عند الماتريدية ليست صفة تأثير وإنما هي صفة يصح لمن اتصف بها الإيجاد والإعدام، أما الإيجاد والإعدام الفعلي فيرجع إلى صفة التأثير التي هي التكوين.
And the statement that the world's existence through God's power does not dispense with al-takwin (bringing-into-existence), because power does not necessitate the actual existence of the thing capable of being brought into existence (al-maqdur), contrary to al-takwin, for it necessitates the occurrence of the things brought into existence (al-mukawwanat) in reality. And he refutes the speech of the Ash'aris, because they argue for the eternity of God's speech by His saying, the Exalted: {Our word to a thing when We will it is only that We say to it 'Be', and it is} [Surat an-Nahl: 40]. And their citing this verse is exactly what an-Nasafi says about the eternity of the attribute of al-takwin. For if al-takwin were identical to the thing brought into existence (al-mukawwan), they would fall into clear contradiction. That is because if a thing were to come to be by an al-takwin that is itself that thing, its coming to be would be by itself, not by another, and whatever does not need another for its coming to be would be eternal. Thus the thing according to their statement would be eternal, and this in turn leads to the eternity of the entire world, which is impossible. And al-takwin after this is either eternal or originated. If it were originated, it would necessitate another bringing into existence, and another after another ad infinitum, which is impossible, because the world's existence is dependent upon its existence, and whatever is dependent in its existence upon what is impossible to establish cannot be conceived to exist. But the world does exist in reality, so the statement that al-takwin is originated is false. And because if it were originated, the matter would not be free from: either it comes to be not in a locus, which is false due to the impossibility of an accident subsisting by itself; or it comes to be in a locus other than God's essence, so that locus would be the creator, not God, which is false; or it comes to be in God's essence, and this necessitates the occurrence of originated things in Him, which is false because it leads to the origination of the essence of the Creator, which is disbelief. Upon this, al-takwin is eternal, subsisting by His essence, Exalted, and its eternity does not necessitate the eternity of the things brought into existence. That is because whatever is brought into being by al-takwin is necessarily originated, since the originated thing depends for its origination upon another. As for the eternal, it is independent of that. And because we say, as the Ash'aris say, that God is knowing and that God is powerful and not—(73) because, according to the Maturidis, it is not an attribute of effect, but rather it is an attribute by which one who is qualified by it is capable of producing and annihilating. As for actual producing and annihilating, it reverts to the attribute of effect, which is al-takwin.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the eternity of the divine attribute al-takwin (bringing-into-existence) and a refutation of the Ash'ari position that identifies it with the thing brought into existence. The argument proceeds as follows: First, it states that the world's existence through God's power does not eliminate the need for al-takwin, because power (qudra) does not by itself necessitate the actual existence of the thing it is capable of effecting; rather, it is the attribute of al-takwin that brings about existence. Then it refutes the Ash'ari appeal to the Quranic verse 'When We will a thing, We say to it "Be", and it is' which they use to argue for the eternity of God's speech. an-Nasafi points out that the verse actually supports his own position that al-takwin is eternal, because if al-takwin were identical to the thing created, then the thing would be self-caused and therefore eternal, leading to the impossible consequence that the entire world is eternal. Next, he examines the alternatives for al-takwin: either it is eternal or originated. If originated, it would require an infinite chain of creations, which is impossible because the world's existence depends on it and an infinite regress cannot be realized. Moreover, if it were originated, it would have to subsist either in no locus (impossible for an accident), in a locus other than God (making that locus the creator), or in God's essence (which would imply change in God and lead to His origination, which is disbelief). Therefore al-takwin must be eternal. Finally, he explains that the eternity of al-takwin does not entail the eternity of the things brought into existence, because things that come into being through al-takwin are by nature originated, while the eternal is self-sufficient. The footnote clarifies that power (qudra) according to the Maturidis is not an attribute of effect but rather the capacity to produce or annihilate; the actual producing and annihilating is the attribute of effect, which is al-takwin.

قديم

A) The thing would be originated.
B) The thing would be eternal.
C) God's speech would be temporal.
D) Takwin would be unnecessary.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari use of the verse 'Be' actually supports the Maturidi view that al-takwin is an eternal attribute, and identifying takwin with creation leads to the impossible eternity of the world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the verse 'Be, and it is,' do you truly believe that God's command is still actively bringing things into existence at this very moment? How does that conviction shape your trust in His provision for your needs today?
?
If you held that God's attribute of bringing-into-existence was merely the same as the created thing, would you then be tempted to rely on the creation itself rather than the Creator? Examine your heart: are there any created things you depend upon as if they were self-sufficient?
?
The Ash'ari position leads to the conclusion that the world would be eternal—how does that subtle error affect one's sense of accountability to God? Do you ever live as if this world is permanent, forgetting that it is continuously sustained by His command?

Proof that Takwin is Eternal and Its Objects Originated
Nasafi proves the eternity of al-takwin by eliminating the possibility of its origination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi proof that al-takwin must be eternal, and why this does not imply that the things brought into existence are eternal.

Core Idea
Takwin is eternal; its products are not.

After establishing the necessity and distinctness of al-takwin, Nasafi provides a rigorous proof that it must be eternal. He considers the two possibilities and demonstrates that if takwin were originated, it would lead to impossibilities such as infinite regress or unacceptable loci for its subsistence. He then clarifies that the eternity of takwin does not entail the eternity of the created things, as they depend on it for their origin. A footnote clarifies the Maturidi distinction between power as capacity and takwin as actual effecting.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dichotomy
Nasafi sets up two possibilities: takwin is either eternal (azali) or originated (hadith). Read the opening sentence.
This is a classic dilemma argument.
2
Examine the infinite regress argument
If takwin were originated, it would require another takwin, leading to an infinite chain. Why is this impossible?
The world exists, so its dependence cannot be on an impossible chain.
3
Examine the three impossible loci
If takwin were originated, it must subsist in a locus. Nasafi lists three possibilities and shows each is impossible. Identify them.
No locus, locus other than God, God's essence – all ruled out.
4
Grasp the distinction between eternal attribute and temporal objects
The passage concludes that takwin is eternal, but the things it creates are not. Why? Because they depend on takwin for their origin.
This guards against the misconception that the world is eternal.

Will you acknowledge that only God's eternal attribute of takwin brings things into being?

Does your heart truly rest in the reality that God's creative attribute is always present, even when you see no immediate results? The Definition of Divine Will and Its Proof
Nasafi defines irada as an eternal attribute, distinguishes it from mashi'a, and presents a proof that God is described by will in reality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic and technical definition of God's will (irada), its relation to volition (mashi'a), and the Sunni proof that God is described by will in reality.

Core Idea
God's will is an eternal attribute that specifies acts; the proof is the specification of similar acts.

Nasafi begins by defining the term 'irada' (will) both linguistically and technically, showing that it is distinct from aversion and compulsion. He then clarifies the relationship between irada and mashi'a, and provides an argument that God is described by will in reality, not metaphorically. This lesson covers the foundational definition and the central proof.

Guided Path
1
Examine the linguistic definition
Notice that irada is derived from al-rawd, meaning seeking or inclination. This sets the conceptual root.
2
Understand the technical definition
The technical definition emphasizes that will is incompatible with aversion and compulsion, and necessitates the specific manner of actions.
3
Compare irada and mashi'a
Most theologians treat them as synonyms, but the Karamiyya differentiate. Understand both positions.
4
Analyze the Sunni proof
The proof from specification of actions shows that actions occurring in specific ways, when other ways are possible, indicates a will in the agent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإرادة صفة أزلية الله تعالى: يعرف النسفي الإرادة بأنها مشتقة في اللغة من الرود، ومن معاني الرود الطلب والميل. أما حدها فهي : معنى ينافر الكراهية والاضطرار، ويوجب خروج المفعولات على وجه دون وجه وعلى هذا فالإرادة والمشيئة ينبئان عن معنى واحد عند المتكلمين إلا الكرامية الذين قالوا: إن الإرادة غير المشيئة، فالمشيئة أزلية والإرادة حادثة في ذات الله تعالى، وله إرادات كثيرة على عدد المرادات. ويسأل هل يوصف الله تعالى بالإرادة؟ ويجيب إن جمهور الأمة وصفوه تعالى بالإرادة على الحقيقة خلافا للنظام، والبغداديين من المعتزلة كالكعبي، والخياط الذين قالوا: الله تعالى يوصف بها على المجاز. ويبين النسفي معنى ما يقوله هؤلاء المعتزلة. ثم يقيم دليل أهل السنة على اتصاف الله تعالى بالإرادة وهو: وقوع مفعولاته المتجانسة على أوصاف مخصوصة يجوز وقوعها على غيرها، ويعلم أن هذا لم يكن من ذواتها وهو يدل على إرادة الفاعل، ولأنه لو لم يكن مريدا لكان مضطرا، والمضطر عاجز. ويناقش المعتزلة في قولهم : إن الإرادة بالنسبة إلى الله هو فعل الله، وبالنسبة لفعل الغير هي أمر الله، ويبطل هذا الكلام. وكذلك يبين فساد رأي من يقول: إن الإرادة هي الشهوة. ويسأل النسفي : هل الله تعالى مريد بإرادة أم بغير إرادة؟ ويجيب بأن من قال بالإرادة قال : إنه مريد بها أما الحسين النجار فقد قال: إنه
The will is an eternal attribute of God, Exalted. an-Nasafi defines al-irada (will) as derived in language from al-rawd (seeking), and among the meanings of al-rawd are seeking and inclination. As for its definition, it is: a meaning that is incompatible with aversion (al-karahiyya) and compulsion (al-idtirar), and necessitates the bringing forth of things in a particular manner rather than another. Upon this, al-irada and al-mashi'a (volition) indicate one meaning according to the mutakallimun (speculative theologians), except for the Karamiyya, who said that al-irada is other than al-mashi'a: al-mashi'a is eternal while al-irada is originated in God's essence, and He has many wills according to the number of things willed. And he asks: Is God, Exalted, described by will? And he answers: The majority of the community described Him, Exalted, by will in reality, contrary to an-Nazzam, and the Baghdadis from the Mu'tazila like al-Ka'bi, and al-Khayyat, who said that God, Exalted, is described by it metaphorically. And an-Nasafi explains the meaning of what these Mu'tazila say. Then he establishes the proof of Ahl al-Sunna for God, Exalted, being qualified by will, which is: the occurrence of His similar acts upon specific descriptions it is possible for them to occur upon others, and it is known that this is not from their essences, and that indicates the will of the agent; and because if He were not willful, He would be compelled, and the compelled is incapable. And he discusses the Mu'tazila concerning their statement that will, with respect to God, is His act, and with respect to the act of another is His command, and he refutes this statement. And likewise he shows the corruption of the opinion of those who say that will is desire (al-shahwa). And an-Nasafi asks: Is God, Exalted, willful by a will or without a will? And he answers that whoever affirms will says that He is willful by it; as for al-Husayn al-Najjar, he said that He...
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of the divine attribute of will (al-irada) as eternal, along with refutations of sectarian distortions. It begins by giving the linguistic derivation of irada from al-rawd (seeking) and its definition as a meaning that is incompatible with aversion and compulsion, and that necessitates the specific bringing forth of actions. an-Nasafi then clarifies that irada and mashi'a (volition) are synonymous for most mutakallimun, except the Karamiyya who differentiate by making mashi'a eternal and irada originated in God's essence, and who assert multiple wills according to the number of things willed. Next, he raises the question of whether God is described by will, answering that the majority of the Muslim community affirm it in reality (haqiqa), opposing an-Nazzam and the Baghdad Mu'tazila (al-Ka'bi and al-Khayyat) who interpret it metaphorically. He then presents the Sunni proof: the fact that God's similar acts are specified with particular characteristics, even though it is possible for them to be otherwise, shows that this specification comes from the agent's will; otherwise, the agent would be under compulsion and therefore incapable. After that, he refutes the Mu'tazili view that will in relation to God is His own act but in relation to others is His command, showing its inconsistency. He also rejects the identification of will with desire (shahwa). Finally, he poses the question whether God is willful by a will or without a will, and notes that those who affirm will say He is willful by it, while al-Husayn al-Najjar had a different view (the text cuts off here).

Key Terms
إرادة
مشيئة
رواد
طلب
ميل
كراهية
اضطرار
مفعولات
حقيقة
مجاز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's will is metaphorical (majaz) and not a real attribute.
Correction: The passage states that the majority of the community describe God by will in reality (haqiqa), and provides a proof from the specification of acts.

Checkpoint
What is the Sunni proof for God being qualified by will (irada) as presented in this passage?
A) The Quranic verse about creation.
B) The occurrence of similar acts in specific ways, which cannot be from their essences, indicating a will.
C) The consensus of the Companions.
D) The fact that will is a linguistic necessity.

Key Takeaway
God's will is an eternal attribute that specifies the manner of actions, proven by the observed specification of similar acts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every detail of your life—the good and the bad—is specified by God's will, or do you sometimes act as if random chance or your own planning controls outcomes? How would your daily choices change if you fully internalized that God's will is the real specifier?
?
If you were honest with yourself, do you sometimes attribute your successes to your own effort and your failures to external circumstances, subtly denying that God's will determines both? What specific success will you consciously attribute to His will today?
?
The proof in this lesson argues that if God were not willful, He would be compelled and incapable. Do you live with the peace that comes from knowing nothing happens outside His will, or do your worries reveal a hidden belief that events are out of His control? What worry will you explicitly surrender to Him right now as an act of faith in His perfect will?

Refutations of Deviant Views on Divine Will
Nasafi refutes Mu'tazili and other erroneous views on divine will and discusses the relation between will and the agent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the refutations of Mu'tazili and other views on God's will, including the equation of will with desire and the question of whether God is willful by a will or without it.

Core Idea
God's will is neither command nor desire, and it is essential to His being not compelled.

After establishing the definition and proof of divine will, an-Nasafi addresses several incorrect views. He refutes the Mu'tazila who claim that will is God's own act or His command, rejects those who equate will with desire, and raises the question whether God is willful by a will or without it. This lesson covers these refutations and sets the record straight.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazili claim
The Mu'tazila said will in relation to God is His act, and in relation to others is His command. Nasafi refutes this by showing its inconsistency.
2
Reject the equation of will with desire
Some identified will with desire (shahwa). Nasafi shows the corruption of this view.
3
Consider the question of willfulness
Nasafi asks whether God is willful by a will or without a will, and notes that those who affirm will say He is willful by it, but al-Husayn al-Najjar had a different view (text cut off).
The passage is incomplete, but the question highlights the importance of the attribute.

?

?
The lesson refutes that God's will is like desire (shahwa). Is there any desire in your heart that you have mistakenly attributed to God, thinking that He 'wants' something in the same way you crave it? What would change if you truly believed that God's will is utterly different from every human inclination?
?
Consider the question: Is God willful by a will or without? An-Nasafi affirms that those who affirm will say He is willful by it. Do you live as though God's will is accidental or temporary, or do you treat it as essential to who He is? If God's will is essential, then His every decision is rooted in His nature—how does that affect your trust in His decree?

The Majority View: God's Will is Real
Nasafi states the question and the two positions on divine will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the majority of the Ummah affirms God's will as a real attribute, while some Mu'tazila consider it metaphorical.

Core Idea
God's will is real, not metaphorical.

This lesson begins with a fundamental question: Is Allah described by irada? Nasafi presents the consensus of the Ummah that irada is a real attribute, and then identifies the Mu'tazila who dissented.

Guided Path
1
Read the question and answer
Read the opening question and Nasafi's immediate answer, noting the position of the majority (جمهور الأمة).
The answer states 'on the reality' (على الحقيقة).
2
Identify the two groups
Identify the majority and the Mu'tazila who oppose them. Note the specific names mentioned: al-Nazzam, al-Ka'bi, and al-Khayyat.
These are Baghdadi Mu'tazila.
3
Understand the metaphorical claim
The Mu'tazila say God is described by irada metaphorically (على المجاز). Reflect on what this means for their theology.
Nasafi will later explain the meaning of their view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسأل هل يوصف الله تعالى بالإرادة؟ ويجيب إن جمهور الأمة وصفوه تعالى بالإرادة على الحقيقة خلافا للنظام، والبغداديين من المعتزلة كالكعبي، والخياط الذين قالوا: الله تعالى يوصف بها على المجاز. ويبين النسفي معنى ما يقوله هؤلاء المعتزلة. ثم يقيم دليل أهل السنة على اتصاف الله تعالى بالإرادة وهو: وقوع مفعولاته المتجانسة على أوصاف مخصوصة يجوز وقوعها على غيرها، ويعلم أن هذا لم يكن من ذواتها وهو يدل على إرادة الفاعل، ولأنه لو لم يكن مريدا لكان مضطرا، والمضطر عاجز. ويناقش المعتزلة في قولهم : إن الإرادة بالنسبة إلى الله هو فعل الله، وبالنسبة لفعل الغير هي أمر الله، ويبطل هذا الكلام. وكذلك يبين فساد رأي من يقول: إن الإرادة هي الشهوة.
And he asks: Is Allah the Exalted described by al-irada? And he answers: Indeed, the majority of the Ummah described Him the Exalted by al-irada in reality, contrary to al-Nazzam, and the Baghdadi Mu'tazila like al-Ka'bi, and al-Khayyat who said: Allah the Exalted is described by it metaphorically. And al-Nasafi explains the meaning of what these Mu'tazila say. Then he establishes the proof of Ahl al-Sunna for the attribution of al-irada to Allah the Exalted, which is: The occurrence of His homogeneous effects upon specific descriptions that could have occurred upon others, and it is known that this was not from their essences, and this indicates the will of the agent, and because if He were not willing, He would be compelled, and the compelled is incapable. And he discusses the Mu'tazila regarding their saying: al-irada with respect to Allah is His action, and with respect to the action of another is His command, and he invalidates this statement. Likewise, he explains the corruption of the view of one who says: al-irada is appetite (al-shahwa).
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage presents a question-and-answer format. The question: Is God described by irada? Nasafi answers that the majority of the Ummah affirm irada as a real attribute of God, contrary to al-Nazzam and some Baghdadi Mu'tazila who say it is metaphorical. He then gives the Ahl al-Sunna proof: God's homogeneous effects (e.g., similar acts of creation) occur with specific qualities that could have been different; since this specificity does not come from the effects themselves, it points to a will in the agent. Moreover, if God were not willing, He would be compelled (mudtarr), and a compelled being is incapable. Nasafi then refutes the Mu'tazila claim that irada is either God's own action or His command to others, showing its inconsistency. Finally, he rejects the idea that irada is the same as appetite (shahwa).

Key Terms
الإرادة
الحقيقة
المجاز
النظام
الكعبي
الخياط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the Mu'tazila universally denied God's will, but they actually considered it metaphorical.
Correction: The Mu'tazila mentioned here did not deny irada entirely; they interpreted it metaphorically.

Checkpoint
Who are the Mu'tazila figures mentioned by Nasafi who say God's will is metaphorical?
A) Al-Nazzam, al-Ka'bi, and al-Khayyat
B) Al-Ash'ari and al-Maturidi
C) Jabir and al-Baydawi
D) Al-Ghazali and al-Razi

Key Takeaway
The majority of the Ummah affirms God's will as a real attribute, against the metaphorical interpretation of some Mu'tazila.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that God's will is real and active in your life, or do you sometimes treat it as a metaphor when things don't go your way? What would change if you took it literally?
?
When you face a trial, do you see it as a direct expression of God's will or just as random? How would your response differ if you affirmed God's will in reality?
?
The majority of the Ummah affirmed God's will as real. Does your heart align with that majority, or do you find yourself slipping into metaphorical thinking when it's convenient? Which of your actions this week would need to change if you truly believed God's will is real?

The Ahl al-Sunna Proof for Divine Will
Nasafi presents the Ahl al-Sunna rational proof for divine will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two-part proof that Ahl al-Sunna use to establish that God possesses a will.

Core Idea
Specificity in creation and the impossibility of compulsion prove God's will.

After stating the majority position, Nasafi presents the rational proof of Ahl al-Sunna for divine will. This proof relies on observing the specificity of God's actions and arguing that without will, God would be compelled.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof carefully
Read the entire proof in one go to grasp its flow. It consists of two parts: the observation of homogeneous effects and the argument from compulsion.
2
Analyze the first part
The first part: God's homogeneous effects (e.g., similar creations) occur with specific descriptions that could have been otherwise. This specificity shows it is not from the things themselves, pointing to a will.
Think of examples like one person being tall and another short.
3
Analyze the second part
The second part: If God were not willing, He would be compelled (مضطر), and a compelled being is incapable. Since God is not incapable, He must have a will.
This is a logical argument from negation.
4
Connect the two parts
Together, these two arguments form a complete proof: the specificity of creation indicates a will, and the absence of will implies compulsion, which is impossible for God.
Thus, irada is a necessary attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسأل هل يوصف الله تعالى بالإرادة؟ ويجيب إن جمهور الأمة وصفوه تعالى بالإرادة على الحقيقة خلافا للنظام، والبغداديين من المعتزلة كالكعبي، والخياط الذين قالوا: الله تعالى يوصف بها على المجاز. ويبين النسفي معنى ما يقوله هؤلاء المعتزلة. ثم يقيم دليل أهل السنة على اتصاف الله تعالى بالإرادة وهو: وقوع مفعولاته المتجانسة على أوصاف مخصوصة يجوز وقوعها على غيرها، ويعلم أن هذا لم يكن من ذواتها وهو يدل على إرادة الفاعل، ولأنه لو لم يكن مريدا لكان مضطرا، والمضطر عاجز. ويناقش المعتزلة في قولهم : إن الإرادة بالنسبة إلى الله هو فعل الله، وبالنسبة لفعل الغير هي أمر الله، ويبطل هذا الكلام. وكذلك يبين فساد رأي من يقول: إن الإرادة هي الشهوة.
And he asks: Is Allah the Exalted described by al-irada? And he answers: Indeed, the majority of the Ummah described Him the Exalted by al-irada in reality, contrary to al-Nazzam, and the Baghdadi Mu'tazila like al-Ka'bi, and al-Khayyat who said: Allah the Exalted is described by it metaphorically. And al-Nasafi explains the meaning of what these Mu'tazila say. Then he establishes the proof of Ahl al-Sunna for the attribution of al-irada to Allah the Exalted, which is: The occurrence of His homogeneous effects upon specific descriptions that could have occurred upon others, and it is known that this was not from their essences, and this indicates the will of the agent, and because if He were not willing, He would be compelled, and the compelled is incapable. And he discusses the Mu'tazila regarding their saying: al-irada with respect to Allah is His action, and with respect to the action of another is His command, and he invalidates this statement. Likewise, he explains the corruption of the view of one who says: al-irada is appetite (al-shahwa).

المضطر
عاجز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does Nasafi argue would be the case if God were not willing?
A) God would be unjust
B) God would be compelled and thus incapable
C) God's actions would be random
D) God would be ignorant

Key Takeaway
The Ahl al-Sunna proof for divine will uses the specificity of created attributes and the absurdity of divine compulsion.

Divine Attributes

Refuting Mu'tazila Definitions of Divine Will
Nasafi refutes Mu'tazila definitions of divine will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's refutation of the Mu'tazila claims that divine will is either God's action or His command, and why it cannot be equated with appetite.

Core Idea
Mu'tazila definitions reduce divine will to something else, but Nasafi shows their inconsistency.

After establishing the proof, Nasafi turns to refute the Mu'tazila who define irada in ways that avoid it being a real attribute. He addresses two views: that irada is God's own action or His command to others, and that irada is appetite.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation of the action/command definition
Read how Nasafi reports the Mu'tazila claim and then states that he invalidates it.
The claim: irada is God's action (for His own acts) or His command (for the acts of others).
2
Understand the inconsistency
Think about why this definition is problematic. For example, command and action are distinct from will; reducing will to them is equivocal.
Nasafi does not elaborate here, but later texts explain the inconsistency.
3
Read the rejection of irada as appetite
Nasafi explains the corruption of the view that irada is appetite (شهوة). Reflect on why this is anthropomorphic and unacceptable.
God is free from passions like appetite.
4
Summarize the refutations
These refutations guard against reducing God's will to something created or to a human-like passion.
Thus, irada is a real, distinct attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسأل هل يوصف الله تعالى بالإرادة؟ ويجيب إن جمهور الأمة وصفوه تعالى بالإرادة على الحقيقة خلافا للنظام، والبغداديين من المعتزلة كالكعبي، والخياط الذين قالوا: الله تعالى يوصف بها على المجاز. ويبين النسفي معنى ما يقوله هؤلاء المعتزلة. ثم يقيم دليل أهل السنة على اتصاف الله تعالى بالإرادة وهو: وقوع مفعولاته المتجانسة على أوصاف مخصوصة يجوز وقوعها على غيرها، ويعلم أن هذا لم يكن من ذواتها وهو يدل على إرادة الفاعل، ولأنه لو لم يكن مريدا لكان مضطرا، والمضطر عاجز. ويناقش المعتزلة في قولهم : إن الإرادة بالنسبة إلى الله هو فعل الله، وبالنسبة لفعل الغير هي أمر الله، ويبطل هذا الكلام. وكذلك يبين فساد رأي من يقول: إن الإرادة هي الشهوة.
And he asks: Is Allah the Exalted described by al-irada? And he answers: Indeed, the majority of the Ummah described Him the Exalted by al-irada in reality, contrary to al-Nazzam, and the Baghdadi Mu'tazila like al-Ka'bi, and al-Khayyat who said: Allah the Exalted is described by it metaphorically. And al-Nasafi explains the meaning of what these Mu'tazila say. Then he establishes the proof of Ahl al-Sunna for the attribution of al-irada to Allah the Exalted, which is: The occurrence of His homogeneous effects upon specific descriptions that could have occurred upon others, and it is known that this was not from their essences, and this indicates the will of the agent, and because if He were not willing, He would be compelled, and the compelled is incapable. And he discusses the Mu'tazila regarding their saying: al-irada with respect to Allah is His action, and with respect to the action of another is His command, and he invalidates this statement. Likewise, he explains the corruption of the view of one who says: al-irada is appetite (al-shahwa).
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage presents a question-and-answer format. The question: Is God described by irada? Nasafi answers that the majority of the Ummah affirm irada as a real attribute of God, contrary to al-Nazzam and some Baghdadi Mu'tazila who say it is metaphorical. He then gives the Ahl al-Sunna proof: God's homogeneous effects (e.g., similar acts of creation) occur with specific qualities that could have been different; since this specificity does not come from the effects themselves, it points to a will in the agent. Moreover, if God were not willing, He would be compelled (mudtarr), and a compelled being is incapable. Nasafi then refutes the Mu'tazila claim that irada is either God's own action or His command to others, showing its inconsistency. Finally, he rejects the idea that irada is the same as appetite (shahwa).

Key Terms
الإرادة
الأمر
الشهوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think divine will is merely God's command or His action, but Nasafi shows this is inconsistent.
Correction: Divine will is a distinct attribute, not reducible to command or action.

Checkpoint
What do some Mu'tazila claim irada is with respect to the action of another?
A) It is God's action
B) It is God's command
C) It is God's knowledge
D) It is God's power

Key Takeaway
Nasafi refutes attempts to reduce divine will to command, action, or appetite, affirming its reality as a distinct attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about Allah's will (irada), do you ever catch yourself imagining it as similar to human desires or decisions? What steps can you take today to purify your understanding of this attribute?
?
If someone told you that Allah's will is just another name for His actions or commands, how would you use Nasafi's refutation to respond? How does this affect your trust in the teachings of the Salaf?
?
Are there any areas in your life where you unconsciously reduce Allah's attributes to human concepts? Commit to one specific way you will correct this in your study of 'aqida this week.

Divine Will: By an Attribute or by Essence?
Nasafi presents the first question on divine will and refutes al-Najjar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the debate between the Ahl al-Haqq and al-Husayn al-Najjar on whether God wills by an irada or by His essence, and why the latter view is considered corrupt.

Core Idea
God wills by an eternal attribute, not by His bare essence.

The first question about divine will is whether God’s willing is through an attribute (irada) or through His essence. Al-Nasafi reports that the majority affirm an attribute of will, but al-Husayn al-Najjar, influenced by Mu'tazilite negation of attributes, claimed God is willing by His essence. This lesson examines that claim and its refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice how Nasafi frames the question and gives the two answers.
The passage is short but dense.
2
Identify the two positions
Find the view of the majority (willing by an irada) and the view of al-Husayn al-Najjar (willing by essence). What is al-Najjar's basis?
Al-Najjar relies on the Mu'tazila who negate attributes.
3
Understand why al-Najjar's view is corrupt
Nasafi declares al-Najjar's statement corrupt without further elaboration here. Think about the implications of denying an attribute of will: it would make God's will either nonexistent or identical to His essence, which leads to problems.
The commentary will help clarify.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسأل النسفي : هل الله تعالى مريد بإرادة أم بغير إرادة؟ ويجيب بأن من قال بالإرادة قال : إنه مريد بها أما الحسين النجار فقد قال: إنه مريد بذاته، معتمدا في كلامه على المعتزلة النافين للصفات، ولا شك في فساد قوله. ويسأل هل إرادته تعالى قائمة بذاته أم لا بذاته؟ فأهل الحق يقولون : إنه تعالى مريد بإرادة قائمة بذاته. أما العلاف والجبائيان فقالوا: إن الله تعالى مريد بإرادة حادثة لا في محل. ويناقشهم النسفي مبينا استحالة قيام العرض بنفسه. ثم يسأل: هل إرادته تعالى أزلية أم حادثة؟ ويجيب بأن أهل الحق قالوا: إنه مريد بإرادة أزلية قائمة به. أما الكرامية فيقولون : إنه في الأزل مريد بمريديَّة، ويقصدون بذلك قدرته على الإرادة، وأنه تعالى قد أحدث العالم بإرادة حادثة. ويناقشهم مبينا استحالة قيام الحادث بذاته تعالى وهنا يقسو عليهم فيتهمهم بالإلحاد. وبعد هذا يذكر النسفي أن الله تعالى مريد بإرادة واحدة كل المرادات خلافا للكرامية القائلين إن لكل مراد إرادة تحققت في ذاته.
And al-Nasafi asks: Is Allah the Exalted willing by an irada or without an irada? And he answers: Those who affirm al-irada said that He is willing by it; but al-Husayn al-Najjar said: He is willing by His essence, relying in his speech on the Mu'tazila who negate attributes, and there is no doubt about the corruption of his statement. And he asks: Is His irada the Exalted subsisting in His essence or not in His essence? The people of truth say: He the Exalted is willing by an irada subsisting in His essence. As for al-Allaf and al-Jubba'iyan (the two Jubba'is), they said: Allah the Exalted is willing by a temporally originated irada that is not in a locus (la fi mahall). And al-Nasafi discusses them, showing the impossibility of an accident subsisting by itself. Then he asks: Is His irada the Exalted eternal or temporally originated? And he answers that the people of truth said: He is willing by an eternal irada subsisting in Him. As for the Karramiyya, they say: In eternity He is willing by a muridiyya (will-ness), meaning by that His ability to will, and that He the Exalted brought the world into existence by a temporally originated irada. And he discusses them, showing the impossibility of the temporal originating in His essence the Exalted, and here he treats them harshly, accusing them of heresy. After this, al-Nasafi mentions that Allah the Exalted is willing by one irada for all objects of will, contrary to the Karramiyya who say that for each object of will there is an irada that occurs in His essence.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage addresses three connected questions about the modality of divine irada. First, is God willing by an irada or by His essence? Nasafi answers that the majority say by an irada, but al-Husayn al-Najjar said by essence, relying on Mu'tazila who negate attributes; Nasafi declares this corrupt. Second, is this irada subsisting in God's essence or not? Ahl al-Haqq (the people of truth) affirm it subsists in His essence, while al-Allaf and the two Jubba'is (Jubba'i and his son) claim it is a temporally originated accident not in a locus. Nasafi refutes them by arguing that an accident cannot subsist by itself (it requires a substrate). Third, is the irada eternal or temporal? Ahl al-Haqq say eternal, subsisting in God. The Karramiyya say God in eternity is willing by a 'muridiyya' (capacity to will) and that He created the world by a temporal irada; Nasafi shows the impossibility of a temporal accident subsisting in God's essence, and even charges them with heresy. Finally, Nasafi affirms that God wills all objects of will with one single irada, contrary to the Karramiyya who posit multiple iradas for each object.

Key Terms
مريد بذاته
الإرادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did al-Husayn al-Najjar say God is willing by His essence?
A) Because he denied the attribute of will entirely
B) Because he relied on the Mu'tazila who negate attributes
C) Because he considered irada to be a created thing
D) Because he believed God's will is temporal

Key Takeaway
God's will is a distinct attribute, not a mode of His essence; denying this attribute leads to corruption.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face trials, do you truly believe that God's will for you is perfect and unchanging, or do you sometimes think He changes His mind based on your actions? What does this lesson challenge in your heart?
?
If God's will were not a distinct attribute but a mode of His essence, would you still be able to trust that His decrees are wise and eternal? How does affirming that His will is an attribute strengthen your reliance on Him?
?
Al-Najjar's view relied on the Mu'tazila who stripped God of His attributes. Are there any ways in which you inadvertently 'strip' God of His majesty by limiting His attributes in your mind? Commit to one specific change in how you think of God.

Subsistence of Divine Irada: In Essence or Not?
Nasafi discusses the locus of divine irada and refutes the Mu'tazilite view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the debate over whether God's irada subsists in His essence or is a temporally originated accident not in a locus, and why the latter is impossible.

Core Idea
God's will is an eternal attribute subsisting in His essence, not a floating accident.

The second question about divine will concerns its locus: does the irada subsist in God's essence or not? The people of truth affirm it subsists in His essence, while al-Allaf and the two Jubba'is claim it is a temporally originated accident with no locus. This lesson explains Nasafi's refutation based on the impossibility of an accident subsisting by itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the three positions: Ahl al-Haqq, al-Allaf and al-Jubba'iyan, and Nasafi's refutation.
2
Understand the three positions
The Ahl al-Haqq say irada subsists in God's essence. Al-Allaf and al-Jubba'iyan say it is a temporally originated accident not in a locus. Nasafi refutes the latter.
An accident (arad) requires a substrate to exist.
3
Grasp the refutation
Nasafi argues that it is impossible for an accident to subsist by itself. An accident must inhere in a substance. Therefore, a temporally originated irada with no locus is impossible.
This is a key argument for the necessity of attributes subsisting in God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسأل النسفي : هل الله تعالى مريد بإرادة أم بغير إرادة؟ ويجيب بأن من قال بالإرادة قال : إنه مريد بها أما الحسين النجار فقد قال: إنه مريد بذاته، معتمدا في كلامه على المعتزلة النافين للصفات، ولا شك في فساد قوله. ويسأل هل إرادته تعالى قائمة بذاته أم لا بذاته؟ فأهل الحق يقولون : إنه تعالى مريد بإرادة قائمة بذاته. أما العلاف والجبائيان فقالوا: إن الله تعالى مريد بإرادة حادثة لا في محل. ويناقشهم النسفي مبينا استحالة قيام العرض بنفسه. ثم يسأل: هل إرادته تعالى أزلية أم حادثة؟ ويجيب بأن أهل الحق قالوا: إنه مريد بإرادة أزلية قائمة به. أما الكرامية فيقولون : إنه في الأزل مريد بمريديَّة، ويقصدون بذلك قدرته على الإرادة، وأنه تعالى قد أحدث العالم بإرادة حادثة. ويناقشهم مبينا استحالة قيام الحادث بذاته تعالى وهنا يقسو عليهم فيتهمهم بالإلحاد. وبعد هذا يذكر النسفي أن الله تعالى مريد بإرادة واحدة كل المرادات خلافا للكرامية القائلين إن لكل مراد إرادة تحققت في ذاته.
And al-Nasafi asks: Is Allah the Exalted willing by an irada or without an irada? And he answers: Those who affirm al-irada said that He is willing by it; but al-Husayn al-Najjar said: He is willing by His essence, relying in his speech on the Mu'tazila who negate attributes, and there is no doubt about the corruption of his statement. And he asks: Is His irada the Exalted subsisting in His essence or not in His essence? The people of truth say: He the Exalted is willing by an irada subsisting in His essence. As for al-Allaf and al-Jubba'iyan (the two Jubba'is), they said: Allah the Exalted is willing by a temporally originated irada that is not in a locus (la fi mahall). And al-Nasafi discusses them, showing the impossibility of an accident subsisting by itself. Then he asks: Is His irada the Exalted eternal or temporally originated? And he answers that the people of truth said: He is willing by an eternal irada subsisting in Him. As for the Karramiyya, they say: In eternity He is willing by a muridiyya (will-ness), meaning by that His ability to will, and that He the Exalted brought the world into existence by a temporally originated irada. And he discusses them, showing the impossibility of the temporal originating in His essence the Exalted, and here he treats them harshly, accusing them of heresy. After this, al-Nasafi mentions that Allah the Exalted is willing by one irada for all objects of will, contrary to the Karramiyya who say that for each object of will there is an irada that occurs in His essence.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage addresses three connected questions about the modality of divine irada. First, is God willing by an irada or by His essence? Nasafi answers that the majority say by an irada, but al-Husayn al-Najjar said by essence, relying on Mu'tazila who negate attributes; Nasafi declares this corrupt. Second, is this irada subsisting in God's essence or not? Ahl al-Haqq (the people of truth) affirm it subsists in His essence, while al-Allaf and the two Jubba'is (Jubba'i and his son) claim it is a temporally originated accident not in a locus. Nasafi refutes them by arguing that an accident cannot subsist by itself (it requires a substrate). Third, is the irada eternal or temporal? Ahl al-Haqq say eternal, subsisting in God. The Karramiyya say God in eternity is willing by a 'muridiyya' (capacity to will) and that He created the world by a temporal irada; Nasafi shows the impossibility of a temporal accident subsisting in God's essence, and even charges them with heresy. Finally, Nasafi affirms that God wills all objects of will with one single irada, contrary to the Karramiyya who posit multiple iradas for each object.

Key Terms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does al-Nasafi reject the Mu'tazilite view that God's irada is a temporally originated accident not in a locus?
A) Because accidents are eternal
B) Because an accident cannot subsist by itself
C) Because the irada must be multiple
D) Because God's essence is not a locus

Key Takeaway
God's attribute of will must subsist in His essence; a temporally originated accident with no locus is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's will is eternal and subsists in His essence, then every moment of your life unfolds according to that will. Are you truly living with the awareness that your choices are within a decree that was never accidental? How does that change the way you face your next decision?
?
The Mu'tazilites tried to protect God's transcendence by separating His will from His essence. Are there areas in your life where you subtly try to distance God from your struggles, as if He is too transcendent to be involved in your pain? What would change if you fully believed His will subsists in His essence and is directly related to your life?
?
Nasafi refutes the idea of an accident without a locus as impossible. In your spiritual life, do you ever try to build faith on shaky foundations—expecting mercy without accountability, or blessings without reliance on God? How can you ground your relationship with God in the truth of His eternal attributes?

Divine Attributes
