First Reason: God Creates a Barrier to Vision
Nasafi presents the first reason: God creates an opposite of vision in our eyes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's being not of a genus allows Him to create a barrier to vision in this world.

Core Idea
God's incomparability makes His temporary invisibility a deliberate act, not a defect.

Nasafi gives two reasons why God is not seen in this worldly life. The first reason addresses a key objection: if God can be seen, why do we not see Him now? Nasafi answers that God creates in our eyes a state opposite to seeing Him, and this is not impossible because God does not belong to any genus. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text and its translation slowly. Notice the key terms 'ضد' (opposite) and 'جنس' (genus).
2
Understand the concept of 'didd'
The word 'ضد' means something that prevents or opposes. Here it refers to a God-created state in our sight that makes vision impossible.
This does not imply a defect in God, but a deliberate act.
3
Grasp the genus argument
Nasafi argues that if God had a genus, then seeing an object of that genus would make it necessary to see God. Since God is not in a genus, no such necessity arises.
This defends God's transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأثناء الحديث يعرض لشبه أخرى، ويناقشها ويخلص إلى أن الله تعالى لا يرى في الدنيا لأمرين: الأول : أن الله خلق في أبصارنا ضد رؤيته، وهذا لا يستحيل عليه، لأن الله تعالى ليس بذي جنس حتى يقال لما رأينا جنسه لم يجز انعدام رؤيته. والثاني: أن رؤيته لم تكن معتادة لنا في الدنيا فلا يقال لا تنعدم، لأن ذلك يؤدي إلى قلب المادة، ويقول : إن هذا ما قال به أكثر أصحابه، وقال به الماتريدي.
And during the discussion, he presents other doubts and discusses them, and concludes that God Most High is not seen in the world for two reasons: First: God created in our sight the opposite of seeing Him, and this is not impossible for Him, because God Most High is not of a genus such that it could be said 'when we saw His genus, the absence of seeing Him is not permissible.' Second: His vision was not customary for us in the world, so it cannot be said that it is not absent, because that would lead to the overturning of matter. He says: This is what most of his companions said, and al-Maturidi said it.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage provides two reasons why God is not seen in this world, despite being visible in principle. First: God creates in our eyes a state that is opposite to seeing Him (a 'didd' of vision). This is not impossible because God is not of a genus, so there is no necessity that if we see something of His genus, we must see Him. Second: Vision of God is not customary ('āda) for us in this life, so its absence is not surprising. Nasafi notes that this is the view of most of his teachers (ashāb) and of al-Maturidi. The second reason also guards against the argument that absence of vision would imply a change in the nature of matter.

Key Terms
ضد
جنس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God can be seen, He must be seen in this world.
Correction: Possibility does not necessitate occurrence; God may create conditions that prevent vision now while allowing it in the hereafter.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi's first reason, why is it not impossible for God to create a barrier to vision in our eyes?
A) Because God is all-powerful
B) Because God is not of a genus
C) Because we cannot see anything invisible
D) Because God wills it so

Key Takeaway
God's invisibility in this world is due to a deliberate barrier He creates, made possible by His unique nature beyond any genus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face spiritual blindness or doubt, do you consider that God may have deliberately placed a barrier? How does this lesson challenge you to trust His wisdom even when you cannot see Him?
?
If God can create a barrier in your physical eyes, what barriers might He have placed in your heart? Are you willing to ask Him to remove them, even if it requires patience and submission?
?
This lesson says God's invisibility is a deliberate act—not a limitation. How does that change your posture toward Him? Will you worship Him with the awe due to the One who chooses when and how to reveal Himself?

Second Reason: Vision of God is Not Customary
Nasafi presents the second reason: vision of God is not customary in this world.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second reason: that vision of God is not customary in this world, and why this does not imply its impossibility.

Core Idea
Non-occurrence does not prove impossibility; custom explains why we do not see God now.

The second reason Nasafi provides is based on the concept of custom ('āda). If something has never been observed, its absence is not evidence that it cannot happen. This argument also prevents a metaphysical confusion about matter. Nasafi then notes that this is the view of most of his teachers and of al-Maturidi himself.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the term 'عادة' (custom) and the phrase 'قلب المادة' (overturning matter).
2
Understand the custom argument
Nasafi says that because seeing God is not customary for us in this world, we cannot claim that its absence is impossible. Custom does not dictate possibility.
This avoids a mistaken inference from experience to necessity.
3
Attribution to authorities
Nasafi attributes this view to most of his companions and to al-Maturidi, showing it is well-founded in the tradition.
This strengthens the argument.

Nasafi vs. al-Qalanisi on Preventing Nature
Nasafi accepts al-Qalanisi's view but disputes his reasoning about preventing nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the difference between al-Qalanisi's and al-Nasafi's views on whether God can prevent a nature from acting while leaving the nature intact.

Core Idea
God's power is not limited by natural natures; He can prevent them by creating opposites.

In this lesson, we explore a subtle theological disagreement. While al-Nasafi agrees with al-Qalanisi that God is not seen in this world due to weakness in our sight, he challenges the reasoning behind it. Al-Qalanisi thought that if the eye is strong, God cannot prevent it from seeing because that would violate its nature. Al-Nasafi argues that God can indeed create an opposite (like blindness) while the nature remains, showing His absolute power.

Guided Path
1
Understand the shared conclusion
Both scholars agree that God is not seen in this world. Identify this common ground before noting their difference.
Al-Qalanisi attributes it to weakness in our sight; Nasafi does not object to this.
2
Identify al-Qalanisi's reasoning
Al-Qalanisi argues that it is impossible for God to prevent the nature of sight from functioning while the nature remains. This is the point of disagreement.
He thinks preventing a nature implies changing it, which is not the case.
3
Grasp al-Nasafi's counterargument
Al-Nasafi replies that God can prevent the nature by creating its opposite (didd) in the organ, even while the natural strength remains. For example, God can cause blindness in a healthy eye.
This shows God's power over natural causation without destroying the nature.
4
Reflect on the theological implication
Consider how this debate underscores God's absolute power: He can override natural processes without altering their inherent dispositions.
This is relevant to discussions on divine causality and miracles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يعرض رأي القلانسي الذي يقول : إن الله تعالى لا يرى في الدنيا لضعف في أبصارنا، ويرتضي النسفي هذا الرأي، إلا أنه يدخل في مناقشة معه بسبب قوله: إن ارتفاع الرؤية بخلق ضدها في البصر حال قوة البصر، ممتنع، لأن – منع ذي الطبع في فعله مع بقاء طبعه محال عند القلانسي. أما عند النسفي فإنه يجوز منع ذي الطبع عن طبعه بخلق ضد طبعه وذلك كانعدام الرؤية بخلق ضدها في البصر حال قوة البصر.
Then he presents the view of al-Qalanisi who says: God Most High is not seen in this world due to weakness in our sight. And al-Nasafi accepts this view, except that he enters into a discussion with him because of his saying: That the removal of vision by creating its opposite in the sight while the sight is strong is impossible, because preventing the possessor of a nature from his action while his nature remains is impossible according to al-Qalanisi. But according to al-Nasafi, it is permissible to prevent the possessor of a nature from his nature by creating the opposite of his nature, and that is like the absence of vision by creating its opposite in the sight while the sight is strong.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This lesson presents a nuanced discussion between al-Nasafi and al-Qalanisi. Al-Qalanisi attributes the lack of vision in this world to a weakness in our sight, which al-Nasafi accepts as a general explanation. However, al-Nasafi disagrees with al-Qalanisi's reasoning: al-Qalanisi claims that it is impossible for God to prevent the nature of sight from functioning while leaving the nature intact. Al-Nasafi counters that God can indeed prevent the nature by creating its opposite (didd) in the organ, even while the natural strength remains. This is analogous to creating blindness in a healthy eye. Thus, the non-occurrence of vision in this world can be due to a direct act of God creating an obstacle, not merely due to inherent weakness.

Key Terms
القلانسي
طبع
ضد
قوة البصر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if the eye is strong, it must see; God cannot prevent it without changing the nature.
Correction: Nasafi shows that God can prevent even a strong nature from acting by creating an opposite, without altering the nature itself.

Checkpoint
On what point does Nasafi disagree with al-Qalanisi?
A) Whether God is seen in the afterlife
B) Whether God can prevent a nature while leaving the nature intact
C) Whether the vision of God is possible
D) Whether the eye has a nature

Key Takeaway
Al-Nasafi demonstrates that God's power is absolute and not constrained by natural natures; He can prevent their action by creating opposites.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that God can override any natural law in your life, even when your own 'nature' or habits seem unchangeable? What would it mean for you to act on that belief today?
?
When you face a situation where your own strength (like the strong eye) seems to guarantee a certain outcome, do you consider that God may create an opposite to prevent it? How does this affect your reliance on God versus reliance on causes?
?
If God can prevent the action of a nature by creating its opposite, then no situation is really beyond His control. Have you been living as if some things are out of God's hands? What is one area you need to surrender to Him right now?

God's Sight Is Not Physical
Nasafi affirms divine sight without spatial conditions, refuting Baghdad Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that divine sight is not dependent on physical conditions like distance or ray connection.

Core Idea
God sees without distance or ray – His sight is absolute.

Nasafi addresses a key objection from the Baghdad Mu'tazila, who denied that God sees or is seen. In this brief but powerful statement, he clarifies that God's sight is not like human vision. There is no space, no light ray, no physical process involved. This lesson establishes the transcendence of God's attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without overthinking, then read the literal translation. Notice the concise style.
The passage is a single sentence with a clear structure.
2
Identify the two negations
Find the two things Nasafi denies about God's seeing: distance (masāfa) and connection of a ray (ittiṣāl shu'ā').
These are spatial/physical conditions that human vision requires.
3
Contrast with the Baghdad Mu'tazila
Note that the Baghdad Mu'tazila claimed God does not see and is not seen. Nasafi's affirmation directly refutes them.
This highlights a key sectarian difference in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويبين النسفي: أن الله سبحانه وتعالى يرانا بلا مسافة بيننا وبينه ولا اتصال شعاع خلافا لما يقوله البغداديون من المعتزلة أن الله لا يرى ولا يرى.
And al-Nasafi explains: That God, glorified and exalted, sees us without distance between us and Him and without connection of a ray, contrary to what the Baghdadis among the Mu'tazila say, that God does not see and is not seen.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This brief passage addresses the nature of God's seeing. Nasafi affirms that God sees us without any spatial conditions such as distance (masāfa) or connection of a ray (ittiṣāl shu'ā'). This is a rejection of the view of the Baghdad school of Mu'tazila, who claimed that God neither sees nor is seen. Nasafi here is clarifying that God's vision is not dependent on physical processes. The point is to uphold God's transcendence while affirming His attribute of sight.

Key Terms
مسافة
اتصال شعاع
البغداديون
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's sight requires distance or a physical ray like human vision.
Correction: Nasafi clarifies that God sees without any spatial or physical conditions.

Checkpoint

A) Through a ray connection
B) From a distance
C) Without distance or ray connection
D) Only in the afterlife

Key Takeaway
God's sight is not dependent on distance or physical rays; it is a transcendent attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as if God sees you every moment, without any distance or barrier? What would change in your daily habits if you deeply believed that His sight is constant and unrestricted?
?
The Baghdad Mu'tazila denied God's sight to avoid anthropomorphism, but Nasafi shows that true transcendence includes perfect sight. Are you ever tempted to limit God's attributes to make Him more 'comfortable' for your understanding? How does that affect your worship?
?
If God sees you without ray or distance, then no sin is hidden and no excuse stands. What sin are you trying to hide from God's sight? What step will you take today to repent and live in the light of His all-encompassing vision?

The Vision of God's Attributes
Nasafi presents two views on the vision of divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main theological positions on whether God's attributes can be seen and Nasafi's own view.

Core Idea
Vision of God's attributes depends on their existence, not their physicality.

This lesson addresses a subtle question: can we see God's attributes, such as His knowledge or power? Nasafi begins by noting that no revealed text settles this issue. He then presents two competing rational positions: one restricts vision to self-subsisting entities, while the other extends it to all existent things. Understanding this distinction is key to grasping the Maturidi position on divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once to get a feel for its structure. Notice that it has two main parts: a statement about revelation and a statement about rational permissibility.
The passage is concise; each clause carries weight.
2
Identify the two positions
Find the description of the first group (those who tie vision to self-subsistence) and the second group (those who tie vision to existence).
Nasafi aligns himself with the second group.
3
Understand the key terms
Focus on 'qā'im bi al-dhāt' (self-subsisting) and 'mawjūd' (existent). These are crucial for the argument.
Attributes are not self-subsisting but are existent.
4
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: if vision attaches to every existent, can we see all of God's attributes? Nasafi says it is permissible (jā'iz), not that it actually occurs.
This is a subtle distinction often misunderstood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالنسبة لرؤية صفاته يقول : إنه لم يُرْوَ نص سمعي برؤيتها، أما بالنسبة لجواز رؤيتها فإن القائلين بجواز تعلق الرؤية بالقائم بالذات، واستحالتها في غير ذلك لا يجوزون رؤية الصفات والقائلون بجواز تعلق الرؤية بكل موجود – ومنهم النسفي – فالصفات جائزة الرؤية.
And regarding the vision of His attributes, he says: No transmitted text (naṣṣ sam'ī) has been reported about seeing them. As for the permissibility of seeing them, those who say that vision attaches only to what subsists by itself (al-qā'im bi al-dhāt) and is impossible regarding other than that do not permit seeing the attributes. And those who say that vision attaches to every existent – and among them is al-Nasafi – then the attributes are permissible to see.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This lesson addresses a secondary question: can God's attributes (like knowledge, power) be seen? Nasafi first notes that there is no explicit revealed text (naṣṣ sam'ī) on this matter. Then he presents two positions. Some theologians argue that vision can only attach to a self-subsisting entity (qā'im bi al-dhāt), so attributes, being not self-subsisting, cannot be seen. Others, including Nasafi, hold that vision attaches to every existent being (kull mawjūd). Since attributes are existent (as real attributes of God), they are in principle visible. However, Nasafi does not assert that they are actually seen, only that it is permissible (jā'iz) to see them.

Key Terms
صفات
رؤية
قائم بالذات
موجود
جائز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that since attributes are not physical, they cannot be seen.
Correction: Nasafi's position is that visibility depends on existence, not physicality. Because attributes are real existent entities, they are in principle visible.

Checkpoint
What is Nasafi's view on the vision of God's attributes?
A) It is impossible
B) It is permissible because vision attaches to every existent
C) It is only possible in the afterlife
D) It is confirmed by revelation

Key Takeaway
Nasafi affirms the permissibility of seeing God's attributes based on their existence, even though no revealed text confirms it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you could truly see God's knowledge, power, and mercy as real existent things, how would that change the way you relate to them in your daily life? Will you begin today to treat these attributes as more than abstract ideas?
?
Nasafi accepts a rational argument even without explicit scripture. Are there areas in your faith where you rely only on tradition or what is 'safe,' avoiding the risk of rational conviction? What would it cost you to follow reason where revelation is silent?
?
The debate about seeing attributes hinges on whether they are truly 'existent' to you. Do you live as if God's attributes are real and present, or do you reduce them to words you recite? What one change would make His mercy more 'seeable' in your actions before tomorrow night?

Two Arguments for the Possibility of Ru'ya
Nasafi presents two arguments against denying ru'ya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two arguments Nasafi uses to counter the denial of ru'ya: that Allah is not a genus and that ru'ya in the hereafter is not bound by worldly habits.

Core Idea
Ru'ya is not impossible by genus or habit.

Nasafi opens by addressing two objections commonly raised against the possibility of seeing Allah. He refutes them concisely, showing that reasoning from genus or from worldly experience does not apply to the divine. This sets the stage for his positive case.

Guided Path
1
Read the first argument
Trace Nasafi's reasoning: Allah has no genus, so analogies from seen genera fail.
2
Read the second argument
Notice that ru'ya in the afterlife is not habitual; hence one cannot object based on lack of worldly experience.
This refutes the 'habit' objection.
3
Reflect on the method
See how Nasafi uses rational arguments (not just texts) to clear obstacles.
This is typical Maturidi methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عليه، لأن الله تعالى ليس بذي جنس حتى يقال لما رأينا جنسه لم يجز انعدام رؤيته. والثاني: أن رؤيته لم تكن معتادة لنا في الدنيا فلا يقال لا تنعدم، لأن ذلك يؤدي إلى قلب المادة، ويقول : إن هذا ما قال به أكثر أصحابه، وقال به الماتريدي. ثم يعرض رأي القلانسي الذي يقول : إن الله تعالى لا يرى في الدنيا لضعف في أبصارنا، ويرتضي النسفي هذا الرأي، إلا أنه يدخل في مناقشة معه بسبب قوله: إن ارتفاع الرؤية بخلق ضدها في البصر حال قوة البصر، ممتنع، لأن – منع ذي الطبع في فعله مع بقاء طبعه محال عند القلانسي. أما عند النسفي فإنه يجوز منع ذي الطبع عن طبعه بخلق ضد طبعه وذلك كانعدام الرؤية بخلق ضدها في البصر حال قوة البصر. ويبين النسفي: أن الله سبحانه وتعالى يرانا بلا مسافة بيننا وبينه ولا اتصال شعاع خلافا لما يقوله البغداديون من المعتزلة أن الله لا يرى ولا يرى. وبالنسبة لرؤية صفاته يقول : إنه لم يُرْوَ نص سمعي برؤيتها، أما بالنسبة لجواز رؤيتها فإن القائلين بجواز تعلق الرؤية بالقائم بالذات، واستحالتها في غير ذلك لا يجوزون رؤية الصفات والقائلون بجواز تعلق الرؤية بكل موجود النسفي - فالصفات جائزة الرؤية. ومنهم ثم يلخص أساس الاختلاف في المسألة في العبارات التالية: "والحاصل أنا لما رأينا الرؤية متعلقة بتلك الأجناس، ولا وصف يجمعها يمكن تعليقها به إلا الوجود علقناها به لوجود دليل تعلقها به تعلق الأحكام بالعلل وعديناها إلى الغائب بتعدي الوجود، ودلتنا رؤيته تعالى إيانا على أن ما اقترن بالرؤية في الشاهد من المباينة والمقابلة، واتصال الشعاع وغير ذلك أوصاف وجود وليست بالقرائن اللازمة لها، لتحققها ،بدونها، فاتبعنا هذه الدلائل، وإن لم يقع في أوهامنا رؤية إلا بهذه القرائن، لما أن المعول على الدليل دون الوهم. وخصومنا أعرضوا عن العلة المطلقة الرؤية، وتمسكوا بما وجدوا من القرائن الاتفاقية، وتمسكوا بالوهم، ورفضوا الدلائل العقلية، وفتحوا على المعطلة أوسع باب لنفي الصانع، وذلك لأنهم لم ينقادوا للدلائل العقلية".
[...] because Allah is not of a genus such that it could be said: since we have seen His genus, it is not possible for His vision to cease. And second: His vision was not habitual for us in this world, so it cannot be said that it does not cease, because that would lead to inversion of substance. And he says: This is what most of his companions said, and al-Maturidi said it. Then he presents the opinion of al-Qalanisi who says: Allah is not seen in this world due to weakness in our eyesight, and al-Nasafi approves this opinion, except that he enters into a discussion with him due to his saying: The prevention of vision by creating its opposite in sight while the sight is strong is impossible, because prevention of the possessor of a nature from its act while its nature remains is impossible according to al-Qalanisi. As for al-Nasafi, he permits prevention of the possessor of a nature from its nature by creating an opposite to its nature, such as the elimination of vision by creating its opposite in the sight while the sight is strong. And al-Nasafi explains: Allah sees us without distance between us and Him and without connection of rays, contrary to what the Baghdadis of the Mu'tazila say – that Allah does not see and is not seen. Regarding the vision of His attributes, he says: No transmitted text has been narrated regarding their vision. As for the permissibility of their vision, those who permit the attachment of vision to that which subsists in the essence, and its impossibility in other than that, do not permit vision of attributes. And those who permit attachment of vision to every existent – and al-Nasafi is among them – then attributes are permissible to be seen. Then he summarizes the basis of disagreement in the issue in the following phrases: 'The conclusion: Since we have seen vision attached to those genera, and there is no description that gathers them that we can attach it to except existence, we attached it to it due to the existence of evidence of its attachment to it, as judgments are attached to causes, and we extended it to the absent by the extension of existence. And His vision of us has indicated that what accompanied vision in the witnessed world – such as separation, facing, and connection of rays and other [aspects] – are descriptions of existence and are not necessary concomitants, because they are realized without them. So we followed these evidences, even if vision does not occur in our imaginations except with these concomitants, because reliance is on evidence not on imagination. And our opponents turned away from the absolute cause of vision, and clung to what they found of accidental concomitants, and clung to imagination, and rejected intellectual evidences, and opened the widest door to the denial of the Creator for the deniers of attributes, and that is because they did not submit to intellectual evidences.'
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part discussion on ru'ya (vision of Allah). It begins with a summary of two arguments: first, that Allah is not of a genus, so reasoning from genus is invalid; second, that ru'ya in the hereafter is not habitual like in this world, so it cannot be dismissed. Then it reports al-Maturidi's agreement. Next, it presents al-Qalanisi's view that ru'ya is impossible in this world due to weak eyesight, and al-Nasafi's partial approval with a critique. Al-Nasafi disagrees with al-Qalanisi's claim that preventing a nature from its act is impossible; al-Nasafi holds that Allah can create an opposite, e.g., preventing vision. Then al-Nasafi affirms that Allah sees us without distance or ray, contra the Baghdad Mu'tazila. On ru'ya of attributes, al-Nasafi notes no scriptural text affirms it, but those who permit ru'ya of every existent (including al-Nasafi) deem attributes visible. The core summary follows: ru'ya is linked to wujud (existence), not accidental attributes like distance or facing. Evidence takes precedence over imagination. Opponents reject intellectual proofs and rely on imagination, opening the door to denying the Creator.

Key Terms
رؤية (ru'ya)
جنس (genus)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does Nasafi say about Allah being a genus?
A) Allah is a genus like other genera
B) Allah is not a genus
C) Genus is irrelevant to ru'ya
D) Allah's genus is unknown

Key Takeaway
Ru'ya is not impossible because Allah has no genus and because afterlife vision is not bound by worldly habit.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you struggle to believe in something unseen about Allah, do you dismiss it because it doesn't fit your worldly experience? How does Nasafi's second argument confront that tendency? Commit to one area where you will stop using worldly habit as a measure of Allah's power.
?
If someone tells you that seeing Allah is impossible because everything we see is limited, how would you respond using Nasafi's first argument? Now ask yourself: In what area of your faith have you allowed such limited thinking to creep in?
?
The second argument warns against 'inversion of substance'—introducing absurdities. Where in your own beliefs might you be accepting an absurd conclusion about Allah because you have not thought through the premises? What will you do about it this week?

Al-Qalanisi's View and Nasafi's Critique
Nasafi critiques al-Qalanisi's reasoning on ru'ya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Qalanisi's position that ru'ya is impossible in this world due to weak eyesight, and Nasafi's critique regarding the prevention of a nature.

Core Idea
Allah can prevent vision by creating its opposite in the eye.

Nasafi presents al-Qalanisi's view that ru'ya is impossible in this world because of our weak eyesight. While he approves the conclusion, he disagrees with al-Qalanisi's reasoning that Allah cannot prevent a nature from acting. Nasafi argues that Allah can create an opposite that blocks vision.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Qalanisi's view
Identify his claim: ru'ya is impossible in this world due to weak eyesight.
2
Understand Nasafi's critique
Al-Qalanisi thinks preventing a nature from its act is impossible; Nasafi disagrees.
Nasafi gives the example of creating blindness.
3
Grasp the theological point
Nasafi affirms divine omnipotence over natural processes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عليه، لأن الله تعالى ليس بذي جنس حتى يقال لما رأينا جنسه لم يجز انعدام رؤيته. والثاني: أن رؤيته لم تكن معتادة لنا في الدنيا فلا يقال لا تنعدم، لأن ذلك يؤدي إلى قلب المادة، ويقول : إن هذا ما قال به أكثر أصحابه، وقال به الماتريدي. ثم يعرض رأي القلانسي الذي يقول : إن الله تعالى لا يرى في الدنيا لضعف في أبصارنا، ويرتضي النسفي هذا الرأي، إلا أنه يدخل في مناقشة معه بسبب قوله: إن ارتفاع الرؤية بخلق ضدها في البصر حال قوة البصر، ممتنع، لأن – منع ذي الطبع في فعله مع بقاء طبعه محال عند القلانسي. أما عند النسفي فإنه يجوز منع ذي الطبع عن طبعه بخلق ضد طبعه وذلك كانعدام الرؤية بخلق ضدها في البصر حال قوة البصر. ويبين النسفي: أن الله سبحانه وتعالى يرانا بلا مسافة بيننا وبينه ولا اتصال شعاع خلافا لما يقوله البغداديون من المعتزلة أن الله لا يرى ولا يرى. وبالنسبة لرؤية صفاته يقول : إنه لم يُرْوَ نص سمعي برؤيتها، أما بالنسبة لجواز رؤيتها فإن القائلين بجواز تعلق الرؤية بالقائم بالذات، واستحالتها في غير ذلك لا يجوزون رؤية الصفات والقائلون بجواز تعلق الرؤية بكل موجود النسفي - فالصفات جائزة الرؤية. ومنهم ثم يلخص أساس الاختلاف في المسألة في العبارات التالية: "والحاصل أنا لما رأينا الرؤية متعلقة بتلك الأجناس، ولا وصف يجمعها يمكن تعليقها به إلا الوجود علقناها به لوجود دليل تعلقها به تعلق الأحكام بالعلل وعديناها إلى الغائب بتعدي الوجود، ودلتنا رؤيته تعالى إيانا على أن ما اقترن بالرؤية في الشاهد من المباينة والمقابلة، واتصال الشعاع وغير ذلك أوصاف وجود وليست بالقرائن اللازمة لها، لتحققها ،بدونها، فاتبعنا هذه الدلائل، وإن لم يقع في أوهامنا رؤية إلا بهذه القرائن، لما أن المعول على الدليل دون الوهم. وخصومنا أعرضوا عن العلة المطلقة الرؤية، وتمسكوا بما وجدوا من القرائن الاتفاقية، وتمسكوا بالوهم، ورفضوا الدلائل العقلية، وفتحوا على المعطلة أوسع باب لنفي الصانع، وذلك لأنهم لم ينقادوا للدلائل العقلية".
[...] because Allah is not of a genus such that it could be said: since we have seen His genus, it is not possible for His vision to cease. And second: His vision was not habitual for us in this world, so it cannot be said that it does not cease, because that would lead to inversion of substance. And he says: This is what most of his companions said, and al-Maturidi said it. Then he presents the opinion of al-Qalanisi who says: Allah is not seen in this world due to weakness in our eyesight, and al-Nasafi approves this opinion, except that he enters into a discussion with him due to his saying: The prevention of vision by creating its opposite in sight while the sight is strong is impossible, because prevention of the possessor of a nature from its act while its nature remains is impossible according to al-Qalanisi. As for al-Nasafi, he permits prevention of the possessor of a nature from its nature by creating an opposite to its nature, such as the elimination of vision by creating its opposite in the sight while the sight is strong. And al-Nasafi explains: Allah sees us without distance between us and Him and without connection of rays, contrary to what the Baghdadis of the Mu'tazila say – that Allah does not see and is not seen. Regarding the vision of His attributes, he says: No transmitted text has been narrated regarding their vision. As for the permissibility of their vision, those who permit the attachment of vision to that which subsists in the essence, and its impossibility in other than that, do not permit vision of attributes. Then he summarizes the basis of disagreement in the issue in the following phrases: 'The conclusion: Since we have seen vision attached to those genera, and there is no description that gathers them that we can attach it to except existence, we attached it to it due to the existence of evidence of its attachment to it, as judgments are attached to causes, and we extended it to the absent by the extension of existence. And His vision of us has indicated that what accompanied vision in the witnessed world – such as separation, facing, and connection of rays and other [aspects] – are descriptions of existence and are not necessary concomitants, because they are realized without them. So we followed these evidences, even if vision does not occur in our imaginations except with these concomitants, because reliance is on evidence not on imagination. And our opponents turned away from the absolute cause of vision, and clung to what they found of accidental concomitants, and clung to imagination, and rejected intellectual evidences, and opened the widest door to the denial of the Creator for the deniers of attributes, and that is because they did not submit to intellectual evidences.'

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, can Allah prevent a natural faculty from its act?
A) No, nature must always act
B) Yes, by creating an opposite
C) Only if the faculty is weak
D) Only in the afterlife

Key Takeaway
Nasafi upholds divine power to override nature, unlike al-Qalanisi's view.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever assume that your natural abilities (like sight, intelligence, health) operate independently of Allah's will? After learning Nasafi's argument, what is one specific area of your life where you need to consciously acknowledge that Allah can override your natural strengths at any moment? Will you pray today for Him to grant you sight of His signs?
?
Al-Qalanisi thought that once a natural faculty is strong, its action is inevitable unless destroyed. Do you hold a similar hidden belief that some of your capacities are beyond Allah's intervention? Confess the area where you feel most self-reliant and commit to a specific dua acknowledging His absolute power over your nature.
?
Nasafi's correction shows that Allah can create an opposite in your eye to prevent vision. How does this truth affect your trust in Allah during times when you feel spiritually blind or unable to see the truth? What will you ask Him to 'create' in your heart to overcome that blindness starting today?

Ru'ya of Attributes: Different Positions
Nasafi discusses ru'ya of attributes and lists two views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the differing opinions on whether Allah's attributes can be seen, and Nasafi's position that any existent can be seen.

Core Idea
For Nasafi, every existent, including attributes, is potentially visible.

Nasafi turns to the vision of divine attributes. He notes that no scriptural text reports seeing attributes. Then he distinguishes two positions: those who think ru'ya can only attach to what subsists in an essence (thus attributes are not visible), and those who allow ru'ya of any existent. Nasafi aligns with the latter.

Guided Path
1
Read the textual note
Nasafi states no transmitted text supports ru'ya of attributes.
2
Identify the two positions
First: ru'ya only of essences. Second: ru'ya of any existent.
Nasafi belongs to the second group.
3
Reflect on implications
If attributes are existent, they can be seen, though no text confirms it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عليه، لأن الله تعالى ليس بذي جنس حتى يقال لما رأينا جنسه لم يجز انعدام رؤيته. والثاني: أن رؤيته لم تكن معتادة لنا في الدنيا فلا يقال لا تنعدم، لأن ذلك يؤدي إلى قلب المادة، ويقول : إن هذا ما قال به أكثر أصحابه، وقال به الماتريدي. ثم يعرض رأي القلانسي الذي يقول : إن الله تعالى لا يرى في الدنيا لضعف في أبصارنا، ويرتضي النسفي هذا الرأي، إلا أنه يدخل في مناقشة معه بسبب قوله: إن ارتفاع الرؤية بخلق ضدها في البصر حال قوة البصر، ممتنع، لأن – منع ذي الطبع في فعله مع بقاء طبعه محال عند القلانسي. أما عند النسفي فإنه يجوز منع ذي الطبع عن طبعه بخلق ضد طبعه وذلك كانعدام الرؤية بخلق ضدها في البصر حال قوة البصر. ويبين النسفي: أن الله سبحانه وتعالى يرانا بلا مسافة بيننا وبينه ولا اتصال شعاع خلافا لما يقوله البغداديون من المعتزلة أن الله لا يرى ولا يرى. وبالنسبة لرؤية صفاته يقول : إنه لم يُرْوَ نص سمعي برؤيتها، أما بالنسبة لجواز رؤيتها فإن القائلين بجواز تعلق الرؤية بالقائم بالذات، واستحالتها في غير ذلك لا يجوزون رؤية الصفات والقائلون بجواز تعلق الرؤية بكل موجود النسفي - فالصفات جائزة الرؤية. ومنهم ثم يلخص أساس الاختلاف في المسألة في العبارات التالية: "والحاصل أنا لما رأينا الرؤية متعلقة بتلك الأجناس، ولا وصف يجمعها يمكن تعليقها به إلا الوجود علقناها به لوجود دليل تعلقها به تعلق الأحكام بالعلل وعديناها إلى الغائب بتعدي الوجود، ودلتنا رؤيته تعالى إيانا على أن ما اقترن بالرؤية في الشاهد من المباينة والمقابلة، واتصال الشعاع وغير ذلك أوصاف وجود وليست بالقرائن اللازمة لها، لتحققها ،بدونها، فاتبعنا هذه الدلائل، وإن لم يقع في أوهامنا رؤية إلا بهذه القرائن، لما أن المعول على الدليل دون الوهم. وخصومنا أعرضوا عن العلة المطلقة الرؤية، وتمسكوا بما وجدوا من القرائن الاتفاقية، وتمسكوا بالوهم، ورفضوا الدلائل العقلية، وفتحوا على المعطلة أوسع باب لنفي الصانع، وذلك لأنهم لم ينقادوا للدلائل العقلية".

What is Nasafi's position on ru'ya of attributes?
A) Attributes cannot be seen
B) Attributes can be seen because they are existent

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah could reveal His attributes to you in a visible form, which attribute would you most dread to see — His justice, His power, or His mercy? Why does that fear reveal something about your own soul?
?
Are you comfortable with the idea that God's attributes are ‘existent’ in a way that could be seen? Or do you, like the unnamed group, prefer to keep God safely abstract and distant? What does that preference say about your trust in His nearness?
?
Nasafi used logic to expand the possibility of vision when scripture was silent. Where in your faith are you using logic to limit God's freedom — and what would it cost you to open that door?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
7 min
The Core Disagreement: Evidence vs. Imagination
Nasafi summarizes the core disagreement on ru'ya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fundamental dispute: ru'ya is based on existence (wujud) as a cause, not on accidental concomitants, and evidence must override imagination.

Core Idea
Reliance on evidence, not imagination, is the key to affirming ru'ya.

Nasafi concludes by summarizing the root of disagreement. He argues that ru'ya is attached to existence alone, not to accidental features like distance or facing. Evidence from Allah seeing us shows these are not necessary. Opponents ignorantly cling to imagination and accidental concomitants, opening the door to denying the Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the summary passage
Follow Nasafi's reasoning: ru'ya is attached to existence, extended to the unseen.
2
Identify the key proof
Allah's seeing us without distance shows that such concomitants are not necessary for vision.
3
Understand the opponent's error
Opponents rely on imagination and accidental concomitants, rejecting rational evidence.
Nasafi warns this leads to atheism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عليه، لأن الله تعالى ليس بذي جنس حتى يقال لما رأينا جنسه لم يجز انعدام رؤيته. والثاني: أن رؤيته لم تكن معتادة لنا في الدنيا فلا يقال لا تنعدم، لأن ذلك يؤدي إلى قلب المادة، ويقول : إن هذا ما قال به أكثر أصحابه، وقال به الماتريدي. ثم يعرض رأي القلانسي الذي يقول : إن الله تعالى لا يرى في الدنيا لضعف في أبصارنا، ويرتضي النسفي هذا الرأي، إلا أنه يدخل في مناقشة معه بسبب قوله: إن ارتفاع الرؤية بخلق ضدها في البصر حال قوة البصر، ممتنع، لأن – منع ذي الطبع في فعله مع بقاء طبعه محال عند القلانسي. أما عند النسفي فإنه يجوز منع ذي الطبع عن طبعه بخلق ضد طبعه وذلك كانعدام الرؤية بخلق ضدها في البصر حال قوة البصر. ويبين النسفي: أن الله سبحانه وتعالى يرانا بلا مسافة بيننا وبينه ولا اتصال شعاع خلافا لما يقوله البغداديون من المعتزلة أن الله لا يرى ولا يرى. وبالنسبة لرؤية صفاته يقول : إنه لم يُرْوَ نص سمعي برؤيتها، أما بالنسبة لجواز رؤيتها فإن القائلين بجواز تعلق الرؤية بالقائم بالذات، واستحالتها في غير ذلك لا يجوزون رؤية الصفات والقائلون بجواز تعلق الرؤية بكل موجود النسفي - فالصفات جائزة الرؤية. ومنهم ثم يلخص أساس الاختلاف في المسألة في العبارات التالية: "والحاصل أنا لما رأينا الرؤية متعلقة بتلك الأجناس، ولا وصف يجمعها يمكن تعليقها به إلا الوجود علقناها به لوجود دليل تعلقها به تعلق الأحكام بالعلل وعديناها إلى الغائب بتعدي الوجود، ودلتنا رؤيته تعالى إيانا على أن ما اقترن بالرؤية في الشاهد من المباينة والمقابلة، واتصال الشعاع وغير ذلك أوصاف وجود وليست بالقرائن اللازمة لها، لتحققها ،بدونها، فاتبعنا هذه الدلائل، وإن لم يقع في أوهامنا رؤية إلا بهذه القرائن، لما أن المعول على الدليل دون الوهم. وخصومنا أعرضوا عن العلة المطلقة الرؤية، وتمسكوا بما وجدوا من القرائن الاتفاقية، وتمسكوا بالوهم، ورفضوا الدلائل العقلية، وفتحوا على المعطلة أوسع باب لنفي الصانع، وذلك لأنهم لم ينقادوا للدلائل العقلية".
[...] because Allah is not of a genus such that it could be said: since we have seen His genus, it is not possible for His vision to cease. And second: His vision was not habitual for us in this world, so it cannot be said that it does not cease, because that would lead to inversion of substance. And he says: This is what most of his companions said, and al-Maturidi said it. Then he presents the opinion of al-Qalanisi who says: Allah is not seen in this world due to weakness in our eyesight, and al-Nasafi approves this opinion, except that he enters into a discussion with him due to his saying: The prevention of vision by creating its opposite in sight while the sight is strong is impossible, because prevention of the possessor of a nature from its act while its nature remains is impossible according to al-Qalanisi. As for al-Nasafi, he permits prevention of the possessor of a nature from its nature by creating an opposite to its nature, such as the elimination of vision by creating its opposite in the sight while the sight is strong. And al-Nasafi explains: Allah sees us without distance between us and Him and without connection of rays, contrary to what the Baghdadis of the Mu'tazila say – that Allah does not see and is not seen. Regarding the vision of His attributes, he says: No transmitted text has been narrated regarding their vision. As for the permissibility of their vision, those who permit the attachment of vision to that which subsists in the essence, and its impossibility in other than that, do not permit vision of attributes. And those who permit attachment of vision to every existent – and al-Nasafi is among them – then attributes are permissible to be seen. Then he summarizes the basis of disagreement in the issue in the following phrases: 'The conclusion: Since we have seen vision attached to those genera, and there is no description that gathers them that we can attach it to except existence, we attached it to it due to the existence of evidence of its attachment to it, as judgments are attached to causes, and we extended it to the absent by the extension of existence. And His vision of us has indicated that what accompanied vision in the witnessed world – such as separation, facing, and connection of rays and other [aspects] – are descriptions of existence and are not necessary concomitants, because they are realized without them. So we followed these evidences, even if vision does not occur in our imaginations except with these concomitants, because reliance is on evidence not on imagination. And our opponents turned away from the absolute cause of vision, and clung to what they found of accidental concomitants, and clung to imagination, and rejected intellectual evidences, and opened the widest door to the denial of the Creator for the deniers of attributes, and that is because they did not submit to intellectual evidences.'
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part discussion on ru'ya (vision of Allah). It begins with a summary of two arguments: first, that Allah is not of a genus, so reasoning from genus is invalid; second, that ru'ya in the hereafter is not habitual like in this world, so it cannot be dismissed. Then it reports al-Maturidi's agreement. Next, it presents al-Qalanisi's view that ru'ya is impossible in this world due to weak eyesight, and al-Nasafi's partial approval with a critique. Al-Nasafi disagrees with al-Qalanisi's claim that preventing a nature from its act is impossible; al-Nasafi holds that Allah can create an opposite, e.g., preventing vision. Then al-Nasafi affirms that Allah sees us without distance or ray, contra the Baghdad Mu'tazila. On ru'ya of attributes, al-Nasafi notes no scriptural text affirms it, but those who permit ru'ya of every existent (including al-Nasafi) deem attributes visible. The core summary follows: ru'ya is linked to wujud (existence), not accidental attributes like distance or facing. Evidence takes precedence over imagination. Opponents reject intellectual proofs and rely on imagination, opening the door to denying the Creator.

Key Terms
وجود (wujud)
وهم (imagination)
دليل (evidence)
قرائن (accidental concomitants)
علة (cause)
معطلة (deniers of attributes)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ru'ya requires physical concomitants like distance and facing.
Correction: Allah sees us without any of these, proving they are not necessary for vision.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why do opponents open the door to denying the Creator?
A) They follow evidence too strictly
B) They reject intellectual evidences and rely on imagination
C) They deny ru'ya altogether
D) They attach ru'ya to existence

Key Takeaway
The dispute over ru'ya ultimately hinges on whether one follows rational evidence or imagination.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Nasafi warns that relying on imagination over evidence 'opened the widest door to the denial of the Creator.' In your own life, when you encounter a truth that your mind cannot fully picture, do you tend to trust your intellect or your comfort zone? Which tendency has caused you more spiritual harm?
?
The passage says we must follow evidence even if our imagination resists. Is there a specific teaching of Islam that you struggle to accept because you cannot imagine how it works? Will you submit to the evidence of revelation despite that struggle? What is one step you can take today to strengthen your trust in divine evidence over your own imagination?
?
Nasafi says the opponents 'clung to imagination, and rejected intellectual evidences.' In what areas of your life—not just theology—do you cling to comfortable assumptions rather than follow evidence? How might this pattern be affecting your relationship with Allah and your commitment to truth? What will you do about it this week?

Two Types of Istita'a: Precedence vs. Concurrence
Nasafi answers two questions about the timing and scope of istita'a.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi distinction between two types of istita'a (capability) and how they relate to human acts: one type precedes and allows opposites; the other accompanies the act and is the immediate power.

Core Idea
Not all capability is the same — one type precedes the act, the other accompanies it.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi addresses a key question in Islamic theology: does the capability to act (istita'a) come before the act or with it? He distinguishes two senses of istita'a — the physical soundness that precedes, and the power (qudra) that accompanies the act. This distinction clarifies the Maturidi position on human agency and divine creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Let the structure of the question and answer come through.
2
Identify the two questions
Notice that two separate questions are posed: (1) Does istita'a precede or accompany? (2) Is it suitable for opposites? Find these in the text.
3
Distinguish the two types of istita'a
The answer immediately splits istita'a into two types. Identify the first type (soundness of causes) and the second type (power as an accident). Notice the different rulings for each.
The first type is agreed upon; the second type is disputed.
4
Compare the theological positions
See which groups say what about the second type: Mu'tazila say it precedes, al-Nasafi and his school, al-Najjariyya, and the Ash'ira say it accompanies. This reflects differing views on human agency.
This distinction sets up the Maturidi position on qadar.
5
Reflect on the significance
Think about why this matters: if the effective power is concurrent with the act, then human action is directly tied to divine creation of power at the moment of action, preserving both responsibility and God's omnipotence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسأل هل الاستطاعة متقدمة على الفعل أم مقارنة له؟ وهل هي صالحة للضدين أم لا؟ ويجيب على ذلك : بأن الاستطاعة بمعنى سلامة الأسباب، وصحة الآلات متقدمة على الفعل وهي صالحة للفعل وضده بلا خلاف بين من يثبتون الاستطاعة. أما الاستطاعة الثانية بمعنى القدرة فالمعتزلة يقولون بتقدمها على الفعل ويستحیل اقترانها به أما النسفي ،وأصحابه والنجارية، والأشاعرة فيقولون: إنها تكون مقارنة للفعل ومحال تقدمها عليه.
And he asks: Does istita‛a precede the act or accompany it? And is it suitable for opposites or not? And he answers that: istita‛a in the sense of soundness of causes and health of instruments precedes the act, and it is suitable for the act and its opposite without disagreement among those who affirm istita‛a. As for the second istita‛a in the sense of power (qudra), the Mu‛tazila say it precedes the act and deem it impossible for it to accompany it. As for al-Nasafī, his companions, al-Najjāriyya, and the Ashā‛ira, they say: It accompanies the act, and it is impossible for it to precede it.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a question-and-answer about the temporal relation of istita‛a to the act. Two questions are posed: (1) Does istita‛a precede or coincide with the act? (2) Is it suitable for opposites? The author immediately answers: The first type (soundness of means) precedes the act and is suitable for both the act and its opposite – this is agreed upon by all who affirm istita‛a. For the second type (the created power), the Mu‛tazila hold that it precedes the act and cannot accompany it. In contrast, al-Nasafī, his school, the Najjāriyya, and the Ash‛arites hold that it accompanies the act and cannot precede it. This division sets the stage for further discussion on human agency and divine creation.

Key Terms
تقدم (taqaddum)
مقارنة (muqārana)
صلاحية للضدين (ṣalāḥiyya lil-ḍiddayn)
المعتزلة (al-Mu‛tazila)
النجارية (al-Najjāriyya)
الأشاعرة (al-Ashā‛ira)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All istita'a precedes the act.
Correction: Only the first type (soundness of causes) precedes; the second type (power as an accident) is concurrent with the act according to al-Nasafī and the Maturidi position.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafī, when does the second type of istita‛a (power as an accident) occur?
A) Before the act
B) Concurrent with the act
C) After the act
D) It does not exist

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi view distinguishes two types of istita'a: the capacity from health precedes the act, but the effective power (qudra) is concurrent with the act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you accomplish something, do you attribute it to your own capacity or to the power Allah gave you at that exact moment? How might this lesson shift your gratitude?
?
If the effective power to act is created only at the moment of action, what does that say about your plans for tomorrow? How should that change the way you rely on Allah?
?
Think of a sin you committed despite having the means (health, opportunity). Was it because you had the power to do it? According to this lesson, Allah created that power concurrently with your sin. How does that affect your understanding of your own responsibility and His justice?

The Shared False Premise of Jabriyya and Qadariyya
al-Nasafi identifies the shared false premise and declares its invalidity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the false premise that both the Jabriyya and Qadariyya agreed upon, leading them to the erroneous conclusion that humans create their own actions.

Core Idea
A single act cannot be under two powers? That common belief led both extremes astray.

Al-Nasafi begins by identifying the root error of both the Jabriyya (extreme predestinarians) and the Qadariyya (Mu'tazila who affirmed free will). He shows that they shared a false premise: that a single thing within power cannot be related to two agents. This lesson unpacks that premise and its consequences.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Notice how al-Nasafi names the two groups and their shared premise.
The passage is concise; pay attention to the logical flow.
2
Identify the false premise
Find the statement that both groups agreed on: that a single maqdur cannot be under two qudras (powers). What is the evidence they used?
They analogized from the witnessed world (al-shahid).
3
Consider why it is false
Al-Nasafi says he will show its invalidity. Think about how the Maturidi position rejects this analogy—what makes the unseen world different?
This step connects to the next lesson on kasb.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقول: إن الذي دفع الجبرية وهم أصحاب جهم، والقدرية وهم المعتزلة إلى القول بأن العبد خالق لأفعاله الاختيارية اتفاقهم على مقدمة كاذبة وهي: أن دخول مقدور واحد تحت قدرة قادرين محال وذلك كما هو في الشاهد، ويبين فساد قولهم. ويقول: إن مذهب أهل السنة الجماعة: أن الأفعال للخلق، فإنهم بها صاروا عصاة أو مطيعين، وأنها مخلوقة لله، مكتسبة للعبد، وقد نفوا إحالة تعلق قدرتين بمقدور واحد، ونفوا الضرورة عن أفعالهم، ويستفاد من هذا ثبوت العدل ونفي الظلم، وإثبات الفضل لله، ويستفاد أيضا أن الله موصوف بما وصف به نفسه، كما قال تعالى: (خَلِقُ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ) [الزمر: 62].
Then he says: Verily, what drove the Jabriyya—who are the followers of Jahm—and the Qadariyya—who are the Mu'tazila—to say that the servant is the creator of his voluntary actions is their agreement on a false premise: that a single thing within power (maqdur) falling under the power of two agents is impossible, as is the case in the witnessed world. And he shows the invalidity of their statement. And he says: Verily, the doctrine of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a is that acts belong to the people (i.e., the servants), for by them they become disobedient or obedient, and that they are created (makhluqa) by Allah, acquired (muktasaba) by the servant. They have denied the impossibility of the relation of two powers to a single maqdur, and they have denied compulsion (darura) regarding their acts. And from this is derived the affirmation of justice (al-'adl) and the negation of injustice (al-zulm), and the establishment of grace (al-fadl) for Allah. And it is also derived that Allah is described by what He described Himself with, as He said, Exalted: 'He is the Creator of everything' [al-Zumar: 62].
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage outlines the central argument of the Maturidi position on human action. Al-Nasafi first identifies the false premise that led both the Jabriyya and the Qadariyya (Mu'tazila) to extremes: they agreed that a single act cannot fall under the power of two agents, because they analogized from the witnessed world. He shows their view is unsound. Then he states the Sunni position: actions are indeed performed by servants, making them obedient or disobedient, yet these actions are created by Allah and acquired (muktasaba) by the servant. This view denies that two powers cannot relate to one act, and denies necessity (jabr) in actions. From this follow justice, no injustice, and all grace is from Allah. Finally, he cites the Qur'anic verse 'Khaliq kulli shay' (Creator of everything) to affirm that Allah is described as He describes Himself.

Key Terms
مقدمة كاذبة
مقدور
قدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Both Jabriyya and Mu'tazila thought that if God creates all actions, then humans cannot be responsible; or if humans are responsible, they must create their own actions. But the real error was their shared premise about impossibility of two powers acting on one thing.
Correction: The Maturidi position holds that one act can be both created by Allah and acquired by the human, without contradiction.

Checkpoint
What false premise did the Jabriyya and Qadariyya both agree on, according to al-Nasafi?
A) That God cannot create evil actions.
B) That humans have no free will.
C) That a single maqdur cannot be under two qudras.
D) That actions are eternal.

Key Takeaway
The shared false premise of Jabriyya and Qadariyya is that a single act cannot be under two agents, leading both to extremes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a complex situation, do you lean toward fatalism (everything is predetermined) or self-reliance (I alone control my actions)? How does recognizing that both extremes come from the same flawed assumption change your perspective?
?
Have you ever justified a belief about God by saying 'It's just common sense' or 'That's how it works in everyday life'? Where might that analogy fail, as it did for the Jabriyya and Qadariyya?
?
If a single act can truly be under both your power and Allah's power without contradiction, how should that reshape the way you pray, plan, and rely on Allah throughout your day?

The Sunni Doctrine of Kasb: Actions as Created and Acquired
al-Nasafi states the Sunni doctrine of kasb and its implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position that human actions are created by Allah and acquired by the servant, and the implications for justice and divine description.

Core Idea
Actions are created by Allah, acquired by the servant—thus responsibility without compulsion.

After refuting the false premise, al-Nasafi states the doctrine of Ahl al-Sunna: actions belong to the servants in terms of acquisition (kasb) but are created by Allah. This lesson explores that position and its theological implications, including justice and the affirmation of Allah's attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the Sunni position
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the key claims: acts are for the people (servants), they are created by Allah, acquired by the servant.
The term 'muktasaba' is crucial.
2
Understand 'kasb'
Kasb means acquisition—the servant has a real role in the action without creating it. This avoids both jabr (compulsion) and tafwid (complete delegation).
Compare with the false premise denied: they rejected the impossibility of two powers on one act.
3
Explore the implications
Al-Nasafi derives that from this doctrine comes justice (no injustice), all grace from Allah, and that Allah is described as He describes Himself. Reflect on why these follow.
The verse 'Khaliq kulli shay' affirms Allah's sole creative power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقول: إن الذي دفع الجبرية وهم أصحاب جهم، والقدرية وهم المعتزلة إلى القول بأن العبد خالق لأفعاله الاختيارية اتفاقهم على مقدمة كاذبة وهي: أن دخول مقدور واحد تحت قدرة قادرين محال وذلك كما هو في الشاهد، ويبين فساد قولهم. ويقول: إن مذهب أهل السنة الجماعة: أن الأفعال للخلق، فإنهم بها صاروا عصاة أو مطيعين، وأنها مخلوقة لله، مكتسبة للعبد، وقد نفوا إحالة تعلق قدرتين بمقدور واحد، ونفوا الضرورة عن أفعالهم، ويستفاد من هذا ثبوت العدل ونفي الظلم، وإثبات الفضل لله، ويستفاد أيضا أن الله موصوف بما وصف به نفسه، كما قال تعالى: (خَلِقُ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ) [الزمر: 62].
Then he says: Verily, what drove the Jabriyya—who are the followers of Jahm—and the Qadariyya—who are the Mu'tazila—to say that the servant is the creator of his voluntary actions is their agreement on a false premise: that a single thing within power (maqdur) falling under the power of two agents is impossible, as is the case in the witnessed world. And he shows the invalidity of their statement. And he says: Verily, the doctrine of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a is that acts belong to the people (i.e., the servants), for by them they become disobedient or obedient, and that they are created (makhluqa) by Allah, acquired (muktasaba) by the servant. And from this is derived the affirmation of justice (al-'adl) and the negation of injustice (al-zulm), and the establishment of grace (al-fadl) for Allah. And it is also derived that Allah is described by what He described Himself with, as He said, Exalted: 'He is the Creator of everything' [al-Zumar: 62].

Commentary
This passage outlines the central argument of the Maturidi position on human action. Al-Nasafi first identifies the false premise that led both the Jabriyya and the Qadariyya (Mu'tazila) to extremes: they agreed that a single act cannot fall under the power of two agents, because they analogized from the witnessed world. He shows their view is unsound. Then he states the Sunni position: actions are indeed performed by servants, making them obedient or disobedient, yet these actions are created by Allah and acquired (muktasaba) by the servant. This view denies that two powers cannot relate to one act, and denies necessity (jabr) in actions. From this follow justice, no injustice, and all grace is from Allah. Finally, he cites the Qur'anic verse 'Khaliq kulli shay' (Creator of everything) to affirm that Allah is described as He describes Himself.

Key Terms
كسب
خلق
عدل
قدورة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if Allah creates actions, then humans have no real role and are compelled. But the Sunni position holds that humans acquire actions, making them responsible.
Correction: Kasb means the servant's action is real but not creative; thus responsibility remains.

Checkpoint
According to the Sunni position stated by al-Nasafi, how are human actions related to Allah and the servant?
A) Allah creates them and the servant creates them independently.
B) Allah creates them and the servant acquires them.
C) The servant creates them and Allah only permits them.
D) Neither Allah nor the servant has any role.

Key Takeaway
The Sunni doctrine of kasb asserts that human actions are created by Allah and acquired by the servant, affirming both divine sovereignty and human responsibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every action of yours—including your obedience and disobedience—is created by Allah, how does that change the way you approach your daily choices? Are you living with a sense of absolute dependence on Him or with an illusion of self-sufficiency? Reflect on one area where you can consciously rely on His creation of your action.
?
The passage says that by their acts people become obedient or disobedient. When you examine your actions today, do you see yourself actively 'acquiring' obedience through deliberate intention, or are you merely drifting? What would it take for you to consciously own your actions as your acquisition before Allah?
?
Since all grace (al-fadl) is from Allah, what does that imply about your successes and failures? Can you genuinely attribute your achievements to His grace and your failures to your own acquisition without falling into despair? How does this truth free you from pride and hopelessness?

Refuting the Mu'tazili Use of 'Ahsan al-Khaliqin'
Al-Nasafi reinterprets 'khalaq' as estimation and design, not creation ex nihilo.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Nasafi reinterprets the term 'khalaq' to refute the Mu'tazili claim that the Qur'anic verse implies human creation ex nihilo.

Core Idea
The word 'khalaq' in the Qur'an means estimation and design, not origination.

The Mu'tazila often cite Qur'anic verses to support their theological positions. One such verse is 'Ahsan al-khaliqin' (best of creators), which they take as evidence that humans can create in the same sense as Allah. Al-Nasafi, in this passage, refutes this by clarifying the linguistic meaning of 'khalaq'. This lesson examines his argument and its implications for understanding divine and human agency.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how al-Nasafi first states the Mu'tazili reliance on the verse, then provides his interpretation.
The verse is from Surah al-Mu'minun, verse 14.
2
Identify the key terms
Identify the four key terms: 'khalaq', 'taqdir', 'taswir', 'ijad', 'ikhtira'. Understand their meanings in this context.
Estimation (taqdir) refers to measuring and planning; depiction (taswir) refers to giving form.
3
Reflect on the refutation
Consider why reinterpreting 'khalaq' as estimation and depiction refutes the Mu'tazili claim. How does this protect the uniqueness of Allah's creative power?
This shows that humans are called 'creators' only metaphorically.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي رده على تعلقهم بالنقل في الآية الكريمة: (فَتَبَارَكَ اللَّهُ أَحْسَنُ الْخَالِقِينَ) [المؤمنون: 14] يقول: الخلق يذكر ويراد به التقدير والتصوير دون الإيجاد والاختراع، وبهذا يجوز أن يسمى العبد خالقا.
And in his refutation of their reliance on transmitted evidence (al-naql) in the noble verse: 'So blessed be Allah, the best of creators' [al-Mu'minun: 14], he says: 'Khalaq' is mentioned and what is meant by it is estimation (taqdir) and depiction (taswir), not bringing into existence (ijad) and invention (ikhtira'). And by this, it is permissible that the servant be called a creator (khaliq).
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage responds to the Mu'tazili misuse of the Qur'anic verse 'Ahsan al-khaliqin' (best of creators). The Mu'tazila argue that if Allah is called the best of creators, then there must be other creators (humans). Al-Nasafi refutes this by explaining that the term 'khalaq' in this context means taqdir (estimation, measuring) and taswir (shaping, forming), not ijad (bringing into existence) or ikhtira' (originating). Therefore, the verse does not imply that humans create in the sense of origination. Rather, humans can be called 'creators' only in a metaphorical sense of designing or shaping.

Key Terms

إيجاد
اختراع

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila believe that the verse 'Ahsan al-khaliqin' proves humans create ex nihilo.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows that 'khalaq' means estimation and design, so the verse does not imply human origination.

Checkpoint

A) As creation ex nihilo
B) As estimation and depiction
C) As making from pre-existing matter
D) As causing to exist

Key Takeaway
Al-Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazili argument by showing that 'khalaq' in the verse means estimation and design, not origination, thus preserving the distinction between divine and human action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This lesson shows that the Mu'tazila used a verse in a literal way to support a theology of human power. Will you sit with that verse and let it reveal its true depth, or will you cling to your interpretation?
?
Al-Nasafi distinguishes between Allah's exclusive act of origination and the human act of shaping or estimating. In what areas of your life are you tempted to subtly claim the role of 'originator'—for example, in your work, your relationships, or your sense of control over outcomes? How does this passage call you to repent and return to the realization that He alone creates from nothing, and you are merely given the ability to arrange what He has provided?

The Condition for Creative Power: Pre-Existent Knowledge
Al-Nasafi proves the impossibility of creative power for other than Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why creative power (qudrat al-takhliq) requires knowledge of the creature before its existence and why this condition is absent in humans.

Core Idea
Creative power requires knowing what you create before it exists — only Allah knows all things before they are.

Al-Nasafi now seals the Maturidi argument against attributing creative power to anyone but Allah. He identifies a condition that must be present for creative power to exist: knowledge of the creature in the state of its non-existence. This condition, he argues, is unique to Allah. Let's examine his proof from the Qur'an and reason.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it, then read the literal translation. Let the author's own words come through before you interpret.
2
Identify the condition for creative power
Al-Nasafi states that a condition (shart) is necessary for the existence of creative power. Find what that condition is and how he supports it with a Qur'anic verse.
The condition is knowledge of the creature while it is still non-existent.
3
Understand why humans lack this condition
Al-Nasafi argues that humans do not possess this condition because their intellect cannot comprehend how something emerges from nothing. Reflect on why this inability shows that humans are doers (fa'ilun) but not creators (khaliqun).
This distinction is central to the Maturidi position on human action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إثبات قدرة التخليق لغير الله محال يقول: إنه لابد لثبوت قدرة التخليق من شرط بانعدامه ينعدم التخليق، ويتركز هذا الشرط في قوله تعالى: (وَأَسِرُّوا قَوْلَكُمْ أَوِ اجْهَرُوا بِهِ إِنَّهُ عَلِيمٌ بِذَاتِ الصُّدُورِ) [الملك: 13]، ومعنى هذا ثبوت علم الخالق بالمخلوق في حال عدمه أي قبل وجوده، وهذا الشرط منعدم في الإنسان، فإن الإنسان لا يقدر عقله كيفية خروج الشيء من العدم إلى الوجود، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك فإن العبد فاعل لما هو مخلوق له، وليس بخالق.
Establishing that the power of creation (qudrat al-takhliq) for other than Allah is impossible. He says: Verily, for the affirmation of the power of creation, a condition is necessary, by the absence of which creation (al-takhliq) is absent. And this condition is concentrated in His saying, Exalted: 'And keep secret your speech or proclaim it; indeed, He is All-Knowing of that within the breasts' [al-Mulk: 13]. And its meaning is the affirmation of the Creator's knowledge of the creature in the state of its non-existence, i.e., before its existence. And this condition is absent in humans, for the human intellect does not comprehend how something goes from non-existence to existence. And if the matter is so, then the servant is a doer (fa'il) of what is created for him, and he is not a creator (khaliq).
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This final passage presents a self-contained proof that creative power cannot belong to anyone besides Allah. Al-Nasafi states that creative power requires a condition: the agent must know the creature while it is still non-existent. He draws this from the Qur'anic verse that Allah knows even the innermost thoughts, which implies knowledge of things before they exist. This condition is absent in humans; human reason cannot grasp how something emerges from nothing into existence. Therefore, humans are doers (fa'ilun) of actions that are created for them, but they are not creators. This concludes the Maturidi argument against attributing creative power to humans.

علم
عدم

فاعل
خالق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Doing an action is the same as creating it.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows that doing (fi'l) is distinct from creating (takhliq); creation requires a condition (knowledge before existence) that only Allah has.

Checkpoint
What condition does al-Nasafi state is necessary for creative power?
A) The ability to see the future
B) Knowledge of the creature before its existence
C) Power over all things
D) The ability to create from nothing

Key Takeaway
Creative power requires pre-existent knowledge of the creature, which is a divine prerogative; humans are agents but not creators.

?

Wisdom in Creating Opposites and Demonstrating Independence
Al-Nasafi lists three wisdoms regarding divine power and independence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God's creation of opposites like good and evil demonstrates His perfect power, freedom from need, and absolute independence.

Core Idea
God creates opposites to show His power, needlessness, and sovereignty.

Al-Nasafi begins by stating that God's creation of disbelief and sins contains profound wisdoms. The first three wisdoms focus on divine attributes: the coexistence of good and evil highlights God's ability to create opposites; His creation of both good and evil shows that He acts without need; and this manifests His independence and might.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Understand the structure: it lists three wisdoms.
2
Identify the first wisdom
The existence of good and evil indicates perfection of power. Reflect on why creating opposites is a display of power.
3
Identify the second wisdom
God's creation of good and evil without need. Contrast with human actions motivated by need or benefit.
4
Identify the third wisdom
Independence and might. Note that this is shown to all people.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والله تعالى في خلق الكفر، والمعاصي حكم بالغة منها : وجود الحسن و القبح، يدل على كمال قدرته في خلق المتضادات. ومنها : أنه حين يخلق الخير والشر، لا يفعل عن حاجة، ولا لجلب نفع، أو دفع مضرة. ومنها : أنه بذلك يظهر للناس جميعا أنه غنى عن خلقه، عزيز بذاته، ومنها: أنه تعالى لما علم أن بعض عباده يعصونه فيما يأمره، ويكفرون بنعمه، وأنه يعذبهم في النار كان تعالى بتخليقه ذلك فيهم عند اختيارهم لأنفسهم موجدا ما فيه تحقيق علمه، وتقرير عدله عند تعذيبه إياهم، وهذه عاقبة للفعل حميدة.
And God Almighty, in the creation of disbelief (kufr) and acts of disobedience (maʿāṣī), has profound wisdoms (ḥikam bāligha). Among them: The existence of good (al-ḥasan) and evil (al-qabīḥ) indicates the perfection of His power in creating opposites. And among them: That when He creates good and evil, He does not act out of need, nor to gain benefit, nor to repel harm. And among them: That by that He shows to all people that He is independent of His creation, mighty in His essence. And among them: That He, exalted, when He knew that some of His servants would disobey Him in what He commands them, and disbelieve in His blessings, and that He would punish them in the Fire, He—by His creating that in them at the time of their own choice—brought into existence that which realizes His knowledge and establishes His justice when He punishes them. And this is a praiseworthy outcome (ʿāqiba ḥamīda) of the act.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage lists several wise purposes (ḥikam) behind God's creation of disbelief and sins. First, the existence of opposites—good and evil—demonstrates the perfection of God's power, as He can create contrary things. Second, God's creation of both good and evil proves that He acts without need, benefit, or fear of harm—unlike creatures. Third, it manifests God's independence (ghanā') and might (ʿizza). Fourth, God's foreknowledge that some will disobey and disbelieve is realized in their actions when they choose; by creating these acts, God fulfills His knowledge and establishes His justice when He punishes them. All these show that even the creation of evil has a praiseworthy outcome, reinforcing that God's actions are all wise.

Key Terms
حكمة
المتضادات
الغنى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the existence of good and evil indicate about God?
A) That He is limited by moral laws
B) The perfection of His power in creating opposites
C) That He cannot prevent evil
D) That evil is an illusion

Key Takeaway
God's creation of opposites like good and evil is a sign of His perfect power, needlessness, and sovereignty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
This lesson teaches that opposites in creation prove Allah's sovereignty. When you see injustice or suffering, do you still affirm that He is in full control? What would it take for you to live with that conviction daily?

Wisdom in Fulfilling Knowledge and Establishing Justice
Al-Nasafi explains the fourth wisdom: God's creation of sins fulfills His knowledge and justice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God creates disbelief in those who choose it to fulfill His foreknowledge and to establish His justice in punishment.

Core Idea
God creates sins in people to realize His knowledge and ensure just punishment.

The fourth wisdom expands on the interconnectedness of divine knowledge and human choice. Al-Nasafi explains that God's creation of disbelief in those who disobey does not make Him unjust; rather, it is a means to actualize His knowledge and to justify His punishment of them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully

2
Understand divine foreknowledge and human choice
Recognize that God's foreknowledge of human disobedience is not the cause; He creates the act in them when they choose it.
3
See the purposes: knowledge and justice
God's creation brings about realization of His knowledge and establishes His justice when punishing.
4
Reflect on the outcome
The phrase 'praiseworthy outcome' shows that even creating sin has a good purpose.
